Jizya Rates and Categories: Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhab Dispute
Ruling with proof and inter-madhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi jizya rates based on wealth, identify which non-Muslims are liable, and explain the Hanafi evidence against Shafi'i objections.

Core Idea
Jizya is a graded compensation for protection, not a uniform tax, and applies to all non-Muslims who may be enslaved.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq presents the Hanafi rulings on jizya, the poll tax on non-Muslim subjects. It covers two scenarios – treaty and conquest – and details the graduated rates based on wealth. The text then defends the Hanafi position against objections, especially from the Shafi'i school, on both the rate and the categories of payers. Understanding these rulings requires appreciating jizya as a compensatory obligation for sparing life and property, not a tax on religion.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish treaty vs. imposed jizya
Identify the two methods of imposing jizya: by mutual consent (treaty) where the amount is fixed by agreement, or by force (after conquest) where standard rates apply. Note that the treaty amount cannot be altered.
This distinction affects whether the rate is fixed or flexible.
2
Learn the three wealth categories and their annual rates
Memorize: poor capable earner (12 dirhams/year, 1/month), middle-class (24 dirhams/year, 2/month), wealthy (48 dirhams/year, 4/month). The wealthy is defined as owning 10,000 dirhams or more.
The rates are based on the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs.
3
Understand the legal justification of jizya
Jizya is not a fee for permitting disbelief, but compensation for not killing or enslaving the adult male non-Muslim. It is comparable to accepting blood money (diya) to forgo retaliation. This answers the atheist objection.
This principle justifies graduated rates since compensation varies with wealth.
4
Identify the categories of non-Muslims from whom jizya is accepted
According to Hanafis, jizya is taken from Kitabis (Jews, Christians), Magians (Zoroastrians), and idol-worshipping non-Arabs. The reason: it is permissible to enslave them, so jizya is also permissible.
Shafi'is restrict jizya to People of the Book and Magians; idol-worshippers are excluded.
5
Compare Hanafi and Shafi'i positions and the evidence
Shafi'i argues for a uniform rate (1 dinar per adult) and limited categories. Hanafis respond with the consensus of the Companions ('Umar, 'Uthman, 'Ali) and the analogy to military aid which varies with wealth.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير والجهاد
فصل: أحكام الجزية
أي في بيان أحكام الجزية
الجزية لو وضعت بتراض، لا يعدل عنها، وإلا توضع على الفقير المعتمل في كل سنة اثنا عشر درهماً، وعلى وسط الحال ضعفه، في كل شهر درهم. وبالسنة وهو ما روي أنه عليه السلام أخذ الجزية من مجوس نجران. وقد طعن بعض الملحدين حيث قالوا: كيف يجوز تقرير الكفار على الكفر بمال، ولو جاز ذلك لجاز تقرير الزاني على الزنا بمال يؤخذ منه؟ وأجيب بأن الجزية لم تكن بدلا عن تقريره على الكفر، بل هي عوض عن ترك القتل والاسترقاق الواجبين، فجاز كإسقاط القصاص بعوض، وهي عقوبة على الكفر فيجوز كالاسترقاق. بتراض بأن صالحهم الإمام على مبلغ معين من الدراهم والدنانير وغيرهما. لا يعدل عنها: أي عن الجزية الموضوعة بالتراضي والصلح؛ لأنها تتقدر بحسب ما يقع عليه الاتفاق. والموجب هو التراضي فلا يجوز التعدي منه إلى غيره. وإلا توضع إلخ: أي وإن لم توضع الجزية بالتراضي بل بالقهر في ما إذا غلب الإمام على الكفار وأقرهم على أموالهم، فحينئذ توضع على الفقير المعتمل أي الصحيح القادر على الكسب في كل سنة اثنا عشر درهماً يؤخذ منه في كل شهر درهم حتى لو لم يعمل مع قدرته وجبت كمن عطل أرض الخراج. واعلم أن المعتبر في الغنا والفقر أكثر السنة، فلو كان غنياً في نصف الحول، وفقيراً في النصف يؤخذ منه جزية الوسط، والغني من يملك عشرة آلاف درهم فصاعداً. وعلى المكثر ضعفه، أي ضعف الضعف وهو ثمانية وأربعون درهماً يؤخذ منه في كل شهر أربعة دراهم. وتوضع على كتابي ومجوسي ووثني عجمي، أي وتوضع على وهو الغنى الظاهر الغناء أي الجزية لجواز استرقاقه - وضع الجزية على الفقير المكتسب في السنة اثنا عشر درهماً، في كل شهر درهم، وعلى وسط الحال ضعف ذلك في كل شهر درهمين، وعلى الغني ضعف ضعفه، في كل شهر أربعة دراهم، وهذا عندنا، وقال الشافعي: يوضع على كل حالم وحالمة ديناراً، والفقير والغني في ذلك سواء؛ لقوله عليه السلام لمعاذ : خذ من كل حالم أو حالمة دينارا أو عدله معافر. ومذهبنا منقول عن عمر وعثمان وعلي رضي الله عنهم والصحابة متوافرون ولم ينكر عليهم أحد منهم، فصار إجماعا؛ ولأن الجزية وجبت نصرة للمقاتلة؛ لأنها وجبت بدلا عن النصرة بالنفس والمال والنصرة يتفاوت بكثرة المال وقلته فكذا ما هو بدله. وعند مالك: على كل محتلم أربعة دنانير أو أربعون درهما، وعند أحمد: يفوض إلى رأي الإمام. كتابي: هو نسبة إلى كتاب منزل من السماء، والمعنى توضع الجزية على الذي يعتقد كتابا من الكتب المنزلة كاليهودي. وقوله: "ومجوسي" أي توضع الجزية عليه لما روي عن عمر رضي الله عنه أنه لم يأخذ الجزية من المجوس حتى شهد عبد الرحمن بن عوف له أخذها من مجوس هجر. وقوله: "وثني عجمي" أي وتوضع على عبدة الأوثان من العجم. وقال الشافعي: لا تؤخذ منهم؛ لأن القتال واجب، بقوله تعالى: {وَقَاتِلُوهُمْ} إلا أنا عرفنا جواز ترك القتال بالجزية في حق أهل الكتاب كما قال تعالى: {مِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَابَ حَتَّى يُعْطُوا الْجِزْيَةَ} وفي حق المجوس بالخبر كما روينا، فبقى ما ورائهم على الأصل، فلا جزية عليهم. ولنا أنه يجوز استرقاقهم، فيجوز ضرب الجزية عليهم؛ ولأن الجزية غير مختصة بأهل الكتاب وبه قال مالك وأحمد في رواية. وعن مالك توضع على كل كافر إلا مشركي قريش.
The book of Siyar and Jihad. Chapter: Rulings of the jizya. i.e. explaining the rulings of jizya. The jizya: if it is placed by mutual consent, it is not deviated from. Otherwise, it is placed upon the poor capable earner in every year twelve dirhams, and upon the middle-class double that, each month one dirham. And by the Sunnah, it is reported that he (peace be upon him) took jizya from the Magians of Najran. And some atheists have objected saying: how is it permissible to confirm the disbelievers upon disbelief for money, and if that were permissible, it would be permissible to confirm the adulterer upon adultery for money taken from him? And it was answered that jizya is not a substitute for confirming him upon disbelief, but rather it is compensation for leaving off the obligatory killing and enslavement, so it is permissible like dropping retaliation for compensation, and it is a punishment for disbelief so it is permissible like enslavement. By mutual consent: that the Imam makes peace with them for a specified amount of dirhams and dinars and others. It is not deviated from: i.e. from the jizya placed by mutual consent and treaty; because it is estimated according to what the agreement falls upon. And the obligating factor is mutual consent, so it is not permissible to deviate from it to other than it. Otherwise it is placed etc.: i.e. and if the jizya is not placed by mutual consent but rather by force, in the case when the Imam overpowers the disbelievers and confirms them upon their property, then it is placed upon the poor capable earner – i.e. the healthy one capable of earning – in every year twelve dirhams, taken from him each month one dirham, so that if he does not work despite his capability, it becomes obligatory, like the one who neglects kharaj land. And know that the consideration for richness and poverty is the majority of the year, so if he is rich for half the year and poor for the other half, the jizya of the middle is taken from him. And the rich is the one who possesses ten thousand dirhams or more. And upon the wealthy is twice it, i.e. twice the double, which is forty-eight dirhams, taken from him each month four dirhams. And it is placed upon a Kitabi, a Magian, and an idol-worshipping non-Arab. i.e. it is placed upon – and he is the manifestly wealthy – i.e. the jizya due to permissibility of enslaving him. Placing the jizya: upon the poor earner is twelve dirhams per year, each month one dirham; upon the middle-class is double that, each month two dirhams; upon the rich is double the double, each month four dirhams. This is according to us. Al-Shafi'i said: it is placed upon every adolescent male and female one dinar, the poor and the rich are equal in that, due to his statement to Mu'adh: Take from every adolescent male or female one dinar or its equivalent of Mu'afir garments. Our madhhab is transmitted from 'Umar, 'Uthman, and 'Ali, and the Companions were abundant, and none of them objected, so it became consensus. And because jizya is obligatory as aid for the combatants, because it is obligatory as compensation for aiding with self and wealth, and aiding varies with abundance and scarcity of wealth, so likewise what is its substitute. According to Malik: upon every pubescent male four dinars or forty dirhams. According to Ahmad: it is delegated to the Imam's opinion. Kitabi: is a relative attribution to a revealed book, meaning jizya is placed upon one who believes in one of the revealed books, like the Jew. And his statement: 'and Magian' meaning jizya is placed upon him due to what was reported from 'Umar that he did not take jizya from the Magians until 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf testified that he took it from the Magians of Hajar. And his statement: 'and idol-worshipping non-Arab' meaning it is placed upon the idol worshippers of the non-Arabs. Al-Shafi'i said: it is not taken from them, because fighting is obligatory by His statement: {And fight them} except that we know the permissibility of leaving fighting for jizya in the case of the People of the Book, as He said: {from those who were given the Book until they give jizya}, and in the case of the Magians by the report as we narrated, thus those beyond them remain upon the original ruling, so there is no jizya upon them. And we have (the argument) that it is permissible to enslave them, so it is permissible to impose jizya upon them; and because jizya is not specific to the People of the Book, and Malik and Ahmad in one narration said the same. And from Malik it is placed upon every disbeliever except the polytheists of Quraysh.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq explains the rulings of jizya, the poll tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects of an Islamic state. It begins by distinguishing two scenarios: when jizya is set by mutual agreement (treaty) and when it is imposed by force after conquest. In the first case, the amount agreed upon cannot be changed. In the second, standard rates apply based on the economic status of the individual: the poor capable earner pays 12 dirhams per year (1 per month), the middle-class pays double (24 dirhams per year, 2 per month), and the wealthy pays double of that (48 dirhams per year, 4 per month). The author then addresses an objection: how can jizya be justified as accepting money for allowing disbelief? The reply is that jizya is not a price for permitting disbelief but rather compensation for not killing or enslaving the adult male non-Muslims, similar to accepting blood money to forgo retaliation. The passage then presents the Hanafi position that jizya is accepted from all non-Muslims including Magians and idol-worshipping non-Arabs, based on precedent from the Companions. The Shafi'i view is given: a uniform rate of one dinar per adult, and jizya only from People of the Book and Magians (the latter considered as having a book). The Hanafis respond with the practice of the early caliphs and the principle that jizya is a substitute for military aid which varies with wealth. The passage also mentions Malik's and Ahmad's views for completeness.

Key Terms
الجزية (al-jizyah): A poll tax imposed on free adult male non-Muslims (dhimmis) in an Islamic state as a sign of submission and in return for protection and exemption from military service.
الفقير المعتمل (al-faqīr al-muʿtamil): The poor person who is physically capable of earning a living, i.e., not disabled or too old to work.
وسط الحال (wasaṭ al-ḥāl): The middle-class person who has some wealth but not enough to be independent of earning.
المكثر (al-mukthir): The wealthy person who possesses abundant wealth (here defined as owning 10,000 dirhams or more).
كتابي (kitābī): A follower of a revealed scripture: Jews, Christians, Samaritans, etc.
مجوسي (majūsī): A Zoroastrian (Magian), follower of the fire-worshipping religion.
وثني عجمي (wathanī ʿajamī): An idol-worshipper from non-Arab origin (e.g., Hindus, Buddhists).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in the passage, what is the annual jizya rate for a middle-class non-Muslim subject?
A) 12 dirhams
B) 24 dirhams
C) 48 dirhams
D) 1 dinar

Key Takeaway
Jizya in the Hanafi school is a graded compensation based on wealth, imposed on all non-Muslim adult males who may be enslaved, justified by the practice of the Caliphs and the principle of substituting for military aid.

Amount of Jizya: Hanafi Graduated Scale and the Shafi'i Objection
Inter-madhhab dispute on jizya amount

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi graduated jizya amounts, explain the Hanafi proof from ijma, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument from the hadith of Mu'adh.

Core Idea
Jizya amounts vary by wealth because jizya substitutes for military support, which varies; fixed rate contradicts purpose.

This lesson examines the amount of jizya imposed on non-Muslim subjects. The Hanafi school adopts a graduated scale based on the practice of the early caliphs and implicit consensus. The Shafi'i school argues for a fixed rate from a hadith. We will analyze the proofs and understand why the Hanafi position is relied upon.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
State the exact amounts for poor, middle, and wealthy as given in the text.
Poor: 12 dirhams/year, Middle: 24, Rich: 48.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Identify al-Shafi'i's view: one dinar fixed on all adults regardless of wealth.
Also note Maliki and Hanbali views as mentioned.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith of Mu'adh that al-Shafi'i cites: 'Take from every adult male or female a dinar or its equivalent.'
The hadith appears general but Hanafi argues it's specific.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: the hadith refers to a specific peace treaty (sulh), not general legislation; the real proof is ijma of the caliphs.
Also the rationale that jizya substitutes for nusra which varies with wealth.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical difference: Hanafi graduated amounts vs. Shafi'i fixed one dinar.
Hanafi is mufta bihi due to ijma.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلى المكثر ضعفه، وتوضع على كتابي ومجوسي ووثني عجمي، أي وتوضع على وهو الغنى الظاهر الغناء أي الجزية لجواز استرقاقه - وضع الجزية على الفقير المكتسب في السنة اثنا عشر درهماً، في كل شهر درهم، وعلى وسط الحال ضعف ذلك في كل شهر درهمين، وعلى الغني ضعف ضعفه، في كل شهر أربعة دراهم، وهذا عندنا، وقال الشافعي: يوضع على كل حالم وحالمة ديناراً، والفقير والغني في ذلك سواء؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لمعاذ : خذ من كل حالم أو حالمة ديناراً أو عدله معافر" أي من كل بالغ وبالغة من غير فصل، ولأن الجزية إنما يجب بدلاً عن القتل حتى لا يجب على من لا يجوز قتله كالذراري، وهذا المعنى ينتظم الغني والفقير. ومذهبنا منقول عن عمر وعثمان وعلي رضي الله عنهم والصحابة متوافرون ولم ينكر عليهم أحد منهم، فصار إجماعاً؛ ولأن الجزية وجبت نصرة للمقاتلة؛ لأنها وجبت بدلاً عن النصرة بالنفس والمال والنصرة يتفاوت بكثرة المال وقلته فكذا ما هو بدله، وما رواه الشافعي فهو في مال وقع عليه الصلح بدليل وجوبه على الحاملة، ولا جزية عليهن، وعدل الشيء بالفتح مثله من خلاف جنسه وبالكسر مثله من جنسه وقوله: "معافر" أي خذ مثل دينار بردا من هذه الجنس، يقال ثوب معافري منسوب إلى معافر بن مر، ثم صار اسماً بغير نسبة، وعند مالك: على كل محتلم أربعة دنانير أو أربعون درهما، وعند أحمد: يفوض إلى رأي الإمام. (مستخلص، فتح، عيني) ضعفه أي ضعف الضعف وهو ثمانية وأربعون درهماً يؤخذ منه في كل شهر أربعة دراهم. (عيني)
And on the wealthy is double its double, and it is imposed on a Jew, a Majusi, and an idol-worshipping non-Arab, meaning it is imposed on the apparent wealth, i.e., jizya, because it is permissible to enslave him. The placement of jizya on the poor earner is twelve dirhams per year, one dirham each month. On the middle state is double that, two dirhams each month. On the wealthy is double its double, four dirhams each month. This is our position. Al-Shafi'i said: One dinar is imposed on every adult male and female, the poor and the rich are equal in that, because of his statement (peace be upon him) to Mu'adh: 'Take from every adult male or female a dinar or its equivalent of Ma'afir' meaning from every adult male and female without distinction. And because jizya is only obligatory as a substitute for killing, so it is not obligatory on those whose killing is not permissible, like children. This meaning encompasses the rich and poor. Our school is transmitted from Umar, Uthman, Ali (may Allah be pleased with them) and the Companions were numerous and none of them denied it, so it became consensus. And because jizya is obligatory for the support of the fighters, as it is a substitute for support with life and wealth, and support varies with abundance and scarcity of wealth, so its substitute varies likewise. What al-Shafi'i narrated is regarding wealth upon which a peace treaty was made, evidenced by its obligation on women, yet no jizya is on them. 'Adl' (with fatha) means its like from a different genus, and (with kasra) means its like from the same genus. His statement 'Ma'afir' means take a dinar of cloth from this genus. It is said a Ma'afiri garment, attributed to Ma'afir ibn Murr, then it became a name without attribution. According to Malik: on every adult male four dinars or forty dirhams. According to Ahmad: it is delegated to the opinion of the Imam. (Mukhtasar, Fath, Ayni) 'Double its double' means double of double, which is forty-eight dirhams, taken from him each month four dirhams. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the amount of jizya (poll tax) on non-Muslim subjects. The Hanafi position, based on practice of the early caliphs and consensus, sets jizya according to wealth: the poor earner pays 12 dirhams annually (1 per month), the middle class 24 dirhams (2 per month), and the wealthy 48 dirhams (4 per month). Al-Shafi'i argues for a fixed rate of one dinar per adult (male or female) based on a hadith of Mu'adh. The Hanafi response distinguishes that the hadith refers to a specific treaty, not general law, and that the amount varies because jizya is a substitute for military support, which varies with wealth. The passage also notes Maliki (4 dinars or 40 dirhams) and Hanbali (delegated to imam) positions. The commentary from Ayni clarifies that 'double its double' for the rich means 48 dirhams annually.

Key Terms
الجزية (al-jizyah): Poll tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects in an Islamic state as a substitute for military service and protection.
معافر (ma'afir): A type of cloth from Yemen, used as equivalent to a dinar in the hadith of Mu'adh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, how much jizya does a middle-class non-Muslim pay per year?
A) 12 dirhams
B) 24 dirhams
C) 48 dirhams
D) 1 dinar

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi graduated jizya scale is based on the consensus of the early caliphs, and the opposing hadith is interpreted as specific to a peace treaty.

On Whom Jizya Is Imposed: Categories and Evidence
Defines categories of non-Muslims liable for jizya and includes inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of non-Muslims liable for jizya in the Hanafi school, identify the evidence for each, and explain the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Jizya is wajib from Kitabi, Majusi, and non-Arab idol-worshippers; the key is permissibility of enslavement.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq defines the three categories of non-Muslims on whom jizya is wajib. It also presents the Hanafi proofs and addresses the Shafi'i objection. Understanding this ruling is crucial for the fiqh of jihad and state relations with non-Muslim minorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
List the three groups: Kitabi (Jew, Christian, Samaritan), Majusi (Zoroastrian), and Wathani Ajami (non-Arab idol-worshipper). Note the distinction between wathan (wall-engraved idol) and sanam (human-shaped idol).
Samaritans are included as Kitabi due to belief in a revealed book (Psalms).
2
State the ruling for each
Jizya is wajib on each category. The ruling is derived from different evidences.
3
Locate the Hanafi proof for Majusi
The Prophet ﷺ took jizya from the Majus of Hajar, testified by Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf and accepted by Umar. This hadith (narrated by Bukhari) establishes permissibility despite Majus not being People of the Book.
The hadith is ahaad (zanni thubut) but qati al-dalalah.
4
Understand the Hanafi proof for Wathani Ajami
Since it is permissible to enslave non-Arab idol-worshippers, imposing jizya is a valid alternative to enslavement. Jizya is not exclusive to People of the Book.
This is supported by qiyas: the option of jizya exists wherever enslavement is allowed.
5
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Shafi'i: jizya is only for People of the Book (9:29) and Majus by hadith; all others must be fought (2:193). Hanafi response: enslavement proves jizya is permissible, and the restriction is overridden by this principle; Malik and Ahmad also include idol-worshippers.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): Shafi'i requires conversion or war for an idol-worshipper; Hanafi accepts jizya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتابي: هو نسبة إلى كتاب منزل من السماء، والمعنى توضع الجزية على الذي يعتقد كتاباً من الكتب المنزلة كاليهودي، فإنه يعتقد التوراة، والسامري، فإنه يعتقد الزبور والنصراني، فإنه يعتقد الإنجيل، وقوله: "ومجوسي" أي توضع الجزية عليه لما روي عن عمر رضي الله عنه أنه لم يأخذ الجزية من المجوس حتى شهد عبد الرحمن بن عوف رضي الله عنه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أخذها من مجوس هجر، رواه البخاري ،وآخرون وعند الشافعي الجزية مخصوصة بأهل الكتاب، والمجوس عنده من أهل الكتاب فيكون داخلاً فيها. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٣٨/١] أيضاً أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وقوله: "وثني عجمي" أي وتوضع على عبدة الأوثان من العجم والوثن ما كان منقوشاً في حائط، والصنم: اسم لما كان على صورة الإنسان وقال الشافعي: لا تؤخذ منهم؛ لأن القتال واجب، بقوله تعالى: وَقَاتِلُوهُمْ ﴾ (البقرة: ۱۹۳) إلا أنا عرفنا جواز ترك القتال بالجزية في حق أهل الكتاب كما قال تعالى: مِنَ الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا الْكِتَابَ حَتَّى يُعْطُوا الْجِزْيَةَ﴾ (التوبة: ٢٩) وفي حق المجوس بالخبر كما روينا، فبقى ما ورائهم على الأصل، فلاجزية عليهم؛ لأنهم ليسوا بأهل كتاب ولنا أنه يجوز استرقاقهم، فيجوز ضرب الجزية عليهم؛ ولأن الجزية غير مختصة بأهل الكتاب وبه قال مالك وأحمد في رواية وعنه في أخرى توضع على كل كتابي فقط، وعن مالك توضع على كل كافر إلا مشركي قريش والعجمي خلاف العربي. (مستخلص، فتح) ومجوسي: أي وعلى مجوسي وهو واحد المجوس وهم قوم يعظمون النار ويعبدونها. (عيني) ووثني: أي وتوضع أيضاً على وثني وهو عابد الأوثان. (عيني)
Kitabi: It is a relation to a book revealed from heaven. The meaning is that jizya is placed on one who believes in a revealed book, like a Jew who believes in the Torah, a Samaritan who believes in the Psalms, and a Christian who believes in the Gospel. His statement: 'and a Majusi' meaning jizya is placed on him because it is narrated from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) that he did not take jizya from the Majus until Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf (may Allah be pleased with him) testified that the Prophet (peace be upon him) took it from the Majus of Hajar, narrated by Bukhari and others. According to al-Shafi'i, jizya is specific to the People of the Book, and the Majus according to him are from the People of the Book, so they are included. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/438] Also that the Prophet (peace be upon him)... and his statement: 'and an idol-worshipping non-Arab' meaning it is placed on idol-worshippers from the non-Arabs. Al-Wathan is what is engraved on a wall, and al-sanam is a name for what is in human form. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not taken from them because fighting is obligatory by His statement: 'Fight them' (2:193) except that we know the permissibility of leaving fighting through jizya for the People of the Book as He said: 'from those who have been given the Scripture until they give jizya' (9:29) and for Majus by the hadith as we narrated, so the rest remain on the original principle, thus no jizya on them because they are not people of the Book. Our proof: it is permissible to enslave them, so it is permissible to impose jizya on them, and because jizya is not exclusive to the People of the Book. This is also the view of Malik and Ahmad in one narration, and from him in another it is placed only on every Kitabi, and from Malik it is placed on every disbeliever except the polytheists of Quraysh. Al-Ajami is the opposite of Arab. (Mukhtasar, Fath) And Majusi: meaning and on a Majusi, which is one of the Majus, a people who venerate fire and worship it. (Ayni) And Wathani: meaning and also placed on a wathani, who is an idol worshipper. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage defines the categories of non-Muslims on whom jizya is imposed. The Hanafi school includes: Kitabi (Jews, Christians, Samaritans), Majusi (Zoroastrians) based on the precedent of the Prophet taking jizya from the Majus of Hajar as testified by Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf and accepted by Umar, and Wathani ajami (idol-worshipping non-Arabs) because it is permissible to enslave them and jizya is not limited to People of the Book. Al-Shafi'i restricts jizya to People of the Book (including Majus by his view) and excludes idol-worshippers, arguing that fighting remains obligatory for them. The Hanafi response: since idol-worshippers can be enslaved, jizya is permissible as an alternative, and this is also the position of Malik and Ahmad. The text also distinguishes between wathan (engraved idol) and sanam (human-shaped idol), both are worshipped.

Key Terms
كتابي (kitabi): One who believes in a revealed book (Jew, Christian, Samaritan).
مجوسي (majusi): Zoroastrian, fire-worshipper; jizya taken from them based on prophetic precedent.
وثني (wathani): Idol-worshipper; specifically non-Arab idol-worshippers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because the Quran explicitly commands it
D) Because they are Arab polytheists

Key Takeaway
Jizya is wajib from Kitabi, Majusi, and non-Arab idol-worshippers in the Hanafi school, based on prophetic practice and the principle that enslavement implies the option of jizya.

Exemptions from Jizya in the Hanafi School
Lists categories exempt from jizya with rationales and internal debates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the categories exempt from jizya in the Hanafi school and state the reasoning for each exemption.

Core Idea
Jizya substitutes for military support; those unable to fight are exempt.

The jizya is a tax on non-Muslims in exchange for protection and exemption from military service. However, Hanafi fiqh specifies that many individuals are exempt because they are unable to provide military support or are granted special status. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq enumerates these exemptions and provides the legal reasoning behind each.

Guided Path
1
Identify the major categories
Scan the text for the key categories explicitly mentioned: Arab polytheists, apostates, children, women, slaves, mukatabs, chronically ill, blind, paralyzed, very old, poor non-working, and non-mixing monk.
2
Understand the rationale for each
For each category, note the reason given: e.g., Arab polytheists and apostates because of severity of disbelief; women and children because they do not fight; slaves because they are not subject to killing; etc.
The core principle is that jizya substitutes for military service (nusra).
3
Note exceptions and internal differences
Observe the exception for women of Banu Taghlib and the differences between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the blind/ill and the monk.
4
Compare with Shafi'i position
The text contrasts the Hanafi position with that of al-Shafi'i concerning the poor non-working and the hadith of Mu'adh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا عربي ومرتد وصبى وامرأة وعبدٍ ومكاتب. أي ولا توضع الجزية على عبدة الأوثان من العرب، ولا على المرتد؛ لتغليظ كفرهما، أما مشركو العرب؛ فلأنه علية نشأ بين أظهرهم، والقرآن نزل بلغتهم، والمعجزة في حقهم أظهر؛ لأنهم كانوا أعرف بمعانيه، وبوجوه الفصاحة، فغلظ عليهم، قال تعالى: ﴿تُقَاتِلُونَهُمْ أَوْ يُسْلِمُونَ﴾ (الفتح: 16) وأما المرتد؛ فلأنه كفر بربه بعد ما رأى محاسن الإسلام وبعد ما هدي إليه، فلا يقبل من الفريقين إلا الإسلام أو السيف زيادة في العقوبة في حقهم، وإذا ظهر عليهم فنساؤهم وذراريهم فيء؛ لأنه علي كان يسترق ذراري مشركي العرب، وأبو بكر رضي الله عنه استرق نساء بني حنيفة وصبيانهم وكانوا مرتدين وكفر المرتد أغلظ من مشركي العرب، ولهذا تجبر نساء المرتدين وذراريهم على الإسلام، ولا تجبر نساء عبدة الأوثان من العرب وذراريهم على الإسلام. [تبيين الحقائق: ٤/١٥٨] (مستخلص، فتح) صبي وامرأة سواء كانت حرة أو أمة أو أم ولد أو مدبرة أو مكاتبة لا توضع عليها إلا إذا كانت من بني تغلب. (ط، مس] أي ولا توضع أيضاً على الصبي، ومثله المجنون والمعتوه ولا على المرأة؛ لأن الجزية خلف عن النصرة، ولا تجب عليهما النصرة بالقتال؛ لأنهما لا يقتلان ولا يقاتلان؛ لعدم الأهلية إلا إذا كانت من بني تغلب، فإنها تؤخذ من نسائهم كما تؤخذ من رجالهم؛ لأن ذلك وجب بالصلح. فإن قيل: يلزمها النصرة بالمال لو كانت مسلمة فكذا إذا كانت كافرة ذمية؟ قلنا: الجزية شرعت خلفاً عن النصرة في حقنا وعن القتال والقتل في حق المأخوذ منه؛ ولهذا يصرف المأخوذ في المقاتلة؛ ليحصل النصرة بماله كما يحصل ببدنه لو كان مسلما. وعبد ومكاتب أي ولا على عبد ولا مكاتب وكذا أبن أم الولد؛ لأنها بدل عن القتل في حقهم، وعن النصرة في حقنا، فعلى الاعتبار الأول توضع وعلى الاعتبار الثاني لا توضع فلا يجب بالشك؛ ولا يؤدي عنهم مواليهم؛ لأنهم تحملوا زيادة الجزية بسببهم أي بالغنا فلو أخذت منهم ثانياً لأجل هؤلاء، يصير الأخذ مرتين، وقوله : وزمن وأعمى أي لا توضع عليهما؛ لأنهما ليسا من أهل القتل والقتال، وكذلك المفلوج والشيخ الكبير، وعن أبي يوسف أنه يجب إذا كان له مال؛ لأنه يقتل في الجملة وبه قال الشافعى في قول، وقوله: وفقير غير معتمل أي لا توضع على فقير غير مكتسب، وفيه خلاف الشافعي؛ لإطلاق حديث معاذ له الذي مر، ولنا: أن عثمان رضي الله عنه لم يوظفها على فقير غير معتمل، وكان ذلك بمحضر من الصحابة ولأن خراج الأرض لم يوظف على أرض لا طاقة لها، فكذا خراج البدن، وقد ذكرنا أن الحديث كان في مال وقع عليه الصلح. وقوله : وراهب لا يخالطهم أي لا توضع على الراهب الذي لا يخالط الناس، وعن أبي حنيفة أن الراهب إذا كان قادراً على العمل، توضع عليه، وهي رواية عن أبي يوسف؛ لأنه ضيع قدرته على العمل، فصار كتعطيل الأرض الخراجية، ووجه رواية المتن: أنه لا قتل عليهم إذا كانوا لا يخالطون الناس، والجزية لإسقاط القتل، :
Not an Arab, an apostate, a child, a woman, a slave, and a mukatab. Meaning: jizya is not placed on idol-worshippers from the Arabs, nor on the apostate, due to the severity of their disbelief. As for the Arab polytheists, because they are a noble people who arose among them, the Quran was revealed in their language, and the miracle was more apparent for them because they were more knowledgeable of its meanings and aspects of eloquence, so severity was applied to them. Allah said: 'You fight them or they become Muslims' (48:16). As for the apostate, because he disbelieved in his Lord after seeing the beauties of Islam and after being guided to it, so from the two groups nothing is accepted except Islam or the sword as an increase in punishment for them. When they are overcome, their women and children become fay', because Ali used to enslave the children of Arab polytheists, and Abu Bakr (may Allah be pleased with him) enslaved the women and children of Banu Hanifa and they were apostates, and the disbelief of the apostate is more severe than that of Arab polytheists. For this reason, the women and children of apostates are forced to embrace Islam, while the women and children of Arab idol-worshippers are not forced. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 4/158) (Mukhtasar, Fath) A child and a woman, whether free or slave, umm walad, mudabbara, or mukataba, jizya is not imposed on her unless she is from Banu Taghlib. (T, Mus) Meaning: it is not imposed on the child, and similarly the insane and the imbecile, nor on the woman, because jizya is in place of nusra (support), and nusra through fighting is not obligatory on them as they are not killed and do not fight due to lack of capacity, except if she is from Banu Taghlib, then it is taken from their women as it is taken from their men because it was obligated by a peace treaty. If it is said: She is obliged to support with wealth if she were Muslim, so likewise if she is a disbelieving dhimmah? We say: Jizja was legislated as a substitute for nusra with respect to us and for fighting and killing with respect to the one from whom it is taken; therefore what is taken is spent on the fighters to achieve support with his wealth just as support is achieved with his body if he were Muslim. And slave and mukatab: meaning not on a slave nor a mukatab, and similarly the child of an umm walad, because it is a substitute for killing with respect to them, and for nusra with respect to us. On the first consideration it would be imposed, on the second it is not imposed, so it is not obligatory due to doubt; and their masters do not pay it on their behalf because they (masters) bear an increase in jizya due to them, meaning due to our exaggeration (charging extra). If jizja were taken a second time for these, it would constitute taking twice. His statement: 'and chronically ill and blind' meaning it is not imposed on them because they are not of the people of killing and fighting, and likewise the paralyzed and the very old. From Abu Yusuf that it is wajib if he has wealth because he is killed in general, and al-Shafi'i said this in one opinion. His statement: 'and a poor person who does not work' meaning it is not imposed on a poor person who does not earn. There is a disagreement with al-Shafi'i due to the general meaning of the hadith of Mu'adh mentioned earlier. Our proof: Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) did not impose it on a poor person who does not work, and that was in the presence of the Companions, and because the land tax (kharaj) is not imposed on land that has no capacity, so the same for the tax on the body. And we have mentioned that the hadith pertains to wealth upon which a peace treaty was made. His statement: 'and a monk who does not mix with them' meaning it is not imposed on the monk who does not mix with people. From Abu Hanifa that if the monk is able to work, it is imposed on him, and this is a narration from Abu Yusuf, because he wasted his ability to work, so it is like neglecting kharaj land. The basis of the version of the matn (text) is that there is no killing (qatl) on them if they do not mix with people, and jizya is for removing killing.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage lists those exempt from jizya. First, Arab polytheists and apostates are exempt because of the severity of their disbelief: for them only Islam or the sword is accepted. This is based on Quran 48:16 and the practice of the early caliphs. Apostates are considered even more severe, and their families are forced to Islam. Second, children and women are exempt because jizya substitutes for military support, which they are not required to provide (except women of Banu Taghlib by treaty). The text responds to an objection: even if a Muslim woman must support with wealth, a dhimmi woman does not because jizya is a substitute for killing, not just wealth. Third, slaves and mukatabs are exempt because jizya is a substitute for killing, and they are not subject to killing; masters do not pay for them as it would double the burden. Fourth, the chronically ill, blind, paralyzed, and very old are exempt as they cannot fight. Abu Yusuf and al-Shafi'i have a view that if such a person has wealth, jizya may be levied. Fifth, a poor person who does not work is exempt; Uthman's practice and analogy to land tax support this, refuting the general hadith of Mu'adh. Sixth, a monk who does not mix with people is exempt because there is no killing on him. Abu Hanifa and a narration from Abu Yusuf say if the monk can work, jizya is imposed, as he wastes his capacity.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): Apostate from Islam, whose disbelief is considered more severe than original polytheism.
بني تغلب (banu taghlib): A Christian Arab tribe whose women pay jizya due to a peace treaty.
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has made a contract of manumission with his master.
زمن (zamin): Chronically ill person.
راهب (rahb): Monk who secludes himself from society.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, why is jizya not imposed on women?
A) Because women are not required to fight
B) Because women are poor
C) Because women are from Banu Taghlib
D) Because women are not people of the Book

Key Takeaway
Jizya is not a blanket obligation; Hanafi fiqh exempts those who cannot provide military support, with rare exceptions for treaty obligations.

Exemptions from Jizya and Its Dropping
Rulings on exemptions from jizya and its dropping conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the categories exempt from jizya in the Hanafi school and explain when jizya drops with reference to the proofs.

Core Idea
Jizya is not imposed on those who cannot fight or whose disbelief is most severe; it drops with Islam or death.

The classical Hanafi texts detail a number of exemptions from the jizya (poll tax) that apply to certain categories of non-Muslims. Understanding these exemptions and the conditions under which jizya drops is essential for the correct application of this ruling. In this lesson, we will explore the key exemptions and the evidence for them, as well as the important dispute over whether jizya drops upon conversion to Islam or death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exempt categories
Read the passage and list all categories on whom jizya is not imposed. Note the reasons given for each exemption.
The main categories are: Arab polytheists, apostates, minors, women, slaves, mukatabs, disabled, blind, poor non-earner, reclusive monk.
2
Understand the basis for exemption
For each category, identify the underlying rationale: inability to fight (women, minors, disabled, etc.) or severity of disbelief (Arab polytheists, apostates).
Jizya is a substitute for military assistance (nusrah) and a penalty for disbelief.
3
Trace the dalil for Arab polytheists and apostates
Find the Quranic verse (48:16) cited and explain how it supports the exemption.
The verse commands fighting them until they submit, implying jizya is not an option.
4
Analyze the dispute on dropping with Islam and death
Compare the Hanafi position with that of al-Shafi'i and Malik. Identify the key proof (hadith) and the counter-argument.
The Hanafi rely on the hadith 'Whoever becomes Muslim, no jizya is due from him.'
5
Apply the rulings to practical scenarios
Test your understanding by applying the exemptions and dropping rules to hypothetical cases (e.g., a blind wealthy dhimmi, a Banu Taghlib woman who converts).
Pay attention to intra-Hanafi differences (e.g., Abu Yusuf on disabled persons with wealth).

(ط، مس] أي ولا توضع أيضاً على الصبي، ومثله المجنون والمعتوه ولا على المرأة؛ لأن الجزية خلف عن النصرة، ولا تجب عليهما النصرة بالقتال؛ لأنهما لا يقتلان ولا يقاتلان ؛ لعدم الأهلية إلا إذا كانت من بني تغلب، فإنها تؤخذ من نسائهم كما تؤخذ من رجالهم؛ لأن ذلك وجب بالصلح .

أي الجزية
- وقيد بعدم مخالطة الناس؛ لأنهم إذا كانوا يخالطون الناس كرواهب هذا الزمان تجب عليهم الجزية بالاتفاق. ولو أدرك الصبي، أو أفاق المجنون أو عتق العبد أو برأ المريض قبل وضع الإمام الجزية، وضع عليهم، وبعد وضعها لا توضع؛ لأن المعتبر أهليتهم وقت الوضع بخلاف الفقير إذا أيسر بعد الوضع حيث توضع عليه؛ لأنه أهل الجزية، وإنما سقطت عنه للعجر وقد زال (مستخلص ،فتح عيني) وزمن أي ولا على زمن وهو الذي بعض أعضائه معدوم أو قواه معطلة. (فتح) وأعمى: أي ولا على أعمى لعدم النصرة بالقتال. (فتح) لا يخالطهم أي لا يخالط الناس ولو خالط كان كغيره، وكذا المفلوج والشيخ الكبير. (ط) وتسقط بالإسلام أي لو أسلم من عليه الجزية بعد ما تمت السنة تسقط عنه الجزية؛ لقوله عليها: "من أسلم فلا جزية عليه وإنما لم يسقط الرق بالإسلام؛ لأنه تعلق به حق معين فلا يبطل به، وقيد بالجزية؛ لأن الديون والخراج والأجرة لا تسقط بالإسلام والموت اتفاقا، وقال الشافعي: لا تسقط الجزية بهما؛ لأنها دين، وبه قال مالك في الموت؛ ولأنها وجبت عوضا عن العصمة وعن السكنى في دار الإسلام وقد وصل إليه المعوض بنيل والسكنى فلا يسقط عنه العوض بعارض. ولنا ما روينا؛ ولأنها عوض عن امتهان وجوده وهو القتل؛ لأنها وجبت عقوبة على الكفر أو بدلا عن النصرة، ولا تبقى العقوبة على الكفر بعد الإسلام ولا بعد الموت وقوله والتكرر" أي وكذلك تسقط الجزية بالتكرر بأن لم يؤخذ منه الجزية حتى حال عليه حولان أو أكثر عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأنها عقوبة، فإذا اجتمعت تداخلت كالحدود، وقالا يطالب بها؛ لأنها واجبة في الذمة فلا تسقط بالتأخير كالزكاة في حق المسلم، وبه قالت الثلاثة،
العصمة.
وخراج الأرض قيل: على هذا الخلاف، وقيل: لا تداخل فيه اتفاقاً. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٣٩/١] (مستخلص) والموت: أي وتسقط بموت الذمي أيضاً ولو بعد مضي السنة. (ط) ولا تحدث الإحداث: إيجاد شيء لم يكن من قبل، والبيعة اسم لمعبد النصارى واليهود وكذا الكنيسة إلا أن استعمال البيعة لمعبد النصارى أغلب، واستعمال الكنيسة لمعبد اليهود أغلب والمعنى أن إحداث البيعة والكنيسة لا يجوز في دار الإسلام؛ لقوله علية: لاخصاء في الإسلام ولا كنيسة، والمراد لا تحدث في دار الإسلام كنيسة لم تكن فإن أحدثوها يجب على أهل الإسلام أن يمنعوها والخصاء بالكسر والمد نزع الخصية، وقيل: المراد به الامتناع من النساء حتى يصير في حكم الخصي، وكذا لا يحدث بيت النار ، ولا الصومعة وهي بيت التخلي تبنى برأس كبير؛ ليتعبد فيها بالانقطاع عن الناس. ومن الإحداث نقلها من مكان إلى آخر؛ لأنه إحداث في ذلك الموضع، ويمنعون من بيع الخمر والخنزير، =
Book of Military Expeditions and Jihad. Chapter on Rulings of Jizya. No [jizya on] Arab [polytheist] nor apostate, nor minor, nor woman, nor slave, nor mukatab. Meaning: Nor on a slave, nor on a mukatab. 'No Arab nor apostate' means jizya is not imposed on idol-worshipping Arabs, nor on the apostate, due to the severity of their disbelief. As for Arab polytheists, because he [the Prophet] arose among them, the Quran was revealed in their language, and the miracle was more manifest for them because they were most knowledgeable of its meanings and aspects of eloquence, so [punishment] was made severe for them. Allah said: 'You fight them or they become Muslim' (48:16). As for the apostate, because he disbelieved in his Lord after seeing the beauties of Islam and after being guided to it, so nothing is accepted from the two groups except Islam or the sword, as an increase in punishment for them. If they are overcome, their women and children become fay', because 'Ali used to enslave the children of Arab polytheists, and Abu Bakr enslaved the women and children of Banu Hanifah, and they were apostates, and the disbelief of the apostate is more severe than that of Arab polytheists. Therefore, the women and children of apostates are compelled to Islam, while the women and children of Arab idol-worshippers are not compelled to Islam. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 4/158) (excerpt, Fath). [The exemption for] a minor and a woman, whether free, slave, umm walad, mudabbara, or mukataba, is not imposed [on them] except if she is from Banu Taghlib. (T, M) Meaning: Nor is it imposed on a minor, and similarly the insane and the mentally deficient, nor on a woman, because jizya is a substitute for [military] assistance, and assistance through fighting is not obligatory for them because they do not kill nor fight due to lack of capacity, except if she is from Banu Taghlib, then it is taken from their women as it is taken from their men, because that was stipulated in the peace treaty. If it is said: A Muslim woman is obligated to provide financial assistance, so why not a dhimmi woman? We say: Jizya was legislated as a substitute for assistance on our part and for fighting and killing on the part of the one from whom it is taken; therefore, what is taken is spent on fighters, so that financial assistance is achieved just as physical assistance would be if he were Muslim. 'And a slave and a mukatab' meaning: nor on a slave nor a mukatab, and similarly the child of an umm walad (because it is a substitute for killing on their part and for assistance on our part; according to the first consideration it would be imposed, according to the second it is not imposed, so it is not obligatory due to doubt; nor do their masters pay it on their behalf because they have already borne an increase in jizya due to them, meaning they have paid enough. So if it were taken from them a second time on account of these, it would be taking twice. And his statement: 'and a disabled person and a blind person' meaning they are not imposed upon because they are not people of killing and fighting, and similarly the paralyzed and the very old. And from Abu Yusuf that it is obligatory if he has wealth, because he is killed in some sense, and al-Shafi'i said the same in one opinion. And his statement: 'and a poor person who does not work' meaning it is not imposed on a poor person who does not earn, and there is a difference with al-Shafi'i due to the general nature of the hadith of Mu'adh mentioned earlier. Our evidence: 'Uthman did not impose it on a poor person who does not work, and that was in the presence of the Companions, and because kharaj on land is not imposed on land that has no capacity, so too the kharaj of the body. And we have mentioned that the hadith was concerning wealth that was part of a peace treaty. And his statement: 'and a monk who does not mix with them' meaning it is not imposed on the monk who does not mix with people. And from Abu Hanifa that if the monk is able to work, it is imposed on him, and that is a narration from Abu Yusuf, because he wasted his ability to work, so he is like one who neglects kharaj land. The basis of the text's narration: there is no killing upon them if they do not mix with people, and jizya is to remove killing. And the disabled and blind, and the poor non-earner, and the monk who does not mix with them, and it drops with Islam and repetition and death. And no new church may be built. Meaning the jizya. And the condition of not mixing with people is because if they mix with people like the monks of this time, jizya is obligatory upon them by consensus. If the minor reaches puberty, or the insane regains sanity, or the slave is freed, or the sick recovers before the Imam imposes the jizya, it is imposed upon them; after its imposition it is not imposed, because their capacity at the time of imposition is considered, unlike the poor person who becomes wealthy after imposition, where it is imposed upon him, because he is eligible for jizya, and it was only dropped due to incapacity which has ceased. (excerpt, Fath 'Ayni) 'Disabled' meaning: nor on a disabled person, who has some missing limbs or incapacitated faculties. (Fath) 'Blind' meaning: nor on a blind person due to lack of assistance through fighting. (Fath) 'Does not mix with them' meaning he does not mix with people; if he mixes, he is like others, and similarly the paralyzed and the very old. (T) 'And it drops with Islam' meaning: if the one upon whom jizya is due becomes Muslim after the year has completed, jizya drops from him, because the Prophet said: 'Whoever becomes Muslim, no jizya is due from him.' Slavery does not drop with Islam because it is attached to a specific right and is not nullified by it. He restricted it to jizya because debts, kharaj, and rent do not drop with Islam or death by consensus. Al-Shafi'i said: jizya does not drop by these [Islam or death] because it is a debt, and Malik said the same regarding death, and because it is compensation for protection and residence in Dar al-Islam, and he has received the compensated benefit of protection and residence, so compensation does not drop due to an accident. Our evidence is what we narrated, and because it is compensation for the humiliation of his existence, which is killing, because it was imposed as a punishment for disbelief or as a substitute for assistance, and punishment for disbelief does not remain after Islam nor after death. And his statement: 'and repetition' meaning: similarly, jizya drops with repetition, i.e., if jizya is not taken from him so that two or more years pass, according to Abu Hanifa, because it is a punishment, so when multiple instances accumulate, they overlap like hudud. The two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] said: he is demanded for it because it is an obligation in the dhimmah and does not drop with delay, like zakat for a Muslim, and the three [imams] said the same. And kharaj on land: it is said this difference applies, and it is said there is no overlapping by consensus. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/439) (excerpt) 'And death' meaning: it drops with the death of the dhimmi as well, even after the year has passed. (T) 'And do not initiate' meaning: bringing into existence something that did not exist before. 'Bi'ah' is a name for the place of worship of Christians and Jews, and similarly 'kanisah', except that the use of 'bi'ah' for Christian worship places is more common, and 'kanisah' for Jewish worship places is more common. The meaning is that initiating the building of a church or synagogue is not permissible in Dar al-Islam, because the Prophet said: 'There is no castration in Islam and no church.' The intent is that no church that did not exist should be built in Dar al-Islam. If they build it, the Muslims must prevent it. 'Khusa' (castration) means removal of testicles, and it is said the meaning is abstaining from women until one becomes like a eunuch. Similarly, no fire temple may be built, nor a 'sawma'ah' (hermitage), which is a place of seclusion built on a high head, for worshiping in isolation from people. And transferring it from one place to another is considered initiating, because it is initiating in that location. And they are prevented from selling wine and pigs.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with its commentary, details the exemptions from jizya (poll tax) and the conditions under which it drops. The passage type is a ruling with proof, as each exemption is supported by textual evidence or rational reasoning.

The text begins by listing those on whom jizya is not imposed: Arab polytheists, apostates, minors, women, slaves, and mukatabs. For Arab polytheists and apostates, the severity of their disbelief makes them ineligible for jizya; they are only offered Islam or the sword. This is based on the Quranic verse (48:16). For apostates in particular, their disbelief after guidance makes their punishment more severe. As a result, their women and children are enslaved if captured, and they are compelled to Islam, unlike Arab polytheists.

Minors and women are exempt because jizya is a substitute for military assistance (nusrah), and they are not obligated to fight. The exception is the women of Banu Taghlib, because their jizya was stipulated in a peace treaty. A possible objection—that a Muslim woman must give financial support—is answered by distinguishing that jizya is specifically a substitute for the obligation of fighting and killing, not just any financial aid.

Slaves and mukatabs are also exempt, because jizya is either a substitute for killing (on their part) or for assistance (on our part). Since both considerations lead to doubt, it is not obligatory. Their masters do not pay on their behalf, as they already bear additional jizya due to them.

The disabled (zamin), blind (a'ma), paralyzed, very old, poor non-earner, and reclusive monk are exempt because they cannot fight. There is an intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf (and Shafi'i) require jizya from the wealthy disabled, because they can be killed in some sense. For the poor non-earner, the Hanafi evidence includes the practice of 'Uthman and analogy to land tax (kharaj). For the monk, if he is able to work but refrains, Abu Hanifa imposes jizya, as he wastes his capacity.

The jizya drops if the person becomes Muslim during the year, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'Whoever becomes Muslim, no jizya is due from him.' This is contrary to Shafi'i and Malik, who consider it a debt that does not drop. The Hanafi view is that it is a punishment for disbelief or a substitute for assistance, both of which cease with Islam or death. Another drop occurs through tafarrur (repetition/non-collection for two or more years) according to Abu Hanifa, due to overlapping punishments similar to hudud; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree, comparing it to zakat.

Finally, the passage prohibits building new churches, synagogues, fire temples, or hermitages in Dar al-Islam, based on the hadith 'No castration in Islam and no church.' Transferring an existing place of worship is considered new construction. Muslims must prevent such buildings, and dhimmis are also prevented from openly selling wine and pork.

Key Terms
جزية (jizyah): A poll tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) in an Islamic state, as a substitute for military service and protection.
مرتد (murtadd): A person who apostatizes from Islam. In this context, jizya is not accepted from apostates; they are offered only Islam or the sword.
بني تغلب (Banū Taghlib): A Christian Arab tribe; their women are liable for jizya by treaty, unlike other women.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, what happens to jizya if a dhimmi dies after the year has passed?
A) It must be paid from his estate.
B) It drops and is not collected.
C) His heirs must pay it.
D) It becomes a debt on his soul.

Key Takeaway
Jizya is exempted for those who cannot fight or whose disbelief is most severe, and it drops upon Islam or death.

Exemptions from Jizya: Who is Not Liable
Rulings on exemptions from jizya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four categories exempt from jizya and explain the condition regarding monks and changes in status before or after jizya placement.

Core Idea
Jizya is only owed by able-bodied, earning dhimmis; the ill, blind, destitute, and secluded monks are exempt.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq lists four groups of dhimmis who do not pay jizya: the chronically ill, blind, poor non-earners, and monks who do not mix with people. Understanding these exemptions is essential for correctly applying the jizya system. The commentary also clarifies when a person becomes liable if their condition changes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exempt categories
Read the Arabic: zamin, a'ma, faqir ghayr mu'tamil, and rahib la yukhalituhum. Note the condition for the monk: if he mixes, he must pay.
The text explicitly exempts these four.
2
Understand the timing condition
If a child reaches puberty, an insane person recovers, a slave is freed, or a sick person recovers before the imam places the jizya, they become liable. After placement, they remain exempt for that year.
Contrast with the poor person: if he later becomes wealthy after placement, he becomes liable because his inability has ceased.
3
Note the rationale for exemptions
Exemptions are based on inability to fight or earn. The blind and chronically ill cannot participate in fighting; the poor non-earner cannot pay; the secluded monk is not a potential soldier.
This is consistent with jizya as a substitute for military service.

Rulings of Jizya. And (no jizya on) the chronically ill, the blind, the poor who does not work, and the monk who does not mix with them. And jizya falls off by Islam, repetition, and death. i.e., and no jizya on the non-earner. = (i.e., the jizya) - And it is conditioned by not mixing with people; because if they mix with people, like the monks of this time, jizya is obligatory on them by agreement. And if the child reaches puberty, or the insane recovers, or the slave is freed, or the sick recovers before the Imam places the jizya, it is placed on them; after placement it is not placed, because consideration is given to their eligibility at the time of placement, contrary to the poor person who becomes wealthy after placement where it is placed upon him, because he is eligible for jizya, and it only fell off due to inability, and it has ceased. (Mukhtasar, Fath al-Qadir, 'Ayni) And 'zaman': i.e., no jizya on the one with chronic illness, who has some limbs missing or faculties disabled. (Fath) And 'a'ma': i.e., no jizya on the blind due to lack of support in fighting. (Fath) 'la yukhalituhum': i.e., he does not mix with people; if he mixes, he is like others, and similarly the paralyzed and the very old. (Tahawi) 'And it falls off by Islam': i.e., if the one on whom jizya is due embraces Islam after the year has completed, jizya falls off from him; due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Whoever embraces Islam, there is no jizya upon him.' And slavery does not fall off by Islam because a specific right is attached to it, so it is not invalidated. And it is restricted to jizya because debts, kharaj, and rental fees do not fall off by Islam or death by agreement. And al-Shafi'i said: Jizya does not fall off by either, because it is a debt, and Malik said the same regarding death; and because it became obligatory as compensation for protection and residence in Dar al-Islam, and he has received the compensated benefit of safety and residence, so the compensation should not fall off due to an incidental occurrence. And our proof is what we have narrated; and because it is compensation for the humiliation of his existence, i.e., killing; because it was made obligatory as punishment for disbelief or as a substitute for support, and punishment for disbelief does not remain after Islam nor after death. And his statement 'wa al-takarrur': i.e., similarly jizya falls off by repetition, by not taking jizya from him until two or more years have passed according to Abu Hanifa, because it is a punishment, so if they accumulate they overlap like hadd punishments. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he is pursued for it because it is a liability in his obligation, so it does not fall off by delay like zakah in the case of a Muslim, and the three (imams) said the same. (al-'ismah) And kharaj of land: it was said that this difference applies, and it was said that there is no overlap in it by agreement. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/439] (Mukhtasar) 'And death': i.e., jizya falls off by the death of the dhimmi also, even if after the passage of the year. (Tahawi)
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq deals with two sets of rulings: (1) who is exempt from paying jizya, and (2) when jizya falls off after being owed. The author begins by listing four categories who do not pay: the chronically ill (zamin), the blind (a'ma), the poor who cannot earn (faqir ghayr mu'tamil), and the monk who does not mix with people (rahib la yukhalituhum). The commentary adds conditions: a monk who mixes must pay jizya by consensus; a poor person who later becomes wealthy becomes liable. Additionally, if a child reaches puberty, insane recovers, slave freed, or sick recovers before the imam places jizya, they are liable; after placement, they are not. The second part discusses when jizya falls off. First, if the dhimmi embraces Islam after the year ends, jizya drops by the hadith 'Whoever embraces Islam, there is no jizya upon him.' The commentary counters Shafi'i and Malik, who argued jizya is a debt that remains. Second, jizya falls off by repetition (takarrur): non-collection for two or more years, per Abu Hanifa, as punishments overlap. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree, likening it to zakah. Third, jizya falls off by the dhimmi's death, even after the year. The text also notes a difference for kharaj.

Key Terms
الجزية (al-jizyah): The poll tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
زمن (zaman): A person with a chronic, incurable illness that prevents participation in fighting.
تكرار (takarrur): Non-collection of jizya for multiple years; according to Abu Hanifa, this results in the jizya falling off due to overlapping of punishments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He must pay immediately
B) He is exempt for that year but will be liable next year
C) He pays nothing ever
D) He pays half

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exempts the chronically ill, blind, poor non-earners, and secluded monks from jizya, and changes in status before or after placement determine liability for that year.

Falling Off of Jizya: When Obligation Ceases
Rulings on falling off of jizya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain when jizya falls off according to the Hanafi school and evaluate the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disputes.

Core Idea
Jizya, being a punishment for disbelief, falls off by Islam, death, and (per Abu Hanifa) non-collection for two years.

This part of the passage addresses the circumstances that terminate the jizya obligation. The Hanafi school holds that jizya drops by the dhimmi's conversion to Islam, his death, and by the non-collection of jizya for two or more years (Abu Hanifa's view). These rulings are supported by the hadith 'Whoever embraces Islam, there is no jizya upon him' and by analogical reasoning. There are significant ikhtilafat with the other schools and within the Hanafi school itself.

Guided Path
1
State the three ways jizya falls off
The text lists: Islam, takarrur (repetition/non-collection), and death. Commit these to memory.
The order in the matn is: 'tasqutu bi al-islam, wa al-takarrur, wa al-mawt'.
2
Analyze the proof for falling off by Islam
The author cites the hadith: 'Whoever embraces Islam, there is no jizya upon him.' The Hanafi rationale: jizya is a punishment for kufr; once kufr ceases, the punishment ceases.
This hadith is the primary proof (dalil naqli).
3
Contrast with the Shafi'i/Maliki objection
Shafi'i and Malik consider jizya a debt (dayn) for protection and residence already received. They argue it does not drop by conversion or death.
The Hanafi response: jizya is a punishment (uqubah) or substitute for support (nasrah), not a debt.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on takarrur
Abu Hanifa holds that if jizya is not collected for two or more years, it drops because punishments overlap (tadakhul). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it does not drop, analogizing to zakah.
The text states: 'Qala yutalabu biha' (he is pursued for it).

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq deals with two sets of rulings: (1) who is exempt from paying jizya, and (2) when jizya falls off after being owed. The author begins by listing four categories who do not pay: the chronically ill (zamin), the blind (a'ma), the poor who cannot earn (faqir ghayr mu'tamil), and the monk who does not mix with people (rahib la yukhalituhum). Additionally, if a child reaches puberty, insane recovers, slave freed, or sick recovers before the imam places jizya, they are liable; after placement, they are not. The second part discusses when jizya falls off. First, if the dhimmi embraces Islam after the year ends, jizya drops by the hadith 'Whoever embraces Islam, there is no jizya upon him.' The commentary counters Shafi'i and Malik, who argued jizya is a debt that remains. Key Terms
الجزية (al-jizyah): The poll tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
تكرار (takarrur): Non-collection of jizya for multiple years; according to Abu Hanifa, this results in the jizya falling off due to overlapping of punishments.
حد (hadd): Fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Islamic law for certain crimes.

A) After one year of non-collection

Key Takeaway
Jizya falls off by conversion to Islam, death, and (in Abu Hanifa's view) non-collection for two years, but the mufta bihi on takarrur is the Sahibayn view that the debt remains.

Prohibition of Building New Churches in Dar al-Islam
Prohibition of new churches in Dar al-Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on building new churches in Dar al-Islam and identify the primary proof (hadith) used.

Core Idea
No new non-Muslim places of worship may be established in Islamic territory.

This lesson addresses a key aspect of the relationship between Muslims and dhimmis: the prohibition of constructing new places of worship for non-Muslims in Dar al-Islam. The Hanafi school relies on a specific hadith to establish this ruling, and we will examine its proof and implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon and what the hukm (legal classification) is. The act is 'building a new church (or synagogue) in Dar al-Islam' and the ruling is prohibition.
The term 'bi'ah' refers to churches, and 'kanisah' to synagogues, though usage overlaps.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited for the ruling. Here, the hadith: 'La ikhsa' fil islam wa la kanisah' (There is no castration in Islam and no church).
The hadith is used as evidence for the prohibition of new churches.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the hadith proves the prohibition. The phrase 'la kanisah' is interpreted as 'there shall be no (building of) churches', indicating a general prohibition.
The prohibition extends to fire temples (bayt al-nar) and monasteries (sawma'ah) by analogy.
4
Note the scope and exceptions
Understand that the prohibition applies to new constructions. Moving an existing church from one place to another is considered new construction. However, old buildings that collapse naturally may be rebuilt.
The exception for repair is covered in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تحدث بيعة . وكنيسة في دارنا، ويعاد المنهدم.
ولا تحدث الإحداث: إيجاد شيء لم يكن من قبل، والبيعة اسم لمعبد النصارى واليهود وكذا الكنيسة إلا أن استعمال البيعة لمعبد النصارى أغلب، واستعمال الكنيسة لمعبد اليهود أغلب والمعنى أن إحداث البيعة والكنيسة لا يجوز في دار الإسلام؛ لقوله عليه: لا إخصاء في الإسلام ولا كنيسة، والمراد لا تحدث في دار الإسلام كنيسة لم تكن فإن أحدثوها يجب على أهل الإسلام أن يمنعوها والخصاء بالكسر والمد نزع الخصية، وقيل: المراد به الامتناع من النساء حتى يصير في حكم الخصي، وكذا لا يحدث بيت النار، ولا الصومعة وهي بيت التخلي تبنى برأس كبير؛ ليتعبد فيها بالانقطاع عن الناس. ومن الإحداث نقلها من مكان إلى آخر؛ لأنه إحداث في ذلك الموضع، ويمنعون من بيع الخمر والخنزير، =
وكنيسة في دارنا، ويعاد المنهدم. ويميز الذمّي عنا في الزي والمركب والسرج، أي عن المسلمين أي وفي المركب لأنهم من أهل الإهانة من هي كثير. وضرب الناقوس خارج الكنيسة، والناقوس لهم كالأذان لنا، فيقطع به إظهار الشرك، وقوله: "في دارنا" أي في دار الإسلام مطلقا لا في الأمصار، ولا في القرى.(مستخلص، فتح، عيني) في دارنا: أي في دار الإسلام أي لا تبنيان ابتداء إن لم يكونا فيها (محشي) ويعاد المنهدم: [ أي ما انهدم بنفسه الكنائس والبيع القديمة لا ما هدمه الإمام، ويعاد من غير زيادة على البناء الأول (عيني)] أي لو الهدمت البيع والكنائس القديمة لا يمنع من إعادتها؛ لأن التوارث من لدن رسول الله له إلى يومنا هذا بترك البيع والكنائس في دار الإسلام، فهذا دليل جواز الإعادة؛ لأن البيعة لا تبقي دائمة إلا أنه يمنع من الزيادة على البناء الأول، وعند أحمد: لا يعاد المنهدم أيضاً، وقيل: هذا في الأمصار دون القرى في غير جزيرة العرب، أما فيها فيمنعون من قراها أيضاً لخبر "لا يجتمع دينان في جزيرة العرب" ويمنعون في الأمصار؛ لأنها التي تقام فيها شعائر الإسلام ولا يمنعون من ذلك في قرية لا يقام فيها الجمع والحدود وإن كان فيها عدد وقيل: يمنعون في كل موضع لم تشع فيه شعائرهم، والمروي عن أبي حنيفة كان في قرى الكوفة؛ لأن أكثر أهلها أهل الذمة، وفي أرض العرب يمنعون من ذلك كله، ومن إدخال الخمر والخنازير فيها، ويمنعون من المشركين مسكناً؛ لما روي عن ابن عباس لما أنه عليه قال في مرضه الذي مات فيه: "أخرجوا المشركين من جزيرة العرب"، رواه البخاري ومسلم [رمز الحقائق: ٤٣٩/١] (فتح)
And no new church (is built). And a church in our territory, and the demolished is rebuilt. [Commentary: "And no new church" - i.e., initiation of something that did not exist before. 'Bi'ah' is the name for the place of worship of Christians and Jews, and similarly 'kanisah', except that 'bi'ah' is more commonly used for Christian worship and 'kanisah' for Jewish worship. The meaning: initiating a new church or synagogue is not permitted in Dar al-Islam because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'There is no castration in Islam and no church.' The intended meaning is that a church that did not exist cannot be built in Dar al-Islam; if they build one, the Muslims must prevent it. 'Castration' refers to removal of testicles, and it is also said to mean abstaining from women to become like a eunuch. Similarly, no fire temple may be built, nor a monastery (sawma'ah), which is a place of seclusion built on a high hill. And moving a church from one place to another is considered initiation. And they (the dhimmis) are prevented from selling wine and pigs. And a church in our territory, and the demolished is rebuilt. And the dhimmi is distinguished from us in dress, mount, and saddle. i.e., from Muslims. And the mount: because they are people of humiliation. And striking the bell (naqus) outside the church; the bell is like the adhan for us, and by it they manifest polytheism. And his statement 'in our territory' means in Dar al-Islam absolutely, not in cities nor in villages. (Mukhtasar, Fath, 'Ayni) 'In our territory': i.e., in Dar al-Islam, meaning they are not to be built initially if they are not already there (Hashiyah). 'And the demolished is rebuilt': i.e., what collapses by itself of the old churches and synagogues, not what the Imam demolishes; and it is rebuilt without increasing upon the original construction. (Ayni) i.e., if the old churches and synagogues collapse, they may be rebuilt because of continuous practice from the time of the Messenger (peace be upon him) until today, by leaving the churches and synagogues in Dar al-Islam. This is proof of the permissibility of rebuilding, because the church does not remain permanently, but increasing upon the original construction is prevented. According to Ahmad, the collapsed is also not rebuilt. And it is said that this ruling applies to cities, not villages outside the Arabian Peninsula. In the Arabian Peninsula, they are also prevented from villages because of the hadith 'Two religions shall not coexist in the Arabian Peninsula.' And they are prevented in cities because that is where the symbols of Islam are established, but they are not prevented in a village where congregational prayer and hadd penalties are not established. And it is said that they are prevented wherever their symbols have not become widespread. The narration from Abu Hanifa was about the villages of Kufa because most of its inhabitants were dhimmis. In the land of the Arabs, they are prevented from all of that, and from bringing wine and pigs into it, and they are prevented from the mushriks dwelling there, based on what Ibn Abbas narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said in his illness from which he died: 'Expel the mushriks from the Arabian Peninsula,' narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/439] (Fath)
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on churches and synagogues in Dar al-Islam. The matn states two points: no new church may be built ('la tuhdath bi'ah'), and a collapsed one may be rebuilt ('yu'adu al-munhadam'). The commentary elaborates: 'bi'ah' refers to places of worship for Christians (primarily) and Jews. New construction is prohibited by the hadith 'La ikhsa' fil islam wa la kanisah' (there is no castration in Islam and no church). The hadith is interpreted to ban new churches. Similarly, fire temples and monasteries are prohibited. Moving a church constitutes new construction. On the positive side, old buildings that collapse naturally may be rebuilt, but without any expansion. Imam Ahmad held even that is disallowed. There is a distinction between cities and villages outside the Arabian Peninsula: in cities, new churches are prohibited but old ones may be repaired; in villages, it depends on whether the symbols of Islam are established. In the Arabian Peninsula, all non-Muslim worship places are prohibited, based on the hadith 'Expel the mushriks from the Jazirat al-'Arab.' The passage also mentions that dhimmis must not strike bells loudly or manifest their religion. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi school's view that Dar al-Islam is the land where Islam is dominant, and dhimmis may retain their existing places of worship but not expand them.

Key Terms
بيعة (bi'ah): Place of worship for Christians, sometimes used for Jews; equivalent to kanisah.
إحداث (ihdath): Creating something new; here specifically building a new church or moving one.
كنيسة (kanisah): Place of worship for Jews, sometimes used for Christians.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on building a new church in Dar al-Islam?
A) It is permissible if the local Muslims agree
B) It is prohibited, and if built, must be prevented
C) It is permissible only for existing communities
D) It is encouraged as a sign of tolerance

Key Takeaway
Building new non-Muslim places of worship in Dar al-Islam is prohibited based on the hadith 'La ikhsa' fil islam wa la kanisah'.

Repair of Old Churches in Dar al-Islam
Permission to repair collapsed churches in Dar al-Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on rebuilding collapsed churches and distinguish it from the Hanbali position.

Core Idea
Naturally collapsed old churches may be rebuilt without expansion, based on continuous practice.

While new churches cannot be built, the Hanafi school permits the repair of old churches that collapse naturally. This lesson explores the reasoning behind this allowance, the conditions, and the disagreement with Imam Ahmad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'repairing an old church that has collapsed due to natural causes'. The ruling is that it is permissible to rebuild it exactly as it was.
The text says 'yu'adu al-munhadam' (the demolished is rebuilt), referring to natural collapse.
2
Understand the condition of no expansion
The rebuilding must be without any increase (ziyada) on the original construction. Only the exact dimensions and features are allowed.
This prevents any expansion of non-Muslim presence.
3
Examine the proof: continuous practice (tawarruth)
The proof for permissibility is the continuous practice from the time of the Prophet until the present day: churches have always existed in Dar al-Islam, and when they collapsed, they were rebuilt.
This is a form of tacit approval by the community.
4
Analyze the Hanbali opposition
Imam Ahmad holds that collapsed churches should not be rebuilt at all, as he considers all remnants of kufr to be removed.
The Hanafi response is that rebuilding does not create new kufr; it merely restores what existed.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi view is the operative position due to the established practice and the difficulty of eliminating all old places of worship.
This is based on the principle of 'tawarruth' (inherited practice).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بيعة (bi'ah): Place of worship for Christians.
المنهدم (al-munhadam): A building that collapses naturally (not demolished by the Imam).
توارث (tawarruth): Continuous practice inherited from generation to generation; used as evidence for permissibility.
