The Obligation of Distinguishing Dhimmis in Appearance
Rulings on differentiating dhimmis from Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rules requiring dhimmis to be distinguished from Muslims in dress, mount, and saddle, and explain the historical basis and wisdom behind these rules.

Core Idea
Dhimmis must be visibly distinct in appearance to manifest the honor of Islam and the humility of those under its protection.

In a society where Muslims and non-Muslims lived together under Islamic rule, early jurists established rules to maintain clear communal identities. The Hanafi school, based on the practice of the Caliph 'Umar, mandated that dhimmis adopt distinguishing marks in clothing, riding, and accessories. This lesson unpacks the specific requirements and their underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being required? The text says 'yu'khadh al-dhimmi bi al-tamayyuz' — the dhimmi is taken to task to be distinguished. This is a legal obligation (wajib) on the authority to enforce and on the dhimmi to comply.
The ruling is not from a primary text but from the practice of the Companions.
2
List the specific requirements
According to the matn and commentary, the dhimmi must: (1) wear distinct clothing (zayy) unlike Muslims, (2) not ride horses (except necessity) and use humble saddles, (3) display the kustij (thick belt), (4) not carry weapons.
These are all means of distinction to show the difference in status.
3
Understand the historical justification
Why did the Prophet not enforce these? Because dhimmis were few and well-known in Medina. In 'Umar's time, intermingling increased, so the need arose. The Companions agreed, giving it the force of consensus.
This shows that the ruling is based on maslaha (public interest) and is flexible in application.
4
Recognize the legal wisdom (hikma)
The underlying reason is that dhimmis are ahl al-ihanah (people of humiliation) and Muslims are ahl al-i'zaz (people of honor). Distinction manifests this hierarchy, which is part of the dhimma contract.
This wisdom is explicitly mentioned in the commentary.
5
Apply to a scenario
A dhimmi in a Hanafi city wears identical clothing to Muslim judges. What should happen? He must be forced to change and wear the kustij, as per the ruling.
The enforcement is the duty of the Muslim authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويميز الذمّي عنا في الزي والمركب والسرج، أي عن المسلمين أي وفي المركب لأنهم من أهل الإهانة من هي كثير. وضرب الناقوس خارج الكنيسة، والناقوس لهم كالأذان لنا، فيقطع به إظهار الشرك، وقوله: "في دارنا" أي في دار الإسلام مطلقا لا في الأمصار، ولا في القرى.
(مستخلص، فتح، عيني) في دارنا: أي في دار الإسلام أي لا تبنيان ابتداء إن لم يكونا فيها (محشي) ويعاد المنهدم: [ أي ما انهدم بنفسه الكنائس والبيع القديمة لا ما هدمه الإمام، ويعاد من غير زيادة على البناء الأول (عيني)] أي لو الهدمت البيع والكنائس القديمة لا يمنع من إعادتها؛ لأن التوارث من لدن رسول الله له إلى يومنا هذا بترك البيع والكنائس في دار الإسلام، فهذا دليل جواز الإعادة؛ لأن البيعة لا تبقي دائمة إلا أنه يمنع من الزيادة على البناء الأول، وعند أحمد: لا يعاد المنهدم أيضاً، وقيل: هذا في الأمصار دون القرى في غير جزيرة العرب، أما فيها فيمنعون من قراها أيضاً لخبر "لا يجتمع دينان في جزيرة العرب" ويمنعون في الأمصار؛ لأنها التي تقام فيها شعائر الإسلام ولا يمنعون من ذلك في قرية لا يقام فيها الجمع والحدود وإن كان فيها عدد وقيل: يمنعون في كل موضع لم تشع فيه شعائرهم، والمروي عن أبي حنيفة كان في قرى الكوفة؛ لأن أكثر أهلها أهل الذمة، وفي أرض العرب يمنعون من ذلك كله، ومن إدخال الخمر والخنازير فيها، ويمنعون من المشركين مسكناً؛ لما روي عن ابن عباس لما أنه عليه قال في مرضه الذي مات فيه: "أخرجوا المشركين من جزيرة العرب"، رواه البخاري ومسلم [رمز الحقائق: ٤٣٩/١] (فتح) ويميز الذمّي عنا في الزّي: قال النووي في شرح مسلم": الزي بفتح الزاء وكسرها وتشديد الياء، الهيئة واللباس أي يؤخذ الذمّي بالتميز عن معشر المسلمين في اللباس والكسوة، ويمنعون عن لباس يختص بأهل العلم والشرف، وكذا يؤاخذون في المركب بأن يمنعوا من ركوب الخيل، وكذا في السروج بأن يركبوا سرجاً كهيئة الأكف إذا ركبوا حماراً أو بغلاً، أو ركبوا خيلاً للضرورة، وكذا يمنعون عن استعمال السلاح، ويؤخذ بإظهار الكستيج بضم الكاف وسكون السين المهملة وكسر التاء الفوقية.
فإن قيل: لم يأخذ النبي عليه أفضل الصلاة والسلام يهود المدينة ولا نصارى نجران ولا مجوس هجر بذلك فكيف يؤخذ الذمي بهذه؟ قلنا: إنهم في زمن رسول الله كانوا معروفين في المدينة لا يشتبه حالهم فلم يقع الاحتياج إلى ذلك ثم في زمن عمر لما كثر في الناس من يعرف ومن لا يعرف وقعت الحاجة إلى ذلك، فأمر بذلك بمحضر من الصحابة وكانوا يرونه صوابا ولأنهم من أهل الإهانة والمسلمون من أهل الإعزاز والكرامة فوجب التميز إظهاراً للتفاوت بينهما، و"الكستيج" الخيط الغليظ الذي يشدون به أوساطهم، وعن أبي يوسف هو الخيط الغليظ بقدر الإصبع يشدّه الذمي فوق ثيابه دون ما يتميز به من الزنانير المتخذة عن الإبريسم، وقال فخر الإسلام الكستيجات هي علامات الكفر، وهي فارسية معربة وحقيقته العجز والذل بلغة العجم.
And the dhimmi is distinguished from us in dress, mount, and saddle: i.e., from Muslims. And the mount: because they are people of humiliation. And striking the bell (naqus) outside the church; the bell is like the adhan for us, and by it they manifest polytheism. And his statement 'in our territory' means in Dar al-Islam absolutely, not in cities nor in villages. (Mukhtasar, Fath, 'Ayni) 'In our territory': i.e., in Dar al-Islam, meaning they are not to be built initially if they are not already there (Hashiyah). 'And the demolished is rebuilt': i.e., what collapses by itself of the old churches and synagogues, not what the Imam demolishes; and it is rebuilt without increasing upon the original construction. (Ayni) i.e., if the old churches and synagogues collapse, they may be rebuilt because of continuous practice from the time of the Messenger (peace be upon him) until today, by leaving the churches and synagogues in Dar al-Islam. This is proof of the permissibility of rebuilding, because the church does not remain permanently, but increasing upon the original construction is prevented. According to Ahmad, the collapsed is also not rebuilt. And it is said that this ruling applies to cities, not villages outside the Arabian Peninsula. In the Arabian Peninsula, they are also prevented from villages because of the hadith 'Two religions shall not coexist in the Arabian Peninsula.' And they are prevented in cities because that is where the symbols of Islam are established, but they are not prevented in a village where congregational prayer and hadd penalties are not established. And it is said that they are prevented wherever their symbols have not become widespread. The narration from Abu Hanifa was about the villages of Kufa because most of its inhabitants were dhimmis. In the land of the Arabs, they are prevented from all of that, and from bringing wine and pigs into it, and they are prevented from the mushriks dwelling there, based on what Ibn Abbas narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said in his illness from which he died: 'Expel the mushriks from the Arabian Peninsula,' narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 1/439] (Fath) And the dhimmi is distinguished from us in dress: al-Nawawi said in Sharh Muslim: 'al-zayy' with fath the za' and kasr and tashdid the ya', means appearance and clothing. i.e., the dhimmi is taken to task to be distinguished from the group of Muslims in clothing and attire, and they are prevented from wearing clothes specific to scholars and nobility. Similarly, they are restricted in mount, such that they are prevented from riding horses, and similarly in saddles, such that they ride on saddles resembling packs, if they ride a donkey or mule, or if they ride a horse out of necessity. Likewise, they are prevented from using weapons, and they are required to display the kustij (belt). If it is said: why did the Prophet (peace be upon him) not enforce this upon the Jews of Medina, Christians of Najran, or Magians of Hajar? We reply: In the time of the Prophet, they were well-known in Medina so no need arose. Then in the time of 'Umar, as the population grew, necessity arose, so he ordered it in the presence of the Companions, and they considered it correct. And because they are people of humiliation, and Muslims are people of honor and dignity, so distinction became obligatory to manifest the difference between them. 'Kustij' is a thick thread that they tie around their waists. According to Abu Yusuf, it is a thick thread the size of a finger that the dhimmi ties over his clothes, distinguishing him from the silk belts. Fakhr al-Islam said the kustij are signs of disbelief; they are a Persian word arabized, meaning in their language weakness and humiliation.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage addresses the requirement for dhimmis to be externally distinguishable from Muslims. The matn says 'yu'khadh al-dhimmi bi al-tamayyuz 'anna fi al-zayy wa al-markab wa al-sarj' (the dhimmi is taken to be distinguished from us in dress, mount, and saddle). The commentators explain: they must wear distinct clothing, not like Muslim scholars or nobles; they must not ride horses (except by necessity) and must use humble saddles; they must not carry weapons; they must display the kustij (a thick belt or cord). The commentary answers an objection: why did the Prophet not enforce these rules? Because in his time, the dhimmis were few and known; later, when Muslims and dhimmis intermingled more, 'Umar instituted these rules with the Companions' consent. The reasoning is that dhimmis are people of humiliation (ahl al-ihanah) and Muslims of honor (ahl al-i'zaz), so distinction manifests this. The kustij is a symbol of submission.

Key Terms
الكستيج (al-kustij): A thick belt or cord worn by dhimmis as a distinguishing mark, often worn over clothes.
الزي (al-zayy): Appearance, dress, or uniform; here specifically the dress code imposed on dhimmis.
الناقوس (al-naqus): A wooden clapper or bell used by Christians to announce prayer times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Prophet (pbuh) not enforce distinguishing marks on dhimmis during his lifetime?
A) Because the rule was not yet revealed
B) Because the dhimmis were few and well-known, so no need arose
C) Because he was lenient with non-Muslims
D) Because the dhimmis refused to comply

Key Takeaway
The requirement for dhimmis to be distinguished in dress and mount is a legal obligation rooted in the dhimma contract, aimed at preserving the honor of Islam and the humility of those under its protection.

Restrictions on Dhimmis and the Inviolability of Their Covenant
Lists restrictions and four actions that do not break the dhimmi covenant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the four actions that do not break the dhimmi covenant and distinguish the Hanafi view from opposing schools, citing the dalil from the hadith of the Jewish man.

Core Idea
Four grave actions do not break the dhimmi covenant; only joining the enemy annuls it.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the Hanafi ruling on the inviolability of the dhimmi pact. While dhimmis are subject to certain restrictions to distinguish them from Muslims, their covenant remains intact even if they commit severe offenses like refusing jizya, zina, murder, or insulting the Prophet (saw). This lesson explores the evidence and the inter-madhhab dispute on this issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Recognize the four specific actions that are questioned regarding their effect on the dhimmi covenant: (1) refusing to pay jizya, (2) zina with a Muslim woman, (3) killing a Muslim, (4) insulting the Prophet (saw). The central question is whether any of these break the pact.
This is a dispute about the scope of dhimma.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
According to the Hanafi school, none of these four actions break the covenant. The pact remains intact, and the dhimmi continues to enjoy protection. Only explicit acts of declaring war or joining the enemy annul the covenant.
This is the position in Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
For insulting the Prophet, the Hanafi rely on the hadith where a Jewish man said 'al-sam alaykum' (death be upon you) and the Prophet (saw) did not take action against him. For refusing jizya, the reasoning is that the pact is based on the commitment to pay, not actual payment; it becomes a debt that can be enforced like other debts. For murder and zina, no explicit text breaks the covenant; they are sins but do not indicate enmity that severs the pact.
The hadith is recorded by Bukhari and Ahmad.
4
Analyze the opposing view
Scholars from other schools (e.g., Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) hold that some or all of these actions break the covenant. Their evidence: insulting the Prophet violates the aman (safe conduct) and is tantamount to treacherous behavior; killing a Muslim is a major violation that nullifies the pact from the victim's side.
Opponents argue that the dhimmi's actions demonstrate hostility.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: If a dhimmi commits one of these acts, under the Hanafi view he remains protected and is subject to the ordinary legal punishments (e.g., qisas for murder, hadd for zina). Under opposing views, his pact is void, making him liable to death or loss of protection and expulsion.
The Hanafi position offers stability in interfaith relations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الفتوى من
وقتل مسلم: أي ولا ينتقض أيضاً بقتله مسلماً. (عيني) وسب النبي : أي ولا ينقض أيضاً بسبه عليها إذا لم يعلن أما إذا أعلن واعتاده فالحق أنه يقتل. (ط، عيني)
Chapter of Siyar and Jihad. Rulings of Jizya. He (the dhimmi) does not ride horses, does not carry weapons, reveals the waistbelt, rides a saddle like a packsaddle. And his covenant is not broken by refusing to pay jizya, by committing zina with a Muslim woman, by killing a Muslim, or by insulting the Prophet, peace be upon him.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq's commentary first lists restrictions on dhimmis: they must not ride horses (only mules or donkeys), not carry weapons, wear a distinctive belt, and use a packsaddle (akaf) instead of a proper saddle (saraj) except in necessity. They must not dress like Muslims, distinguish their women with bells, mark their houses, refrain from initiating salam, and walk in narrow streets. Then it addresses the inviolability of the dhimmi covenant: four major violations do not break the contract. Refusal to pay jizya does not break it because the pact is based on the commitment to pay, not actual payment; it becomes a debt. Zina with a Muslim woman does not break it according to Hanafis, unlike Ahmad and Ibn Qasim al-Maliki. Killing a Muslim does not break it, contrary to the three (Abu Hanifa's students? Actually 'al-thalatha' refers to the other three imams?). Insulting the Prophet (saw) does not break it based on the hadith where a Jew said 'al-sam alaykum' and the Prophet did not kill him. The Shafi'i and others argue it should break because insult breaks faith, but the Hanafi response is that the covenant is not broken by such acts; only joining the enemy or overpowering a place breaks it. The commentary also includes a lengthy quote from al-Shifa defining sabb and its ruling of execution without repentance.

Key Terms
الذمي (al-dhimmi): A non-Muslim living under Muslim protection with a pact (dhimma).
الجزية (al-jizyah): A per capita tax imposed on dhimmis in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
انتقض العهد (intaqada al-'ahd): The dissolution or invalidation of the protection pact between Muslims and dhimmis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following actions breaks the covenant of a dhimmi?
A) Refusing to pay jizya
B) Killing a Muslim
C) Joining the enemy in dar al-harb
D) Insulting the Prophet (saw)

Key Takeaway
The dhimmi covenant is remarkably durable: only open combatancy breaks it, not individual sins.

What Breaks the Dhimmi's Covenant: Joining Dar al-Harb or Overpowering
States the two actions that invalidate the dhimmi pact and compares to apostasy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two actions that invalidate the dhimmi's covenant according to the Hanafi school, explain the analogy to apostasy, and distinguish the Hanafi position from other madhhabs.

Core Idea
The dhimmi's covenant is only voided by active combat: joining dar al-harb or overpowering a place to fight.

The dhimmi enjoys protected status in Islamic law, but that protection is not absolute. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies the precise actions that break the covenant according to the Hanafi school. Understanding these limits is crucial for applying the rules of warfare and the treatment of non-Muslim residents. The text also draws a careful analogy to apostasy, highlighting both similarities and crucial differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two invalidating actions
Read the matn: 'بل باللحاق تمه، أو بالغلبة على موضع للحراب'. Determine what each action entails: al-lihaq (joining dar al-harb) and al-ghalabah (overpowering a place to fight).
Spying is also included by analogy.
2
Understand the logic of combatancy
The commentary explains that these actions make the dhimmi a harbi (combatant) against Muslims. Focus on the phrase 'صاروا بذلك حرباً علينا' – the key is active hostility.
3
Analyze the qiyas to the apostate
The text says 'وصار كالمرتد'. Identify the illa (effective cause): both sever ties with Muslims and join the enemy. Note that the analogy is partial.
The commentary lists three specific differences: killing vs. enslavement, forced acceptance vs. no force, and wealth treatment.
4
Derive the distinctive Hanafi rulings
From the qiyas and its limitations, extract the Hanafi position: captured dhimmi is enslaved (not killed), not forced to accept dhimma, and his wealth becomes fay' for the state.
Contrast with other schools that treat the dhimmi more like an apostate.
5
Compare with other madhhabs
The passage cites Malik (kill and enslave), Shafi'i and Ahmad (choice). Note the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) in the treatment of captured dhimmis.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf rooted in different analogical reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بل باللحاق تمه، أو بالغلبة على موضع للحراب، وصار كالمرتة.
أي بل ينقض عهده عندنا أي بدار الحرب
بعد اللحوق والغلبة
بل باللحاق ثمه إلخ أي ينقض عهد الذميين بلحوق دار الحرب أو أن يغلبوا على موضع ليحاربوننا؛ لأنهم صاروا بذلك حرباً علينا، وكذا لو جعل الذمي نفسه طليعة للمشركين أي المبعوث منهم ليطلع على أخبار العدو، وقوله: "وصار "كالمرتد أي في هذين الوجهين؛ لأنه التحق بالأموات بتباين الدارين غير أن الذمي إذا أسر يسترق، بخلاف المرتد فإنه يقتل ولا يجبر الذمي الأسير على قبول الذمة، بخلاف المرتد فإنه يجبر على الإسلام، والمال الذي لحق الذمي به دار الحرب يكون فيئاً، وليس لورثته أن يأخذوه كالمرتد، وقال مالك: إذا ظفر بهم الإمام على دار الحرب يقتلهم ويسبيهم، وعند الشافعي وأحمد يخير بين الاسترقاق والقتل. رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٠/١] (فتح) للحراب لأنهم صاروا بذلك حرباً علينا. (عيني) كالمرتد في حل قتله ودفع ماله لورثته. (عيني)
Rather, it is broken by joining them, or by overpowering a place to fight, and he becomes like an apostate.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage explains what actually breaks the dhimmi's covenant according to the Hanafi school. Two actions invalidate the pact: (1) joining dar al-harb (the abode of war) by relocating there, and (2) overpowering a Muslim territory to fight against Muslims. In both cases, the dhimmi becomes a combatant (harbi). The text draws an analogy to an apostate (murtadd) in terms of killing being permissible and his wealth becoming fay' (spoils) for the Muslim state. However, there are differences: a captured dhimmi is not killed but enslaved, whereas the apostate is killed; the dhimmi is not forced to return to dhimma, while the apostate is forced to accept Islam. The commentary also mentions that if a dhimmi acts as a spy by informing the enemy, it is similar. It notes the positions of Malik (who kills and enslaves) and Shafi'i and Ahmad (who give the imam a choice between enslavement and execution).

Key Terms
اللحاق (al-lihaq): Joining the enemy camp physically by relocating to dar al-harb.
الغلبة (al-ghalabah): Overpowering a territory to fight against Muslims, thus becoming a harbi.
المرتد (al-murtadd): One who renounces Islam; used here for analogy in terms of being a combatant.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule where fighting is permitted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to a dhimmi who joins dar al-harb?
A) His covenant is broken and he becomes a combatant, his wealth is fay'
B) His covenant is broken and he is killed immediately
C) His family is also punished
D) He is given a chance to return

Key Takeaway
Only active participation in warfare—by physically joining dar al-harb or overpowering a territory—invalidates the dhimmi's pact, and even then the dhimmi is not killed like an apostate.

Taxation of Bani Taghlib and the Status of Their Freed Slaves
Details the jizya rate for Christian Arab tribe Taghlib and the ruling on their freed slaves.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the tax paid by Bani Taghlib, explain why women are liable, and distinguish the treatment of their mawla.

Core Idea
The payment from Bani Taghlib follows zakat rules, not jizya conditions, due to the pact of Umar.

This passage addresses the unique situation of the Christian Arab tribe Bani Taghlib. Umar (ra) made a pact with them to pay double the zakat rate of Muslims rather than the standard jizya. This leads to specific rulings on who is liable—including women—and how the tax applies to their freed slaves (mawla). The text also discusses disagreements with other scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The tax for Bani Taghlib is double the Muslim zakat (half a tenth on wealth). The basis is Umar's pact with them.
This is not standard jizya; it follows zakat rules.
2
Understand the legal nature
Although Umar called it jizya, the pact specified 'double zakat', so the conditions of zakat apply, not the humiliating conditions of jizya.
Key point: the pact overrides default jizya rules.
3
Analyze the dispute on women
Hanafis: women are liable because zakat applies to women. Opponents (Zufar, Shafi‘i, Malik): women exempt because it is jizya in reality.
Hanafi proof: the pact agreed on double zakat, and zakat obligates women.
4
Examine the mawla ruling
The mawla (freed slave) of a Taghlibi pays normal jizya, not double. Zufar argued he should pay double, but Hanafis reject this.
The hadith 'the mawla of a people is from them' applies to lineage, not tax relief.
5
Note the objections and responses
Zufar's claim that the mawla should be treated like the patron is countered: following the patron would mean lighter burden, and the hadith does not extend to taxation.
Hanafis also point out that the mawla of a Muslim pays jizya, showing the mawla does not inherit the patron's tax status.

تغلبي: بكسر اللام نسبة إلى بني تغلب وهم قوم من نصارى العرب سكنوا بقرب الروم. (عيني) ضعف زكاتنا: [وهو نصف العشر؛ لأن الزكاة ربع العشر وضعف الربع نصف. (عيني)] أي يؤخذ من أموال تغلب ضعف ما يؤخذ من المسلمين في الزكاة وهو نصف العشر؛ لأن عمر له صالحهم على ضعف الزكاة بمحضر من الصحابة من غير نكير، وأشار إلى أن المأخوذ منهم وإن كان جزية لا يراعى فيه شرائطها من وصف الصغار، وتقبل من النائب بل يراعى شرائط الزكاة وأسبابها؛ لأن الصلح وقع كذلك. وعند زفر والشافعي ومالك لا يؤخذ من نسائهم؛ لأنه جزية في الحقيقة على ما قال عمر : هذه جزية فسموها كيف شئتم ولا جزية على النساء، ولنا أن عمر الله صالحهم على ضعف الزكاة، والزكاة تجب على النسوان فكذا ضعفها، وقيد بالبالغ ؛ لأنه لا يؤخذ من الصبي والصبية أي من مواشيهم وأموالهم بخلاف أراضيهم؛ لأن الزكاة لا تجب عليهم فكذا المضاعفة بخلاف المرأة فإنها أهل للوجوب، وعند أحمد: يؤخذ من المرأة ومن غير منهم أيضاً. [ رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٠/١] (فتح) ومولاه كمولى القرشي [ أي كمعتق القرشي في الجزية والخراج حتى يوضعان عليهما وإن كان التغلبي والقرشي لا يوضعان عليهما. (عيني)] أي إذا أعتق القرشي عبداً كافراً يؤخذ منه الجزية، ولا يعتبر حاله بحال مولاه معتق التغلبي يؤخذ منه الجزية إذا كان كافراً ولا يضاعف عليه، وقال زفر يضاعف على مولى التغلبي؛ لأنه ملحق بمولاه؛ لقوله عليه: "إن مولى القوم منهم. ولنا أنه لو ألحق بالمولى هنا كان تخفيفاً؛ إذ التضعيف أخف؛ لأنه ليس فيه وصف الذل والمولى المعتق لا يلحق بالأصل في التخفيف وورود الحديث على خلاف القياس في حرمة الصدقة، فلا يلحق به ما ليس بمعناه رمز الحقائق: ٤٤١/١]

ألا ترى أن الجزية توضع على مولى المسلم إذا كان كافراً ولو لحق في التخفيف لما وضع عليه بخلاف الصدقات؛ لأن الحرمان يثبت بالشبهات فألحق المولى بالهاشمي. (مستخلص، فتح)
And from a Taghlibi is taken double our zakat, and his mawla (freed slave) is like the mawla of a Qurashi.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage deals with the special case of Bani Taghlib, a Christian Arab tribe. Umar (ra) made a pact with them that they would pay double the zakat rate paid by Muslims (i.e., half a tenth instead of a quarter tenth). This payment is technically jizya but follows the rules of zakat: it is taken from their wealth like zakat, not with the humiliating conditions of jizya. There is a disagreement: Zufar, al-Shafi'i, and Malik say women are not liable because it is jizya and jizya is not on women. The Hanafi position, based on Umar's pact, is that since the payment is analogous to zakat, and zakat is due on women, double zakat is also due on them. The commentary also clarifies that children are exempt. Then it discusses the mawla (freed slave) of a Taghlibi: his mawla pays jizya at the normal rate (not double). Zufar argued that the mawla should pay double because he is attached to the Taghlibi, but the Hanafi position is that the mawla is not subject to double taxation because the concept of following the patron (mawla) in tax relief would mean lighter burden, and the hadith 'the mawla of a people is from them' applies in lineage not in tax treatment.

Key Terms
تغلبي (taghlabi): A member of the Christian Arab tribe Bani Taghlib.
ضعف الزكاة (di'f al-zakat): Double the standard zakat rate; for livestock and wealth it is half a tenth instead of a quarter tenth.
المولى (al-mawla): A freed slave; the patron-client relationship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only from adult males
B) From both adult males and females
C) Only from the wealthy
D) From all members including children

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the pact with Bani Taghlib made their payment follow zakat rules, so women are liable and the mawla pays normal jizya.

Breaking the Dhimmi Covenant: Conditions and Consequences
Conditions for dhimmī covenant breakage and comparison with apostate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two conditions that break a dhimmi's covenant according to the Hanafi school, and distinguish the Hanafi ruling from the treatment of apostates and from the positions of Mālik, al-Shāfiʿī, and Aḥmad.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's covenant is broken by joining dar al-ḥarb—he becomes a ḥarbī, enslaved if caught, not killed like an apostate.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school on the inviolable nature of the dhimmi covenant. While the covenant is strong, it is not absolute. The Hanafis define precise conditions under which it is nullified—and the consequences differ markedly from apostasy and from other madhāhib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for covenant breakage
According to the Hanafi school, two actions break the covenant: (1) the dhimmi joins dār al-ḥarb (the abode of war), or (2) they are overpowered in a place and become combatants against Muslims. Spying for the polytheists is also included.
The covenant is a contract; these acts are breach of contract.
2
Compare with the apostate (murtadd)
The text states the dhimmi becomes 'like an apostate' in certain respects: killing becomes permissible (though applied differently), and the wealth taken to dār al-ḥarb becomes fay' (booty for the treasury). However, key differences exist: the captured dhimmi is enslaved, not killed, and is not forced back into dhimma, unlike the apostate who is executed and forced to return to Islam.
The comparison is partial; the schools share some rulings but diverge in penalties.
3
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Mālik holds that the imam kills and enslaves the captured dhimmi. Al-Shāfiʿī and Aḥmad give the imam a choice between enslavement and execution. The Hanafi position restricts the penalty to enslavement only.
The thamarah al-khilāf (practical difference) is whether the dhimmi can be executed.
4
Apply to a hypothetical scenario
Consider a dhimmi who actively spies for the enemy. He is captured. Under the Hanafi school, his covenant is broken; he is enslaved, not killed, and his property becomes fay'. The imam may not force him back to dhimma.
This illustrates the consistent application of the principle that the covenant is contractual and breach leads to harbi status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بل باللحاق تمه، أو بالغلبة على موضع للحراب، وصار كالمرتة. أي بل ينقض عهده عندنا أي بدار الحرب بعد اللحوق والغلبة. بل باللحاق ثمه إلخ أي ينقض عهد الذميين بلحوق دار الحرب أو أن يغلبوا على موضع ليحاربوننا؛ لأنهم صاروا بذلك حرباً علينا، وكذا لو جعل الذمي نفسه طليعة للمشركين أي المبعوث منهم ليطلع على أخبار العدو، وقوله: "وصار كالمرتد" أي في هذين الوجهين؛ لأنه التحق بالأموات بتباين الدارين غير أن الذمي إذا أسر يسترق، بخلاف المرتد فإنه يقتل ولا يجبر الذمي الأسير على قبول الذمة، بخلاف المرتد فإنه يجبر على الإسلام، والمال الذي لحق الذمي به دار الحرب يكون فيئاً، وليس لورثته أن يأخذوه كالمرتد، وقال مالك: إذا ظفر بهم الإمام على دار الحرب يقتلهم ويسبيهم، وعند الشافعي وأحمد يخير بين الاسترقاق والقتل. (فتح) للحراب لأنهم صاروا بذلك حرباً علينا. (عيني) كالمرتد في حل قتله ودفع ماله لورثته.
Rather, by joining [dar al-harb] or by overpowering a place, he becomes like a warrior, and he becomes like an apostate. That is, his covenant is broken according to us, i.e., by [entering] dar al-harb after joining and being overpowered. 'Rather, by joining then' etc., meaning the covenant of dhimmis is broken by joining dar al-harb or by their being overpowered in a place so that they fight us, because they thereby become warriors against us. Similarly, if the dhimmi makes himself a spy for the polytheists, i.e., sent by them to learn news of the enemy. And his statement: 'and he becomes like an apostate' means in these two respects, because he has joined the dead by the separation of the two abodes, except that the dhimmi when captured is enslaved, unlike the apostate who is killed; and the captured dhimmi is not forced to accept dhimma, unlike the apostate who is forced to Islam. And the wealth that the dhimmi takes to dar al-harb becomes fay', and his heirs may not take it, like the apostate. Malik said: if the imam catches them in dar al-harb, he kills them and enslaves them. According to al-Shafi'i and Ahmad, he is given the choice between enslavement and killing. (Fath) 'to fight' because they have thereby become warriors against us. ('Ayni) 'like an apostate' in the permissibility of killing him and giving his wealth to his heirs.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage explains the conditions under which a dhimmi's covenant of protection is broken. According to the Hanafi school, if a dhimmi joins dar al-harb (the abode of war) or is overpowered by the enemy and becomes a combatant against Muslims, his covenant is nullified. He is then treated like a warrior (harbi) and, in specific rulings, like an apostate. However, differences exist: a captured dhimmi is enslaved, not killed, and is not forced back into dhimma, whereas an apostate is executed and forced to return to Islam. The wealth he takes to dar al-harb becomes fay' (booty for the public treasury), and his heirs have no claim—similar to an apostate. The passage also records the views of Imam Malik (who permits killing and enslaving) and al-Shafi'i and Ahmad (who grant the imam a choice between execution and enslavement). This illustrates the Hanafi distinction: the dhimmi's status changes due to hostile acts, but certain apostate-like consequences (death penalty, forced return) do not apply.

Key Terms
الذمة (al-dhimmah): The covenant of protection granted to non-Muslims living under Islamic rule.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): The abode of war, territory not under Muslim rule and with which no peace treaty exists.
المرتد (al-murtadd): A Muslim who abandons Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to a dhimmi who joins dar al-harb?
A) He is killed like an apostate.
B) He is enslaved if captured and not forced back to dhimma.
C) He is given the choice between Islam and death.
D) He is returned to his dhimma after the war.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a dhimmi's covenant breaks upon joining dar al-harb; the resultant status is that of a harbi, not an apostate, so enslavement applies instead of execution.

Jizyah from Banu Taghlib: Double Zakat as a Contractual Tax
Ruling on the tax for Christian Arabs of Banu Taghlib as double zakat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the tax imposed on Banu Taghlib and distinguish it from regular jizyah by analyzing the treaty of 'Umar and its implications for women and freed slaves.

Core Idea
The tax on Banu Taghlib is double zakat by treaty, so its rules follow zakat, not jizyah.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses a unique tax arrangement: the Christian Arab tribe Banu Taghlib pays double the standard zakat rate instead of the jizyah. The Hanafi school bases this on the peace treaty of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab, which imposed the tax with the consent of the Companions. This lesson examines the ruling, its conditions, and related disputes regarding women and freed slaves, emphasizing that the contractual nature overrides the label 'jizyah'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the tax and its basis
Recognize that Banu Taghlib pay double zakat (half a tenth on wealth) as per the treaty of 'Umar. Note that this rate is double the Muslim zakat rate of a quarter-tenth.
The text says 'weakf zakatina' i.e., double our zakat.
2
Distinguish from regular jizyah
Understand that although the tax replaces jizyah, its conditions (humiliation, direct payment) are not required; instead, zakat rules apply because the treaty specified 'double zakat'.
3
Analyze the dispute on women
Compare the Hanafi argument (zakat is obligatory on women, so double zakat applies) with the opposing view (it's jizyah, so no tax on women per 'Umar's statement).
Hanafis hold that adult women pay; opponents (Zufar, Shafi'i, Malik) exempt women.
4
Evaluate the mawla ruling
Examine whether the freed slave (mawla) of a Taghlibi pays the double tax or regular jizyah. Hanafis say regular jizyah (not doubled); Zufar argues it should be doubled because the mawla is attached to the master.
The hadith 'The mawla of a people is one of them' is used by Zufar, but Hanafis restrict it to sadaqah rulings.
5
Consolidate the principle
Conclude that the tax follows the contractual agreement (treaty terms), not the label. The ruling is based on the specific pact with Banu Taghlib and the Ijma of the Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويؤخذ من تغلبي ضعف زكاتنا ومولاه كمولى القرشي. تغلبي: بكسر اللام نسبة إلى بني تغلب وهم قوم من نصارى العرب سكنوا بقرب الروم. ضعف زكاتنا: وهو نصف العشر؛ لأن الزكاة ربع العشر وضعف الربع نصف. أي يؤخذ من أموال تغلب ضعف ما يؤخذ من المسلمين في الزكاة وهو نصف العشر؛ لأن عمر رضي الله عنه صالحهم على ضعف الزكاة بمحضر من الصحابة من غير نكير، وأشار إلى أن المأخوذ منهم وإن كان جزية لا يراعى فيه شرائطها من وصف الصغار، وتقبل من النائب بل يراعى شرائط الزكاة وأسبابها؛ لأن الصلح وقع كذلك. وعند زفر والشافعي ومالك لا يؤخذ من نسائهم؛ لأنه جزية في الحقيقة على ما قال عمر رضي الله عنه: هذه جزية فسموها كيف شئتم ولا جزية على النساء، ولنا أن عمر رضي الله عنه صالحهم على ضعف الزكاة، والزكاة تجب على النسوان فكذا ضعفها، وقيد بالبالغ؛ لأنه لا يؤخذ من الصبي والصبية أي من مواشيهم وأموالهم بخلاف أراضيهم؛ لأن الزكاة لا تجب عليهم فكذا المضاعفة بخلاف المرأة فإنها أهل للوجوب، وعند أحمد: يؤخذ من المرأة ومن غير منهم أيضاً. (فتح) ومولاه كمولى القرشي أي كمعتق القرشي في الجزية والخراج حتى يوضعان عليهما وإن كان التغلبي والقرشي لا يوضعان عليهما. أي إذا أعتق القرشي عبداً كافراً يؤخذ منه الجزية، ولا يعتبر حاله بحال مولاه معتق التغلبي يؤخذ منه الجزية إذا كان كافراً ولا يضاعف عليه، وقال زفر يضاعف على مولى التغلبي؛ لأنه ملحق بمولاه؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: "إن مولى القوم منهم". ولنا أنه لو ألحق بالمولى هنا كان تخفيفاً؛ إذ التضعيف أخف؛ لأنه ليس فيه وصف الذل والمولى المعتق لا يلحق بالأصل في التخفيف وورود الحديث على خلاف القياس في حرمة الصدقة، فلا يلحق به ما ليس بمعناه. ألا ترى أن الجزية توضع على مولى المسلم إذا كان كافراً ولو لحق في التخفيف لما وضع عليه بخلاف الصدقات؛ لأن الحرمان يثبت بالشبهات فألحق المولى بالهاشمي.
And from the Taghlibi is taken double our zakat, and his mawla is like the mawla of the Qurayshi. Taghlibi: with kasra on the lam, attribution to Banu Taghlib, a people of Arab Christians who lived near the Byzantines. Double our zakat: i.e., half a tenth, because zakat is a quarter of a tenth, and double a quarter is half. That is, from the wealth of Taghlib is taken double what is taken from Muslims in zakat, which is half a tenth, because 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, made a peace treaty with them for double zakat in the presence of the Companions without any objection. And it indicates that what is taken from them, even if it is jizyah in reality, its conditions (like the description of humiliation) are not observed, and it is accepted from the deputy; rather the conditions and causes of zakat are observed, because the peace treaty was concluded accordingly. According to Zufar, al-Shafi'i, and Malik, it is not taken from their women, because it is in reality jizyah, as 'Umar said: 'This is jizyah, call it what you wish, and there is no jizyah on women.' Our evidence: 'Umar made peace on double zakat, and zakat is obligatory on women, so likewise its double. And it is restricted to the adult because it is not taken from the child, male or female, i.e., from their livestock and wealth, unlike their lands, because zakat is not obligatory on them, so likewise the doubling; unlike the woman, who is fit for obligation. According to Ahmad, it is taken from the woman and from others as well. (Fath) 'And his mawla is like the mawla of the Qurayshi' i.e., like the freed slave of a Qurayshi regarding jizyah and kharaj, such that they are imposed on the mawla even though the Taghlibi and Qurayshi themselves are not subject to them. That is, if a Qurayshi frees a kafir slave, jizyah is taken from the slave; his situation is not considered by the situation of his master. Similarly, the mawla of a Taghlibi: jizyah is taken from him if he is a kafir, but it is not doubled on him. Zufar said: it is doubled on the mawla of the Taghlibi because he is attached to his master due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'The mawla of a people is one of them.' Our evidence: if he were attached to the master here, it would be a concession, because the doubling is lighter, since it does not contain the description of humiliation; and the freed slave is not attached to the original in concession, and the hadith came contrary to analogy regarding the prohibition of sadaqah, so what is not in its meaning is not attached to it. Do you not see that jizyah is imposed on the mawla of a Muslim if he is a kafir, and if he were attached in concession it would not be imposed on him; unlike sadaqat, because deprivation is established by mere ambiguities, so the mawla is attached to the Hashimi.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage deals with the special tax regime for Banu Taghlib, a Christian Arab tribe. They were not subject to the standard jizyah with its humiliation conditions; rather, 'Umar ibn al-Khattab made a peace treaty with them imposing double the zakat rate (i.e., half a tenth on wealth) instead. This is treated like zakat in its legal details: it is taken from the men (adults) only, not from women or minors, because zakat applies to women but not to minors. The Hanafis argue that since the basis is double zakat, zakat's rules apply. Opponents (Zufar, Shafi'i, Malik) consider it jizyah and thus not taken from women. The second part discusses the mawla (freed slave) of a Taghlibi or Qurayshi. According to Hanafis, the mawla of a Taghlibi pays jizyah but not doubled; the mawla of a Qurayshi pays jizyah despite his master's exemption. Zufar argues the mawla should be treated like his master (double), but Hanafis respond that attaching the mawla here would be a concession (lightening), and the hadith 'the mawla of a people is one of them' applies only to sadaqah (where it is a restriction), not to jizyah.

Key Terms
بني تغلب (Banu Taghlib): A Christian Arab tribe that lived near the Byzantine borders; they paid double zakat instead of jizyah.
المولى (al-mawla): A freed slave; here discussed regarding liability for jizyah/kharaj after emancipation.
الجزية (al-jizyah): The poll tax on non-Muslim subjects; for Banu Taghlib replaced by double zakat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, from whom is the double zakat taken from Banu Taghlib?
A) Adult men only.
B) Adult men and women.
C) All adults and children.
D) Only the wealthy.

Key Takeaway
The tax on Banu Taghlib is a contractual obligation that follows the rules of zakat, not jizyah, because the treaty specified double zakat and was agreed by the Companions.

The Four Categories of Bayt al-Mal and Their Expenditures
Defines the four categories of Bayt al-Mal and their expenditures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four categories of Bayt al-Mal and state the designated expenditures for each category, as well as explain the ruling on borrowing between funds and the difference between rizq and ata.

Core Idea
The Muslim treasury has four separate funds, each with specific sources and purposes, and the Imam must allocate them accordingly.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq defines the four categories of the Islamic treasury (Bayt al-Mal) and their respective expenditures. Understanding these categories is essential for grasping the fiscal structure of an Islamic state and the responsibilities of the ruler. The text also addresses how the Imam may borrow between funds and distinguishes between 'rizq' (monthly pay) and 'ata' (annual stipend).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Four Categories
List the four categories of Bayt al-Mal as described: (1) kharaj, jizya, and wealth taken without fighting; (2) zakat and ushr; (3) khums of spoils, minerals, and treasure; (4) luqata, estates with no heirs, and blood money of a person without a guardian.
Each category has its own source of revenue.
2
Match Sources to Expenditures
For each category, note the prescribed spending: Category 1 goes to general Muslim interests (defense, infrastructure, salaries for judges/soldiers/scholars); Category 2 goes to zakat recipients; Category 3 goes to the five recipients named in Quran 8:41; Category 4 goes to poor foundlings and those without guardians.
The Imam must not mix funds.
3
Understand Borrowing Rules
If one category is empty, the Imam may borrow from another but must repay when funds become available, except if the borrowed funds were from zakat or khums given to poor kharaj payers—they need not repay.
This is a unique Hanafi position.
4
Distinguish Between Rizq and Ata
Rizq is monthly salary for soldiers; ata is an annual or occasional stipend. Ata is a gift not owned until possession, so if a soldier dies mid-year after receiving a full year's ata, there is a dispute among Hanafi imams whether the family must return the unused portion.
The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say no return; Muhammad says yes.

في مصالحنا كسد الثغور وبناء القناطر .
أي مصالح المسلمين
بلا قتال : بأن أخذ بصلح، فلو بقتال يخمس ثم يقسم الباقي بين الغانمين كما مر. (ط، عيني) يصرف في مصالحنا: اعلم أن بيوت مال المسلمين أربعة لكل خزانة ومصرف: الأول: ما ذكره المصنف أي
الخراج والجزية، والمال المأخوذ من التغلبي وهدية أهل الحرب ،للإمام، والذي أخذنا من أهل الحرب بلا قتال، ومن جملة هذا النوع ما يأخذه العاشر من أهل الحرب وأهل الذمة إذا مروا عليه ومال أهل نجران، وما صولح عليه أهل الحرب على ترك القتال قبل نزول العسكر بساحتهم، كل ذلك يصرف إلى مصالح المسلمين، مثل سد الثغور أي تحصينها بالرجال والعدة والذخيرة وبناء القناطر والجسور وأرزاق القضاة والعمال الذين يأخذون الصدقات، ويدخل فيه كل من يعمل للمسلمين كالكتاب عند القضاة والرقباء على السواحل، ومثل أرزاق العلماء أي أصحاب التفسير والفقه والحديث والعلوم الشرعية، ومثل المقاتلة ومثل نفقة ذراري هؤلاء؛ لأن نفقة الذرية على الآباء، فلو لم يعطوا كفايتهم لاحتاجوا إلى الاكتساب. وإنما قيد بقوله : "بلا" قتال؛ لأن المأخوذ منهم بالقتال يخمس ثم يقسم بين الغانمين وأفاد بقوله: كـ"سد الثغور" بكاف التمثيل أنه يصر أيضاً هذا النوع لنحو الكراع والسلاح وعمارة المساجد والرباطات والعدة للعدو، وحفر أنهار العامة وترميمها والصرف على إقامة شعائر المساجد من وظائف الإمامة والأذان ونحوهما، الثاني: من أنواع بيت المال الزكاة والعشر، ومصرفهما ما ذكر في كتاب الزكاة ممن يجوز صرف الزكاة إليه. والثالث: خمس الغنائم والمعادن والركاز، ومصرفه ما ذكره الله تعالى في قوله: ﴿فَأَنَّ لِلَّهِ خُمُسَهُ الله (الأنفال: ٤١) ، وقد ذكر في كتاب السير والرابع: اللقطات والتركات التي لا وارث لها ودية مقتول لا ولي له، ومصرفها اللقيط الفقير والفقراء الذين لا أولياء لهم، يعطون منها نفقاتهم وأدويتهم، ويكفن منها موتاهم ويعقل منها جناياتهم، وعلى الإمام أن يجعل لكل نوع من هذه الأنواع بيتاً يخصه، ولا يخلط بعضه ببعض. فإن لم يكن في بعضها شيء، فله أن يستقرض عليه من النوع الآخر، ويصرفه إلى أهل ذلك، ثم إذا حصل من ذلك النوع شيء يرده في المستقرض منه إلا أن يكون المصروف من الصدقات أو خمس لغنيمة على أهل الخراج، وهم فقراء، فإنه لا يرد فيه شيئاً؛ لأنهم مستحقون للصدقات، وكذا في غيره إذا صرفه إلى مستحقه، ويجب على الإمام أن يتقي الله تعالى، ويصرف إلى كل مستحق قدر حاجته من غير زيادة، فإن قصر في شيء من ذلك كان الله عليه حسيباً. رمز الحقائق: ٤٤١/١] (فتح)

أي وكفاية المقاتلة أي ذراري من ذكر من هؤلاء المذكورين
والجسور: جمع جسر وهو أعم من القنطرة؛ لأنه قد يكون بالخشب وقد يكون بالتراب، والقنطرة لا تكون إلا بالحجر. (عيني) والعمال: بضم العين جمع عامل، وهو الذي يعمل للمسلمين مثل الساعي الذي يجمع الزكاة والعشور [ رمز الحقائق: ٤٤١/١] والعلماء: أي وكفاية العلماء والمفتيين. (عيني)
ومن مات إلخ كالمرأة إذا ماتت ولها نفقة مفروضة في ذمة الزوج، وقيد بقوله: "في نصف السنة"؛ لأنه إذا مات في آخر السنة يستحب صرفه إلى ورثته؛ لأنه قد أوفى عناه فيصرف إليه ؛ ليكون أقرب إلى الوفاء، ولو عجل لواحد منهم كفاية سنة ثم عزل أو مات قبل تمام السنة قيل: يجب رد ما بقي من السنة، وقيل: لا يرجع عند الشيخين ويرجع على قياس قول محمد في نفقة الزوج. رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٢/١] واعلم أن الرزق والعطاء متقاربان إلا أن الفقهاء فرقوا بينهما، فقيل: الرزق: ما يخرج للجندي كل شهر، والعطاء: ما يخرج له في السنة مرة أو مرتين وقيل العطاء كل سنة أو شهر، والرزق يوماً بيوم، وقيل: العطاء ما يصرف للمقاتلة، والرزق ما يجعل لفقراء المسلمين غير المقاتلة. العطاء: وهو اسم لما يصرف إليهم؛ لأنه صلة فلا يملك قبل القبض. (عيني)
The Book of Campaigns and Jihad. Rulings of Jizya. Kharaj, jizya, the wealth of the Taghlibi, the gift of the people of war, and what we take from them without fighting: it is spent by the Imam (i.e., the wealth of the people of war) for our interests, like fortifying frontiers and building bridges. (i.e., the interests of Muslims.) Without fighting: that is, taken by peace treaty. If taken by fighting, it is subject to khums, then the remainder is divided among the participants in the battle as previously mentioned. (T, Ayni) It is spent for our interests: Know that the treasuries of the Muslims are four, each with a treasury and a spending category. The first: what the author mentioned, i.e., kharaj and jizya, the wealth taken from the Taghlibi, the gift of the people of war, for the Imam, and what we take from the people of war without fighting. Included in this type is what the tithe-collector takes from the people of war and the dhimmis when they pass by him, the wealth of the people of Najran, and what the people of war are reconciled upon to leave fighting before the army descends upon their territory. All of that is spent for the interests of the Muslims, such as fortifying frontiers (i.e., strengthening them with men, equipment, and supplies), building bridges and crossings, the salaries of judges and officials who collect the alms. Included in this is everyone who works for the Muslims, like scribes for judges and guards on the coasts, and like the salaries of scholars (i.e., exegetes, jurists, hadith specialists, and religious sciences), and like the fighters, and like the expenses of their offspring; because the maintenance of offspring is incumbent upon fathers, so if they are not given sufficiency they would need to earn. He only restricted it by 'without fighting' because what is taken from them by fighting is subjected to khums then divided among the participants. And by saying 'like fortifying frontiers' with the preposition of similarity, he indicates that this type is also spent for such things as horses and weapons, building mosques and ribats, preparing for the enemy, digging and repairing public canals, and spending on establishing the rites of mosques such as the functions of imamate, adhan, and the like. The second type of Bayt al-Mal: zakat and ushr, and their spending is what was mentioned in the Book of Zakat regarding those to whom zakat may be given. The third: the khums of spoils, minerals, and buried treasure, and its spending is what Allah mentioned in His saying: 'And know that of anything you obtain as spoils, for Allah is one-fifth of it' (Al-Anfal 41), and it was mentioned in the Book of Campaigns. The fourth: luqatahs (found property) and estates that have no heir, and the blood money of a slain person who has no guardian, and its spending is for the foundling poor and the poor who have no guardians; they are given their expenses and medicines, their dead are shrouded from it, and their injuries are paid from it. The Imam must allocate a separate treasury for each of these types and not mix them. If there is nothing in one, he may borrow from another type and spend it for its recipients. Then when something from that type comes in, he repays what he borrowed, unless the expenditure was from the alms or the khums of spoils upon the people of kharaj who are poor; then he does not repay anything because they are deserving of alms. Similarly, in other cases if he spends it on its deserving recipients. The Imam must fear Allah and spend for each deserving person the amount of his need without excess. If he falls short in any of that, Allah will hold him accountable. (Ramooz al-Haqaiq 1/441) (Fath) Al-khafah? al-thughur: plural of thaghr, which is the place of the enemy. (Ramooz al-Haqaiq 1/441) (T) Min al-qanatir: plural of qantara, which is what is built over water for crossing. (Ramooz al-Haqaiq 1/441) The Book of Campaigns and Jihad: Rulings of Jizya. And the bridges and the sufficiency of judges, officials, scholars, fighters, and their offspring. Whoever dies in the middle of the year is deprived of the stipend. (i.e., and the sufficiency of the fighters, i.e., the offspring of those mentioned.) And al-jusur: plural of jisr, which is more general than qantara because it may be of wood or earth, while qantara is only of stone. (Ayni) And al-ummal: with damm on the ayn, plural of amil, which is the one who works for the Muslims, such as the collector who collects zakat and ushr. (Ramooz al-Haqaiq 1/441) And al-ulama: i.e., the sufficiency of scholars and muftis. (Ayni) 'Whoever dies [in the middle of the year]' etc. is like a woman who dies while she has a prescribed nafaqah due from her husband. He restricted it by 'in the middle of the year' because if he dies at the end of the year, it is recommended to spend it for his heirs because he has fully performed his service? so it is spent for him to be closer to fulfillment. If one gives one of them a year's sufficiency in advance and then is dismissed or dies before the year is complete, it is said: he must return the remainder of the year; and it is said: he does not take it back according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), but he does take it back according to the analogy of Muhammad's opinion regarding the nafaqah of the wife. (Ramooz al-Haqaiq 1/442) Know that 'rizq' and 'ata' are close in meaning, but the jurists differentiate between them. It is said: rizq is what is given to the soldier every month, and ata is what is given to him once or twice a year. And it is said: ata is every year or month, and rizq is day by day. And it is said: ata is what is spent for the fighters, and rizq is what is set aside for the poor Muslims who are not fighters. (Fath) Al-ata: it is a name for what is spent to them because it is a gift, so it is not owned before taking possession. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage from the commentary of Kanz al-Daqaiq explains the four categories of the Muslim treasury (Bayt al-Mal) and their respective expenditures. The first category includes kharaj (land tax), jizya (poll tax), wealth of the Taghlibi Christians, gifts from hostile people, and any wealth taken from them without fighting (i.e., by peace treaty). This wealth is at the disposal of the Imam and must be spent for the general interests of the Muslims, such as fortifying borders, building bridges, paying judges, officials, scholars, fighters, and supporting their families. It can also be used for military equipment, mosques, and public works. The second category is zakat and ushr, whose recipients are detailed in the Book of Zakat. The third is the one-fifth (khums) of spoils, minerals, and buried treasure, whose expenditure is specified in the Quranic verse (8:41). The fourth category includes lost property, estates with no heirs, and blood money of a person without a guardian; these are given to the poor and foundlings. The Imam must keep these funds separate and may borrow from one category for another if needed, with an exception for zakat/khums given to poor kharaj payers—they need not repay. The passage also discusses the distinction between 'rizq' (monthly soldier pay) and 'ata' (annual or occasional stipend) and mentions a ruling: if a stipend is advanced for a full year and the recipient dies mid-year, there is a difference of opinion among the Hanafi imams—the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say the surplus need not be returned, while Muhammad says it should be returned, analogizing to the wife's nafaqah.

Key Terms
الخراج (al-kharaj): A land tax levied on agricultural land, typically from non-Muslim subjects.
الجزية (al-jizyah): A poll tax imposed on free adult non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) in exchange for protection and exemption from military service.
العطاء (al-ata): A stipend or grant given from the state treasury, typically to soldiers or others, often annually or semi-annually.
الرزق (al-rizq): Sustenance or salary, in this context monthly pay for soldiers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a permissible expenditure from the first category of Bayt al-Mal (kharaj and jizya)?
A) Building a bridge.
B) Paying salaries of judges.
C) Distributing to the poor as zakat.
D) Purchasing weapons for the frontier.

Key Takeaway
The four categories of Bayt al-Mal must be kept separate; each has specific sources and designated expenditures, and borrowing between them is allowed only under strict conditions.

Stipends: Death Mid-Year and the Advance Payment Dispute
Commentary on stipend distribution and death during service

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stipend forfeiture when a fighter dies mid-year and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over returning advanced stipends.

Core Idea
A stipend is a gift not owned until receipt; its return upon death before year-end is disputed between the Sahibayn and Imam Muhammad.

The state treasury provides stipends to fighters, but what happens if the recipient dies before the year ends? The Hanafi school has a clear default rule, but a dispute arises when the stipend is paid in advance. This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentaries walks through the ruling and the reasoning behind the two positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Read the passage: 'Whoever dies in the middle of the year is deprived of the stipend.' This means if a fighter dies before completing half the year, the stipend is forfeited. If he dies after half the year, it is recommended to give it to his heirs.
This is the general principle based on the idea that the stipend is a gift for services rendered.
2
Understand the nature of the stipend
The passage clarifies that 'ata' is a gift (silah) and is not owned before physical receipt. This distinction is key to the dispute.
Contrast with rizq (monthly salary) which may have different rules.
3
Analyze the advance payment scenario
If the stipend is given for the whole year in advance and the recipient is dismissed or dies before the year ends, two views exist: the Sahibayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) say no return; Muhammad says the remainder must be returned.
The dispute hinges on whether the stipend is a gift (silah) or compensation for service.
4
Examine the proofs
Muhammad analogizes to a wife's maintenance: if she dies after receiving advance maintenance, the remainder is returned. The Sahibayn argue the stipend is a gift, not a salary, so once given it is not recoverable.
The Sahibayn see the stipend as a discretionary grant, not a debt.
5
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: under Sahibayn, heirs keep the entire advanced stipend; under Muhammad, they must return the portion for the unserved period.
This is a real-world consequence for families of fallen soldiers.

(عيني) والعمال: بضم العين جمع عامل، وهو الذي يعمل للمسلمين مثل الساعي الذي يجمع الزكاة والعشور [ رمز الحقائق: ٤٤١/١] والعلماء: أي وكفاية العلماء والمفتيين. (فتح) العطاء: وهو اسم لما يصرف إليهم؛ لأنه صلة فلا يملك قبل القبض. (عيني)
And bridges and the sufficiency of judges, workers, scholars, fighters, and their children. Whoever dies in the middle of the year is deprived of the stipend. That is: and the sufficiency of fighters, i.e., the children of those mentioned among these mentioned ones. And al-jusur: plural of jisr, which is more general than qanatirah; because it may be of wood and may be of earth, while qanatirah is only of stone. (Ayni) And whoever dies etc. is like a woman if she dies and she has a fixed maintenance in the dhimmah of her husband, and it is restricted by his saying: 'in the middle of the year'; because if he dies at the end of the year, it is recommended to give it to his heirs; because he has completed his service, so it is given to him to be closer to fulfillment. And if he advanced to one of them the sufficiency of a year, then he was dismissed or died before the completion of the year, it is said: he must return what remains of the year, and it is said: he does not return it according to the two shaykhs, and it is returned by analogy with the saying of Muhammad concerning the maintenance of the wife. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/442] And know that al-rizq and al-ata are close, except that the jurists differentiated between them. It is said: rizq is what is given to the soldier every month, and ata is what is given to him once or twice a year. And it is said: ata is every year or month, and rizq is day by day. And it is said: ata is what is disbursed to fighters, and rizq is what is set aside for poor Muslims who are not fighters. (Fath) Al-Ata: it is a name for what is disbursed to them; because it is a gift (silah), so it is not owned before receipt. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the rulings concerning military stipends and related expenditures from the state treasury. The commentator first explains that the term 'jisr' (bridge) is more general than 'qanatirah' (stone arch), as it can be made of wood or earth. 'Ummal' (workers) refers to those who serve the Muslims, such as collectors of zakat and tithes. The core ruling is that if a stipend recipient dies in the first half of the year, the stipend is forfeited; if in the second half, it is recommended to give it to his heirs because he already served most of the year. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: if one is given the year's stipend in advance and then dies or is dismissed before year-end, the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the remainder is not recoverable, while Muhammad says it must be returned, analogous to a wife's maintenance. Finally, the terms 'rizq' and 'ata' are distinguished: rizq is monthly or daily, while ata is annual or for fighters specifically. The ataa is a gift (silah) and is not owned until physically received.

Key Terms
العطاء (al-ata'): A stipend given once or twice a year to fighters, considered a gift (silah).
الرزق (al-rizq): A stipend given monthly or daily, often for non-fighters.
الصلة (al-silah): A gift or gratuity, not a contractual payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), if a soldier is given his annual stipend in advance and then dies before the year ends, what is the ruling?
A) The remaining portion must be returned to the treasury.
B) The heirs keep the entire stipend.
C) The stipend is forfeited entirely.
D) Only half is kept.

Key Takeaway
A stipend (ata) is treated as a gift not owned until receipt, and its return upon early death is disputed within the Hanafi school: Sahibayn say no return, Muhammad says yes by analogy with maintenance.

Male Apostate: Call to Islam Before Killing
Ruling on killing male apostate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing a male apostate and explain the dislike of killing before presenting Islam, using the dalil from the hadith.

Core Idea
An apostate is not killed immediately; he must be called back to Islam first.

In this lesson, we examine the first ruling on apostasy: the male apostate. The Hanafi school emphasizes that while the apostate's blood becomes permissible (mubah) due to his rejection of Islam, killing him before offering him the chance to repent is disliked (makruh). This reflects the Sunna of calling to Islam even after apostasy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage rules that it is disliked (makruh) to kill the apostate before presenting Islam to him. Identify the hukm level: makruh tanzihi (disliked) not haram.
The killer is not liable for blood money or expiation.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' (من بدل دينه فاقتلوه) which establishes that the apostate's blood is mubah. However, the command to call to Islam is based on the Prophetic practice of giving the opportunity to repent.
The hadith is cited later in the passage for the female apostate dispute.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The general command 'kill him' indicates permissibility of killing, but the Hanafi school adds the condition that the call to Islam must precede execution, deriving this from the Prophet's own practice and from the principle of al-amr ma'a al-imkan: the command to kill is suspended until the call.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some early scholars held that the apostate must be killed immediately without calling. The Hanafi position is that calling is a sunna mu'akkada (emphasized sunna).

باب المرتدين
كتاب السير والجهاد أو عما انتقل إليه. وكره قتله قبله ولم يضمن قاتله، ولا تقتل المرتدة بل تحبس حتى
المرتد

بردته أي مراعى عند أبي حنيفة أي المرتد

دائما وتجبر على الإسلام
والخامس من يقر بالكل، لكن ينكر عموم رسالة المصطفى الله كالعيسوية. فيكفى في الأولين بقول لا إله إلا الله، وفي الثالث: بقول محمد رسول الله، وفي الرابع بأحدهما، وفي الخامس بهما مع التبري عن كل دين يخالف دين الإسلام وإنما كانت توبة المرتد بالتبري عن الأديان كلها غير دين الإسلام؛ لأنه لا . دین حتى يكلف بالتبري عنه، وفيه إشعار بأنه لو قال الكافر: "لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله" يصير مسلماً إذا علم أنه الإسلام، ويشترط معرفة اسمه عليها دون معرفة اسم أبيه وجده ثم اعلم أن الإسلام كما يكون بالقول يكون بالفعل أيضاً كما لو صلى مكتوبة وأتمها مقتدياً أو أذن في الوقت، أو سجد للتلاوة، أو أدى زكاة السائمة لا بغير ذلك.(فتح) أو عما انتقل إليه :: أي أو يتبرأ عن الدين الذي انتقل. (مص) إليه؛ لحصول المقصود، والأول هو الأولى؛ لأن المرتد لا . دین له. (عيني) وكره قتله أي يكره قتل المرتد قبل عرض الإسلام عليه؛ لما فيه من ترك المندوب، سواء قتله الإمام أو غيره، إلا أن الغير يؤدب لجرأته على الإمام، وعلى القول بوجوب العرض يكره تحريما، لكن لا يضمن قاتله؛ لأنه مباح الدم فلا شيء عليه من الدية والكفارة، وإنما كره القتل؛ لأنه يمكن أن يسلم. (مستخلص، فتح) قبله : أي قبل عرض الإسلام عليه ومعنى الكراهية هنا ترك المستحب. (عيني)
ولا تقتل المرتدة إلخ: [سواء كانت حرة أو أمة. (ط، عيني] أي إذا ارتدت المرأة، لا تقتل عندنا، وقال الشافعي: تقتل؛ لإطلاق قوله عليه : من بدل دينه فاقتلوه"، وكلمة "من" يعم الرجال والنساء، وقد تحقق تبديل الدين منها، وبه قال مالك وأحمد، ولنا: أن النبي لها الله فهي عن قتل النساء؛ لأن المبيح للقتل كفر المحارب، والحرب معدوم في المرأة، فكما لا تقتل في الكفر الأصلي لا تقتل في الكفر الطاري، وقوله: "بل" تحبس"؛ لأنها امتنعت عن إيفاء حق الله تعالى بعد الإقرار مع القدرة على إيفائه، فتحبس وتجبر على الأداء في حقوق العباد. ولو قتلها قاتل لم يضمن
شيئاً؛ لأن قيمة الدم بالإسلام، وقد زال، لكنه يؤدب على ذلك؛ لارتكابه ما لا يحل. (مستخلص، فتح)
حتى تسلم أي إلى أن تسلم وتضرب في كل ثلاثة أيام مبالغة على الحمل إلى الإسلام. (عيني) ويزول ملك المرتد : لأنه بالردة زالت عصمة دمه، فكذا عصمة ماله وقوله: "زوالاً موقوفاً" أي إلى أن يتبين حاله؛ لأنه هالك حكماً، فصار كالهالك حقيقة في زوال الملك. وقوله: "فإن أسلم" الفاء تفسيرية، والجملة تفسير لقوله: "زوالا موقوفا" ، والمراد أنه بالردة يزول ملكه زوالاً موقوفاً، فإن استمر حتى مات حقيقة، أو حكم بلحاقه، استمر الزوال الثابت من وقت الردة، وإن عاد عاد إلى ملكه، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما: لا يزول ملكه؛ لأنه مكلف محتاج، فإلى أن يقتل يبقى ملكه كالمحكوم عليه بالرجم والقصاص، ولأبي حنيفة: أنه مقهور في الدنيا حتى يقتل، ولا قتل بدون الحرب تحقيقاً أو تقديراً، وكونه حربياً يوجب زوال ملكه،
وإن مات، أو قتل على ردّته، ورث كسب إسلامه وارثه المسلم بعد قضاء دين إسلامه.
وهو مرتد
أو حكم بلحاقه
أي وذلك بعد إلخ
إلا أنه مدعو إلى الإسلام بالإجبار عليه، ويرجى عوده إليه، فتوقفنا في أمره، فإن أسلم جعل العارض كأن لم يكن في حق هذا الحكم، وصار كأن لم يزل فلم يعمل السبب، وإن مات أو قتل على ردته، أو لحق بدار الحرب وحكم بلحاقه، استقر كفره، فيعمل السبب عمله، وهو إزالة الملك. (مستخلص، فتح) وإن مات إلخ: أي وإن لم يسلم المرتد ومات أو قتل على ردته انتقل ما اكتسبه في الإسلام إلى ورثته المسلمين، وكان ما اكتسبه في حال الردة فيئا وتقضى الديون التي لزمته في الإسلام بما اكتسبه في حالة الإسلام، والديون التي لزمته في الردة بما اكتسبه في حالة الردة وعن أبي حنيفة أنه يبتدأ بكسب الإسلام، فتقضى عنه، فإن لم يف بذلك، تقضى من كسب ردته، وعنه على عكس ذلك، فصارت عنده ثلاثة وجوه: وجه الأول وهو ظاهر الرواية أن المستحق بالسببين مختلف وحصول كل واحد من السببين باعتبار السبب الذي وجب به الدين، فيقضى كل دين من الكسب المكتسب في تلك الحالة، لتكون الغرم بالغنم.
ووجه الثاني : أن كسب الإسلام ملكه حتى يخلفه الوارث فيه، ومن شرط هذه الخلافة الفراغ من حق المورث، فيقدم الدين عليه، وكسب الردة ليس بملك له ؛ لبطلان الملك ؛ للردة فلا يقضى دينه إلا إذا تعذر قضاءه من محل آخر، فحينئذ يقضى منه وجه القول الثالث: أن كسب الإسلام حق الورثة وكسب الردة خالص حقه، فكان قضاء دينه منه أولى إلا إذا تعذر بأن لم يف به، فحينئذ يقضى من كسب الإسلام تقديماً لحقه، وأما عندهما، فيقضى ديونه من الكسبين؛ لأنهما جميعاً ملكه وكلا الكسبين موروث لورثته؛ لأن ملكه في الكسبين باق، ولا يزول ملكه كما تقدم، فإذا كان ملكه فينتقل بموته إلى ورثته وقال الشافعي: كلاهما فيء؛ لأنه مات كافراً، والمسلم لا يرث الكافر.
حربي
ثم بقي مال لا أمان لهم، فيكون فيئاً، ولهما أن الإرث فيه يستند إلى ما قبل ردته؛ إذ الردة سبب الموت، فيكون توريث المسلم من المسلم، ولأبي حنيفة: أنه يمكن الاستناد في كسب الإسلام؛ لوجوده قبل الردة، ولا يمكن الاستناد في كسب الردة؛ لعدمه ،قبلها، وقال مالك وأحمد مثل قول الشافعي وكسب المرتدة سواء كان كسب الإسلام أو الردة ،لورثتها، وهذا بالاتفاق ويرثها زوجها إن ارتدت وهي مريضة وماتت في العدة، وإن كانت صحيحة لا يرثها؛ لأنها لا تقتل فلا تصير فارة بالردة بخلاف المرتد، فإنه يصير فاراً بالردة وإن كان صحيحاً؛ لوجوب القتل، فأشبه الطلاق في مرض الموت. ثم اختلفت الروايات عن أبي حنيفة فيمن يرث المرتد، فروى الحسن عنه أنه يرثه كان وارثاً له وقت ردته، من كذلك إلى وقت موته أو قتله أو القضاء بلحاقه، وروى أبو يوسف أنه يعتبر وجوده وقت الردة، ولا يبطل بموته أو بشيء آخر قبل موت المرتد، وروى محمد عنه أنه يعتبر كونه وارثاً عند موت المرتد أو قتله، أو القضاء بلحاقه سواء كان موجوداً عند الردة، أو حدث بعده وهو الأصح. (مستخلص، فتح)
وبقي
Chapter of Apostates. Book of Siyar and Jihad. Or [repentance from] what he converted to. It is disliked to kill him before [presenting Islam] and his killer is not liable. The female apostate is not killed but imprisoned until she becomes Muslim. And the ownership of the apostate over his property ceases with a suspended cessation; if he becomes Muslim his ownership returns... [continues with full text translation covering definitions, repentance, killing, female apostate, property suspension, inheritance, and intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disputes.]
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with its commentary, covers several rulings on apostates (murtadd). First, it defines the apostate and explains the conditions for repentance. The author notes that a male apostate should have Islam presented to him before execution, and killing him before that is disliked (makruh) but carries no penalty because his blood is mubah (permissible). Then it addresses the female apostate: she is not killed but imprisoned until she returns to Islam. This is the Hanafi position, against the Shafi'is who argue from the general command 'kill the one who changes his religion.' The Hanafi response is based on the Prophet's prohibition of killing women, because the justification for killing is the capacity for combat, which women lack. The commentary also explains that if someone kills the female apostate, he is not liable for blood money or expiation, but he is disciplined. 

The next part discusses the property of the apostate. According to Abu Hanifa, ownership of property acquired during Islam is suspended (zawal mawquf) upon apostasy. If the apostate returns to Islam, the ownership reverts. If he dies or is killed as an apostate, the suspension continues and the property is treated as if ownership was removed from the moment of apostasy. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that ownership does not cease; the apostate continues to own his property until execution, similar to someone sentenced to death. 

Finally, inheritance is discussed. If the apostate dies as a non-Muslim, his earnings during Islam go to his Muslim heirs after debts; earnings during apostasy become fay' (booty). The commentary details three narrations from Abu Hanifa on the order of paying debts from the two categories. The Sahibayn hold that both types are owned and inherited by Muslim heirs. Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad hold that all earnings are fay' because a Muslim cannot inherit from a non-Muslim. The text also covers the special case of the female apostate's earnings, which are inherited by consensus, and different narrations from Abu Hanifa on who inherits from the apostate.

Key Terms
مرتد (murtadd): A person who disbelieves after having believed.
عرض الإسلام (ard al-Islam): Presenting Islam to the apostate and inviting him to repent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on killing a male apostate before presenting Islam to him?
A) Mustahab (recommended)
B) Makruh (disliked)
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Wajib (obligatory)

Key Takeaway
A male apostate must be called to Islam before execution; killing without the call is disliked but not liable.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
10 min
Female Apostate: Imprisonment Not Killing
Ruling on female apostate with inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that a female apostate is imprisoned and not killed, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A female apostate is imprisoned until she returns to Islam, never killed.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between male and female apostates: while the male may be killed after being called, the female is never killed. The justification is rooted in the prohibition of killing women in war and the absence of combat capability in women. The Shafi'i school disagrees, citing the general command 'kill the one who changes his religion.'

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The female apostate (free or slave) is not killed but imprisoned indefinitely until she returns to Islam. No capital punishment.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i (and Malik, Ahmad) hold that the female apostate is killed, like the male, based on the general command of the hadith.
The hadith uses the masculine pronoun but is considered general.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The hadith 'Whoever changes his religion, kill him' is general (amm) and includes females. The word 'man' (من) encompasses both genders in Arabic usage.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the hadith is qualified by other evidences, specifically the Prophet's prohibition of killing women in war. Since the justification for killing the apostate is his hostile nature (harbi), and women do not participate in combat, they are not killed. Also, the hadith on killing women is specific and takes precedence.
The Hanafi response is based on takhsis al-amm bi al-khass (specifying the general by the specific).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi: female apostate imprisoned indefinitely. Shafi'i: female apostate executed after the call.
