إلا أنه مدعو إلى الإسلام بالإجبار عليه، ويرجى عوده إليه، فتوقفنا في أمره، فإن أسلم جعل العارض كأن لم يكن في حق هذا الحكم، وصار كأن لم يزل فلم يعمل السبب، وإن مات أو قتل على ردته، أو لحق بدار الحرب وحكم بلحاقه، استقر كفره، فيعمل السبب عمله، وهو إزالة الملك. (مستخلص، فتح) وإن مات إلخ: أي وإن لم يسلم المرتد ومات أو قتل على ردته انتقل ما اكتسبه في الإسلام إلى ورثته المسلمين، وكان ما اكتسبه في حال الردة فيئا وتقضى الديون التي لزمته في الإسلام بما اكتسبه في حالة الإسلام، والديون التي لزمته في الردة بما اكتسبه في حالة الردة وعن أبي حنيفة أنه يبتدأ بكسب الإسلام، فتقضى عنه، فإن لم يف بذلك، تقضى من كسب ردته، وعنه على عكس ذلك، فصارت عنده ثلاثة وجوه: وجه الأول وهو ظاهر الرواية أن المستحق بالسببين مختلف وحصول كل واحد من السببين باعتبار السبب الذي وجب به الدين، فيقضى كل دين من الكسب المكتسب في تلك الحالة، لتكون الغرم بالغنم.
ووجه الثاني : أن كسب الإسلام ملكه حتى يخلفه الوارث فيه، ومن شرط هذه الخلافة الفراغ من حق المورث، فيقدم الدين عليه، وكسب الردة ليس بملك له ؛ لبطلان الملك ؛ للردة فلا يقضى دينه إلا إذا تعذر قضاءه من محل آخر، فحينئذ يقضى منه وجه القول الثالث: أن كسب الإسلام حق الورثة وكسب الردة خالص حقه، فكان قضاء دينه منه أولى إلا إذا تعذر بأن لم يف به، فحينئذ يقضى من كسب الإسلام تقديماً لحقه، وأما عندهما، فيقضى ديونه من الكسبين؛ لأنهما جميعاً ملكه وكلا الكسبين موروث لورثته؛ لأن ملكه في الكسبين باق، ولا يزول ملكه كما تقدم، فإذا كان ملكه فينتقل بموته إلى ورثته وقال الشافعي: كلاهما فيء؛ لأنه مات كافراً، والمسلم لا يرث الكافر.
حربي
ثم بقي مال لا أمان لهم، فيكون فيئاً، ولهما أن الإرث فيه يستند إلى ما قبل ردته؛ إذ الردة سبب الموت، فيكون توريث المسلم من المسلم، ولأبي حنيفة: أنه يمكن الاستناد في كسب الإسلام؛ لوجوده قبل الردة، ولا يمكن الاستناد في كسب الردة؛ لعدمه ،قبلها، وقال مالك وأحمد مثل قول الشافعي وكسب المرتدة سواء كان كسب الإسلام أو الردة ،لورثتها، وهذا بالاتفاق ويرثها زوجها إن ارتدت وهي مريضة وماتت في العدة، وإن كانت صحيحة لا يرثها؛ لأنها لا تقتل فلا تصير فارة بالردة بخلاف المرتد، فإنه يصير فاراً بالردة وإن كان صحيحاً؛ لوجوب القتل، فأشبه الطلاق في مرض الموت. ثم اختلفت الروايات عن أبي حنيفة فيمن يرث المرتد، فروى الحسن عنه أنه يرثه كان وارثاً له وقت ردته، من كذلك إلى وقت موته أو قتله أو القضاء بلحاقه، وروى أبو يوسف أنه يعتبر وجوده وقت الردة، ولا يبطل بموته أو بشيء آخر قبل موت المرتد، وروى محمد عنه أنه يعتبر كونه وارثاً عند موت المرتد أو قتله، أو القضاء بلحاقه سواء كان موجوداً عند الردة، أو حدث بعده وهو الأصح. (مستخلص، فتح)
وبقي
Chapter of Apostates. Book of Siyar and Jihad. Or [repentance from] what he converted to. It is disliked to kill him before [presenting Islam] and his killer is not liable. The female apostate is not killed but imprisoned until she becomes Muslim. And the ownership of the apostate over his property ceases with a suspended cessation; if he becomes Muslim his ownership returns... [continues with full text translation covering definitions, repentance, killing, female apostate, property suspension, inheritance, and intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disputes.]
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with its commentary, covers several rulings on apostates (murtadd). First, it defines the apostate and explains the conditions for repentance. The author notes that a male apostate should have Islam presented to him before execution, and killing him before that is disliked (makruh) but carries no penalty because his blood is mubah (permissible). Then it addresses the female apostate: she is not killed but imprisoned until she returns to Islam. This is the Hanafi position, against the Shafi'is who argue from the general command 'kill the one who changes his religion.' The Hanafi response is based on the Prophet's prohibition of killing women, because the justification for killing is the capacity for combat, which women lack. The commentary also explains that if someone kills the female apostate, he is not liable for blood money or expiation, but he is disciplined. 

The next part discusses the property of the apostate. According to Abu Hanifa, ownership of property acquired during Islam is suspended (zawal mawquf) upon apostasy. If the apostate returns to Islam, the ownership reverts. If he dies or is killed as an apostate, the suspension continues and the property is treated as if ownership was removed from the moment of apostasy. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that ownership does not cease; the apostate continues to own his property until execution, similar to someone sentenced to death. 

Finally, inheritance is discussed. If the apostate dies as a non-Muslim, his earnings during Islam go to his Muslim heirs after debts; earnings during apostasy become fay' (booty). The commentary details three narrations from Abu Hanifa on the order of paying debts from the two categories. The Sahibayn hold that both types are owned and inherited by Muslim heirs. Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad hold that all earnings are fay' because a Muslim cannot inherit from a non-Muslim. The text also covers the special case of the female apostate's earnings, which are inherited by consensus, and different narrations from Abu Hanifa on who inherits from the apostate.

Key Terms
مرتدة (murtaddah): Female apostate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on killing a female apostate?
A) She is killed like the male apostate.
B) She is not killed but imprisoned until she returns to Islam.
C) She is exiled.
D) She is given a choice and then executed if she refuses.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school does not kill female apostates; they are imprisoned until they repent.

Ownership Suspension Upon Apostasy (Zawal Mawquf)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ownership during apostasy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Abu Hanifa's concept of suspended ownership (zawal mawquf) for the apostate's property and contrast it with the Sahibayn's position.

Core Idea
Upon apostasy, the apostate's ownership over his property is suspended, not automatically terminated.

The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on what happens to the apostate's property. Abu Hanifa introduces the unique concept of 'zawal mawquf' (suspended cessation): ownership ceases temporarily upon apostasy, but if he returns to Islam, ownership reverts. The two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that ownership remains intact until execution. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
State the position of Abu Hanifa
Upon apostasy, the apostate's ownership over his property ceases, but the cessation is suspended (zawal mawquf). If he returns to Islam, ownership returns; if he dies or is killed, the cessation becomes permanent from the moment of apostasy.
This is based on the apostate being considered dead in some respects (hālik hukman).
2
State the position of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that ownership does not cease at all. The apostate remains the owner of his property until he is executed. This is because he is still a responsible agent (mukallaf) and has needs.
They analogize to someone sentenced to death by rajm or qisas: they still own property.
3
Follow Abu Hanifa's proof
Because apostasy makes his blood permissible (mubah al-dam), his property also loses its sanctity. The suspension is to give him a chance to return; if he does, ownership is reinstated as if the apostasy never happened.
The suspension is like a pending condition.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's response
They argue that property is needed for sustenance and to fulfill obligations; the apostate still lives until execution, so ownership must remain for practical reasons.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Under Abu Hanifa, if the apostate returns to Islam, he gets his property back. Under the Sahibayn, he never lost it. If he dies, in Abu Hanifa's view, the property from Islam period is inherited, and from apostasy period becomes fay'. In Sahibayn's view, all is inherited.

According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what is the status of the apostate's ownership?
A) Ownership ceases immediately.
B) Ownership ceases in a suspended manner.

Key Takeaway

Inheritance of the Apostate's Earnings
Ruling on inheritance with intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the inheritance of earnings acquired during Islam and during apostasy according to the Hanafi school, and identify the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
Earnings during Islam go to Muslim heirs; earnings during apostasy are fay', according to Abu Hanifa.

When the apostate dies or is killed, his estate is divided based on when the assets were acquired. The Hanafi school distinguishes between 'kasb al-Islam' (earnings while Muslim) and 'kasb al-riddah' (earnings after apostasy). Abu Hanifa holds that the former passes to Muslim heirs after debts, while the latter goes to the public treasury (fay'). The Sahibayn hold that all is inherited. The Shafi'i school says all is fay'. This lesson unpacks the intricate rulings and the three narrations from Abu Hanifa on debt priority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of earnings
Earnings acquired before apostasy (kasb al-Islam) and after apostasy (kasb al-riddah). The ruling differs for each.
2
State Abu Hanifa's primary position
Earnings from Islam: inherited by Muslim heirs after debts from that period. Earnings from apostasy: become fay' (public treasury). Debts from each period are paid from the corresponding earnings.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (three narrations)
There are three narrations from Abu Hanifa on the order of paying debts: (1) each debt from its own earnings (the primary), (2) first pay from kasb al-Islam, then from kasb al-riddah if insufficient, (3) first pay from kasb al-riddah, then from kasb al-Islam.
This shows the complexity and the ongoing ijtihad within the school.
4
State the Sahibayn's position
Both types of earnings are owned by the apostate and thus inherited by Muslim heirs after all debts.
Because they hold ownership does not cease.
5
State the Shafi'i position
All earnings become fay' because the apostate dies as a non-Muslim, and Muslims cannot inherit from non-Muslims.
This is the inter-madhhab dispute.

باب المرتدين
كتاب السير والجهاد أو عما انتقل إليه. وكره قتله قبله ولم يضمن قاتله، ولا تقتل المرتدة بل تحبس حتى

والخامس من يقر بالكل، لكن ينكر عموم رسالة المصطفى الله كالعيسوية. فيكفى في الأولين بقول لا إله إلا الله، وفي الثالث: بقول محمد رسول الله، وفي الرابع بأحدهما، وفي الخامس بهما مع التبري عن كل دين يخالف دين الإسلام وإنما كانت توبة المرتد بالتبري عن الأديان كلها غير دين الإسلام؛ لأنه لا . دین حتى يكلف بالتبري عنه، وفيه إشعار بأنه لو قال الكافر: "لا إله إلا الله محمد رسول الله" يصير مسلماً إذا علم أنه الإسلام، ويشترط معرفة اسمه عليها دون معرفة اسم أبيه وجده ثم اعلم أن الإسلام كما يكون بالقول يكون بالفعل أيضاً كما لو صلى مكتوبة وأتمها مقتدياً أو أذن في الوقت، أو سجد للتلاوة، أو أدى زكاة السائمة لا بغير ذلك.(فتح) أو عما انتقل إليه :: أي أو يتبرأ عن الدين الذي انتقل. حتى تسلم أي إلى أن تسلم وتضرب في كل ثلاثة أيام مبالغة على الحمل إلى الإسلام. (عيني) ويزول ملك المرتد : لأنه بالردة زالت عصمة دمه، فكذا عصمة ماله وقوله: "زوالاً موقوفاً" أي إلى أن يتبين حاله؛ لأنه هالك حكماً، فصار كالهالك حقيقة في زوال الملك. وقوله: "فإن أسلم" الفاء تفسيرية، والجملة تفسير لقوله: "زوالا موقوفا" ، والمراد أنه بالردة يزول ملكه زوالاً موقوفاً، فإن استمر حتى مات حقيقة، أو حكم بلحاقه، استمر الزوال الثابت من وقت الردة، وإن عاد عاد إلى ملكه، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما: لا يزول ملكه؛ لأنه مكلف محتاج، فإلى أن يقتل يبقى ملكه كالمحكوم عليه بالرجم والقصاص، ولأبي حنيفة: أنه مقهور في الدنيا حتى يقتل، ولا قتل بدون الحرب تحقيقاً أو تقديراً، وكونه حربياً يوجب زوال ملكه،
وإن مات، أو قتل على ردّته، ورث كسب إسلامه وارثه المسلم بعد قضاء دين إسلامه.
وهو مرتد
أو حكم بلحاقه
أي وذلك بعد إلخ
إلا أنه مدعو إلى الإسلام بالإجبار عليه، ويرجى عوده إليه، فتوقفنا في أمره، فإن أسلم جعل العارض كأن لم يكن في حق هذا الحكم، وصار كأن لم يزل فلم يعمل السبب، وإن مات أو قتل على ردته، أو لحق بدار الحرب وحكم بلحاقه، استقر كفره، فيعمل السبب عمله، وهو إزالة الملك. (مستخلص، فتح) وإن مات إلخ: أي وإن لم يسلم المرتد ومات أو قتل على ردته انتقل ما اكتسبه في الإسلام إلى ورثته المسلمين، وكان ما اكتسبه في حال الردة فيئا وتقضى الديون التي لزمته في الإسلام بما اكتسبه في حالة الإسلام، والديون التي لزمته في الردة بما اكتسبه في حالة الردة وعن أبي حنيفة أنه يبتدأ بكسب الإسلام، فتقضى عنه، فإن لم يف بذلك، تقضى من كسب ردته، وعنه على عكس ذلك، فصارت عنده ثلاثة وجوه: وجه الأول وهو ظاهر الرواية أن المستحق بالسببين مختلف وحصول كل واحد من السببين باعتبار السبب الذي وجب به الدين، فيقضى كل دين من الكسب المكتسب في تلك الحالة، لتكون الغرم بالغنم.
ووجه الثاني : أن كسب الإسلام ملكه حتى يخلفه الوارث فيه، ومن شرط هذه الخلافة الفراغ من حق المورث، فيقدم الدين عليه، وكسب الردة ليس بملك له ؛ لبطلان الملك ؛ للردة فلا يقضى دينه إلا إذا تعذر قضاءه من محل آخر، فحينئذ يقضى منه وجه القول الثالث: أن كسب الإسلام حق الورثة وكسب الردة خالص حقه، فكان قضاء دينه منه أولى إلا إذا تعذر بأن لم يف به، فحينئذ يقضى من كسب الإسلام تقديماً لحقه، وأما عندهما، فيقضى ديونه من الكسبين؛ لأنهما جميعاً ملكه وكلا الكسبين موروث لورثته؛ لأن ملكه في الكسبين باق، ولا يزول ملكه كما تقدم، فإذا كان ملكه فينتقل بموته إلى ورثته وقال الشافعي: كلاهما فيء؛ لأنه مات كافراً، والمسلم لا يرث الكافر.
حربي
ثم بقي مال لا أمان لهم، فيكون فيئاً، ولهما أن الإرث فيه يستند إلى ما قبل ردته؛ إذ الردة سبب الموت، فيكون توريث المسلم من المسلم، ولأبي حنيفة: أنه يمكن الاستناد في كسب الإسلام؛ لوجوده قبل الردة، ولا يمكن الاستناد في كسب الردة؛ لعدمه ،قبلها، وقال مالك وأحمد مثل قول الشافعي وكسب المرتدة سواء كان كسب الإسلام أو الردة ،لورثتها، وهذا بالاتفاق ويرثها زوجها إن ارتدت وهي مريضة وماتت في العدة، وإن كانت صحيحة لا يرثها؛ لأنها لا تقتل فلا تصير فارة بالردة بخلاف المرتد، فإنه يصير فاراً بالردة وإن كان صحيحاً؛ لوجوب القتل، فأشبه الطلاق في مرض الموت. ثم اختلفت الروايات عن أبي حنيفة فيمن يرث المرتد، فروى الحسن عنه أنه يرثه كان وارثاً له وقت ردته، من كذلك إلى وقت موته أو قتله أو القضاء بلحاقه، وروى أبو يوسف أنه يعتبر وجوده وقت الردة، ولا يبطل بموته أو بشيء آخر قبل موت المرتد، وروى محمد عنه أنه يعتبر كونه وارثاً عند موت المرتد أو قتله، أو القضاء بلحاقه سواء كان موجوداً عند الردة، أو حدث بعده وهو الأصح. (مستخلص، فتح)
وبقي
Chapter of Apostates. Book of Siyar and Jihad. Or [repentance from] what he converted to. It is disliked to kill him before [presenting Islam] and his killer is not liable. The female apostate is not killed but imprisoned until she becomes Muslim. And the ownership of the apostate over his property ceases with a suspended cessation; if he becomes Muslim his ownership returns... [continues with full text translation covering definitions, repentance, killing, female apostate, property suspension, inheritance, and intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab disputes.]
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with its commentary, covers several rulings on apostates (murtadd). First, it defines the apostate and explains the conditions for repentance. The author notes that a male apostate should have Islam presented to him before execution, and killing him before that is disliked (makruh) but carries no penalty because his blood is mubah (permissible). Then it addresses the female apostate: she is not killed but imprisoned until she returns to Islam. This is the Hanafi position, against the Shafi'is who argue from the general command 'kill the one who changes his religion.' The Hanafi response is based on the Prophet's prohibition of killing women, because the justification for killing is the capacity for combat, which women lack. The commentary also explains that if someone kills the female apostate, he is not liable for blood money or expiation, but he is disciplined. 

The next part discusses the property of the apostate. According to Abu Hanifa, ownership of property acquired during Islam is suspended (zawal mawquf) upon apostasy. If the apostate returns to Islam, the ownership reverts. If he dies or is killed as an apostate, the suspension continues and the property is treated as if ownership was removed from the moment of apostasy. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that ownership does not cease; the apostate continues to own his property until execution, similar to someone sentenced to death. 

Finally, inheritance is discussed. If the apostate dies as a non-Muslim, his earnings during Islam go to his Muslim heirs after debts; earnings during apostasy become fay' (booty). The commentary details three narrations from Abu Hanifa on the order of paying debts from the two categories. The Sahibayn hold that both types are owned and inherited by Muslim heirs. Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad hold that all earnings are fay' because a Muslim cannot inherit from a non-Muslim. The text also covers the special case of the female apostate's earnings, which are inherited by consensus, and different narrations from Abu Hanifa on who inherits from the apostate.

Key Terms
كسب الإسلام (kasb al-Islam): Earnings acquired during the period of being Muslim.
كسب الردة (kasb al-riddah): Earnings acquired after apostasy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa's primary view, what happens to the earnings an apostate acquired after apostasy (kasb al-riddah) if he dies?
A) It is inherited by his Muslim heirs.
B) It becomes fay' (public treasury).
C) It is used to pay all his debts first.
D) It is destroyed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between kasb al-Islam and kasb al-riddah for inheritance, a ruling that differs from both the Sahibayn and the Shafi'i school.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
advanced
12 min
Legal Effects of an Apostate Joining the Enemy
Hanafi ruling with rational proof on apostate's ilhaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the apostate's mudabbar, umm walad, and debts upon ilhaq, and explain the qiyas with death that underlies it.

Core Idea
Ilhaq makes the apostate like dead: mudabbar freed from one-third, umm walad from all, debts due.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq deals with a specific scenario: an apostate leaves Muslim territory and joins the enemy. The Hanafi school treats this as analogous to death regarding property rights, but certain effects require a judge's ruling. We will unpack the ruling, the proof (qiyas), and the disagreements with other schools and within the Hanafi school itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key rulings
List the legal consequences that take effect when the judge rules that the apostate has joined the enemy: mudabbar freed from one-third, umm walad freed from all wealth, deferred debts become immediately due.
Rulings require a judge's ruling, not mere ilhaq.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The Hanafi proof is qiyas (analogy): ilhaq severs the apostate's link to Islamic authority as death does. The text states: 'باللحاق صار من أهل الحرب، وهم أموات في حق أحكام أهل الإسلام لانقطاع ولاية الإلزام'.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the authority of obligation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effective cause ('illa) is the cutting of the authority of obligation (wilayat al-ilzam), which is common between death and ilhaq. Therefore, the same rulings apply.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa holds that transactions (sale, etc.) are suspended until return or death. Abu Yusuf says they are valid as from a healthy person; Muhammad says as from a sick person. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab dispute
Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad say the apostate's property remains entirely suspended because the world is one dar. The Hanafi tarjih is based on the loss of Islamic protection via ilhaq.
Practical difference: in Hanafi fiqh, freed slaves are free immediately; in Shafi'i, they remain slaves.

قضاء
أي يكون موقوفا أي المرتد
تفسير لقوله توقف ما كان موقوفا
وكسب ردته أي الذي اكتسبه في حال الردة (عيني) قيء: أي غنيمة توضع في بيت المال. (معدن) دين: أي الدين الذي ركبه في حال ردته. (عيني) وإن حكم بلحاقه أي إذا لحق المرتد بدار الحرب مرتداً، وحكم الحاكم بلحاق المرتد بدار الحرب، عتق مدبره من الثلث وكذا مدبرها إذا لحقت، وعتق أم ولده من كل ماله وحل دينه أي الذي كان عليه على سبيل التأجيل، فيؤخذ منه في الحال، ويبطل التأجيل، ونقل ما اكتسبه في حالة الإسلام إلى ورثته المسلمين، وقال الشافعي: يبقى ماله موقوفاً بناء على أصله أن الدنيا كلها دار واحدة عنده، فلا يعتق مدبره ولا أم ولده ولا يحل دينه الذي عليه؛ لأنه حقيقة و به قال مالك وأحمد، ولنا: أنه باللحاق صار من أهل الحرب، وهم أموات في حق أحكام أهل الإسلام لانقطاع ولاية الإلزام كما انقطعت الموتى، فصار كالموت إلا أنه لا يتقرر لحاقه إلا بحكم الحاكم؛ لاحتمال أن يعود إلينا، فلابد من وهو ظاهر الرواية، وفي بعض الروايات تثبت الأحكام بمجرد الالتحاق.
عن
حي
القضاء،
وقوله: "عتق مدبره إشارة إلى أن أحكام الموت تتحقق بمجرد الحكم باللحاق ولا يشترط القضاء بتلك الأحكام، وبه قال الجمهور، وإليه أشار محمد في أكثر المواضع، وقيل: يشترط القضاء بشيء من أحكام الموتى، ولا يكتفى بالقضاء باللحاق. (مستخلص، فتح)
دينه أي الدين المؤجل الذي عليه؛ لأن اللحاق كالموت، وأما دينه الموجل الذي له فيبقى على أجله. (ط، عيني) توقف مبايعته أراد بالمبايعة كل ما كان مبادلة مال بمال فشمل الصرف والسلم والصلح عن إقرار والإجارة وقبض الدين؛ لأنه مبادلة حكمية، والرهن؛ لأنه معاوضة مالية والهبة بشرط العوض. وقوله: "وعتقه" أي مع توابعه كالتدبير والكتابة وقوله: فإن آمن نفذ وإن هلك بطل"، هذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا يجوز هذه التصرفات، عاد
إلى الإسلام أو لم يعد، وهذا على الأصل المذكور، وهو أن الردة تزيل الملك زوالاً مراعي عنده خلافاً لهما. ثم اعلم أن تصرفات المرتد على أربعة أنواع: الأول: نافذ بالاتفاق كالاستيلاد والطلاق وقبول الهبة وتسليم الشفعة والحجر على عبده المأذون؛ لأنها لا تستدعي الولاية. الثاني: باطل بالاتفاق كالنكاح والذبيحة والإرث؛ لأنها تعتمد الملة ولا ملة له. الثالث موقوف بالاتفاق كالمفاوضة والتصرف على ولده الصغير، ومال ولده؛ لأنها تعتمد المساواة، ولا مساواة بين المسلم والمرتد مالم يسلم والرابع مختلف فيه كالبيع والشراء تتوقف هذه التصرفات عنده وعندهما تنفذ إلا عند أبي يوسف يصح كما يصح من الصحيح، وعند محمد: ينفذ كما ينفذ
من المريض. (مستخلص، فتح عيني)
وهبته: ورهنه وتصرفه في ماله. هلك أي على ردته بأن مات أو قتل أو لحق بدار الحرب. (عيني)
Book of Siyar and Jihad. Chapter of Death. And the earnings of his apostasy are booty after the repayment of the debt of his apostasy. And if it is judged that he has joined (the enemy), his mudabbar and umm walad are freed, i.e. the judge's ruling, from one-third of all his wealth, and his debt becomes due, and his sale, manumission, and gift are suspended; if he becomes safe (returns to Islam), it is executed, and if he perishes (dies), it is void. (Explanation: His earnings in apostasy are booty placed in the treasury. Debt means the debt he incurred during apostasy. If he joins the enemy and the judge rules his joining, his mudabbar is freed from one-third, and similarly his mudabbara if she joins, and his umm walad is freed from all his wealth, and his debt becomes due—the deferred debt is collected immediately, and deferment is void. What he earned in Islam is transferred to his Muslim heirs. Al-Shafi'i said: his wealth remains suspended, based on his principle that the world is one dar, so his mudabbar and umm walad are not freed, nor his debt becomes due. Malik and Ahmad agreed with him. Our proof: by joining, he becomes one of the people of war, and they are like dead people in terms of Islamic rulings because the authority of obligation is cut off as with the dead, so he becomes like dead, except that his joining is not confirmed except by the judge's ruling, due to the possibility of his return. This is the apparent narration. In some narrations, the rulings are established merely by joining. His statement 'freed his mudabbar' indicates that the rulings of death are realized merely by the ruling of joining, and it is not necessary to rule on those rulings specifically; this is the view of the majority, and Muhammad indicated this in most places. It is said: rulings of the dead must be specifically ruled. (Mustakhlas, Fath) His debt meaning the deferred debt he owes, as joining is like death. As for the deferred debt owed to him, it remains on its schedule. (Ta, 'Ayni) Suspension of his sale: by sale he means any exchange of property for property, including currency exchange, salam, sulh based on acknowledgment, ijara, and receipt of debt, as it is a juridical exchange; and rahn as it is financial consideration; and conditional gift. His statement 'and his manumission' means with its subsidiaries like tadbir and kitaba. His statement 'if he becomes safe (returns), it is executed; if he perishes, it is void' – this is according to Abu Hanifa. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said these transactions are valid whether he returns to Islam or not, based on the principle that apostasy removes ownership in a manner that is subject to review (mura'a) according to Abu Hanifa, contrary to them. Then know that the transactions of an apostate are of four types: first, valid by consensus, such as istilad (procreation with a slave woman), divorce, acceptance of a gift, receipt of pre-emption, and restriction of his authorized slave, as they do not require guardianship. Second, void by consensus, such as marriage, slaughter (dhabiha), and inheritance, as they depend on religion and he has no religion. Third, suspended by consensus, such as partnership (mufawada) and acting on behalf of his minor child and his child's property, as they depend on equality and there is no equality between Muslim and apostate unless he becomes Muslim. Fourth, subject to disagreement, such as sale and purchase. These transactions are suspended according to him (Abu Hanifa), while according to the two they are valid; according to Abu Yusuf, they are valid as from a healthy person; according to Muhammad, they are valid as from a sick person. (Mustakhlas, Fath 'Ayni) And his gift and his pawn and his disposition in his wealth. 'Perish' means if he dies in apostasy, whether by death, killing, or joining the enemy. ('Ayni)
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq discusses the legal consequences of an apostate who leaves the Muslim territory and joins the enemy (ilhaq bi dar al-harb). The Hanafi school compares this to death, but with qualifications. The passage begins by stating that the apostate's earnings during apostasy become booty (fay') for the Muslim treasury, but only after settling the debts he incurred during apostasy. If the judge rules that he has joined the enemy, his mudabbar (a slave whose manumission is deferred until the master's death) is freed from one-third of his wealth, and his umm walad (slave mother of his child) is freed from all his wealth. This is because joining the enemy makes him like a dead person whose ownership ends. However, this effect requires a judge's ruling because there is a possibility he might return. The text then mentions that his deferred debts become immediately due, and the property he earned while Muslim goes to his Muslim heirs. The commentary contrasts the Hanafi position with that of al-Shafi'i, who holds that the apostate's property remains suspended because he considers the entire world as one dar (territory). The Hanafi proof is that by joining the enemy, the apostate loses the protection of Islamic law, similar to death. The passage further details the types of transactions: some are valid by consensus (like istilad, divorce), some void (marriage, slaughter), some suspended (partnership with a Muslim), and some subject to ikhtilaf (sales). According to Abu Hanifa, the latter are suspended until the apostate returns or dies; according to the Sahibayn, they are valid. The text ends with definitions and clarifications.

Key Terms
الردة (al-ridda): Apostasy from Islam by a Muslim by word or deed.
اللحاق (al-ilhaq): The apostate's act of joining the enemy in dar al-harb.
المدبر (al-mudabbar): A slave whose manumission is deferred until the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens to a transaction (e.g., sale) made by an apostate after ilhaq if the apostate returns to Islam?
A) The transaction is void from the start.
B) The transaction is executed (nifadh).
C) The transaction remains suspended indefinitely.
D) The transaction is valid only if approved by the heir.

Key Takeaway
Ilhaq makes the apostate like dead regarding his property, but a judge's ruling is essential to confirm the status.

Diyah from Apostate's Earnings: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the source of diyah from apostate's earnings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the source of diyah when an apostate commits accidental killing, and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of this dispute.

Core Idea
For an apostate who kills by mistake, Abu Hanifa takes diyah from Islamic earnings only; the Sahibayn take from both Islamic and apostasy earnings.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: from which of the apostate's earnings should diyah (blood money) be paid when he accidentally kills someone and then flees or dies? The resolution has practical implications for the victim's family and the apostate's estate. We will explore the two positions and their detailed grading by Imam Muhammad in al-Jami'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is accidental killing by an apostate. The ruling (hukm) is that diyah is wajib (obligatory) upon the apostate or his estate.
This is agreed upon by all Hanafi imams.
2
State the dispute on the source of diyah
Abu Hanifa holds that diyah is taken only from the earnings earned during the apostate's time as a Muslim (kash al-Islam). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it is taken from both kash al-Islam and earnings during apostasy (kash al-riddah).
The dispute is internal to the Hanafi school.
3
Follow the detailed grading by Muhammad in al-Jami'
Muhammad elaborates: if only one type of earning exists (Islamic or apostasy), diyah is taken from that. If both exist, according to the Sahibayn, diyah is taken from both; according to Abu Hanifa, it is taken first from Islamic earnings, and if insufficient, then from apostasy earnings.
This shows the precise practical difference.
4
Note the agreement when the apostate returns to Islam
If the apostate returns to Islam and then dies (or does not die), the diyah is taken from both earnings by agreement, because all his property is now considered his estate without the special suspension of apostasy earnings.
This unanimity highlights the exceptional nature of the original dispute.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: in a case where Islamic earnings are insufficient, Abu Hanifa would take diyah fully from apostasy earnings (only after exhausting Islamic earnings), while the Sahibayn would take proportionally from both from the start. The victim's family may receive full compensation earlier under the Sahibayn's view.
Also, if the apostate has no Islamic earnings, Abu Hanifa would still take diyah from apostasy earnings, so the difference is only in the order and proportionality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالدية في كسب الإسلام أي إذا قتل المرتد رجلاً خطأ، ثم لحق بدار الحرب أو قتل على ردته، فدية المقتول في كسب الإسلام خاصة عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا فيما اكتسب في حالة الإسلام والردة جميعاً، فيه. قال محمد في "الجامع": فإن لم يكن له إلا كسب الإسلام، أو إلا كسب الردة، تستوفى الدية منه، وإن كان له كسبهما، فعلى قولهما تستوفي الدية من الكسبين، وعلى قوله تستوفى من كسب الإسلام أولاً، فإن فضل شيء منها أخذ الفضل من كسب الردة، وإن لم يكن له إلا كسب الردة كان عليه الدية. ذلك المال. من وهذا إذا لم يسلم المرتد، وإذا أسلم ثم مات أو لم يمت يكون في الكسبين جميعاً بالاتفاق؛ لأن الكل ماله، ولهذا يجري فيه الإرث بالاتفاق، والتقييد باللحاق والقتل اتفاقي، وإنما قيد بهما تنبيهاً على أن المرتد يقتل إلا أن يسلم أو يلحق بدار الحرب وقيد بقوله: "رجلا" مع أن الحكم في قتل المرأة كذلك؛ لأن القتل غالباً يحصل فيما بين الرجال دون النساء. (مستخلص وفتح وعيني)
Thus the blood-money is in the earnings of Islam, meaning: if an apostate kills a man by mistake, then joins the Abode of War or is killed upon his apostasy, then the blood-money of the slain is taken specifically from his earnings in Islam according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: from what he earned in both the state of Islam and apostasy together. Muhammad said in al-Jami': if he does not have except earnings of Islam or except earnings of apostasy, the blood-money is taken from it, and if he has both, then according to the two it is taken from both earnings, and according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is taken from the earnings of Islam first, then if anything remains, it is taken from the earnings of apostasy, and if he does not have except earnings of apostasy, then the blood-money is upon him. This (applies) if the apostate does not become Muslim, and if he becomes Muslim then dies or does not die, it is from both earnings by agreement, because all of it is his property, and therefore inheritance applies to it by agreement, and the condition of joining or being killed is incidental; it is mentioned only to indicate that the apostate is killed unless he becomes Muslim or joins Dar al-Harb, and he said 'a man' although the ruling is the same for killing a woman, because killing usually occurs between men rather than women. (Mukhtasar, Fath, 'Ayni)
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the source of diyah when an apostate accidentally kills someone. The apostate might have earnings from his time as a Muslim and earnings from his time as an apostate. Abu Hanifa holds that the diyah is taken only from the earnings earned during Islam (kash al-Islam) if he flees or is killed on apostasy. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is taken from both earnings combined. Muhammad adds a detailed grading: if only one type of earning exists, diyah comes from that; if both exist, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad take from both proportionately, while Abu Hanifa takes from Islamic earnings first, then apostasy earnings. If the apostate later returns to Islam and then dies, all earnings are liable by agreement. The condition of fleeing or being killed is for emphasis, not limitation.

Key Terms
كسب الإسلام (kash al-islām): Earnings acquired during the time when the person was a Muslim.
كسب الردة (kash al-riddah): Earnings acquired during the state of apostasy.
دية (diyah): Blood-money compensation paid for accidental killing or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Diyah is taken from both earnings equally.
B) Diyah is taken from Islamic earnings first; if insufficient, from apostasy earnings.
C) Diyah is taken only from Islamic earnings; apostasy earnings are never used.
D) Diyah is taken from apostasy earnings first; then from Islamic earnings.

Key Takeaway
The diyah for accidental killing by an apostate is taken from his earnings, but the priority between Islamic and apostasy earnings is disputed between Abu Hanifa (Islamic first) and the Sahibayn (both proportionally).

Diyah for Cutting a Muslim's Hand Who Then Apostatizes
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on liability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah when a Muslim's hand is cut intentionally and the victim then apostatizes and dies, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between the Shaykhayn and Muhammad/Zufar.

Core Idea
If a Muslim's hand is cut, then he apostatizes and dies, the cutter pays half diyah if death occurs during apostasy, full diyah if he returns to Islam.

This lesson examines a nuanced case in Jinayat (injuries) where the victim's religious status changes between the injury and death. The Hanafi school holds that diyah (blood money) is wajib on the cutter, but the amount depends on whether the victim died as an apostate or after returning to Islam. There is a well-known intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Muhammad al-Shaybani with Zufar regarding the case where the victim returns to Islam. Understanding this dispute sharpens the ability to apply the school's principles on the interaction between injury liability and legal personality.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and parties
A Muslim (the cutter) intentionally cuts off the hand of another Muslim (the victim). The cutting is ‘amd (intentional). Later, the victim apostatizes and dies from the wound.
The key variable is the victim's religious status at death: apostate or Muslim (having returned).
2
Determine the victim's status at death
Two sub-cases: (a) the victim died while still an apostate, (b) the victim returned to Islam (by repentance) and then died from the wound.
The ruling differs based on this status.
3
State the agreed Hanafi ruling
All Hanafi authorities agree that if the victim dies as an apostate, the cutter pays only half diyah. This is because the victim's blood becomes unprotected (mubah) due to apostasy, reducing the full diyah obligation.
Half diyah is wajib on the cutter's own wealth (not on the 'aqila).
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
If the victim returns to Islam before death, the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that full diyah is wajib, because the victim died as a protected Muslim. Muhammad and Zufar hold that even in this case only half diyah is wajib, because the cutting occurred while the victim was still a Muslim (protected), but the death occurred after apostasy, and the return to Islam does not restore the full value.
The dispute hinges on whether the liability for full diyah attaches at the moment of cutting or at the moment of death.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of the Shaykhayn: full diyah if the victim returns to Islam before death. This is supported by later authorities such as al-'Ayni and Fath al-Qadir.
Thus, the cutter pays half diyah if the victim dies as an apostate, and full diyah if the victim returns to Islam then dies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ارتد بعد القطع عمداً أي مسلم والعياذ بالله أي المرتد على الردة أو الحق فجاء مسلماً فمات منه، أي دار الإسلام القطع القطع فالمكاتبة والولاء لمورثه أي إذا لحق المرتد بدار الحرب، وترك عبداً في دار الإسلام، فقضى به لابن المرتد، فكاتبه الابن، ثم جاء المرتد مسلماً، فبدل الكتابة والولاء للمرتد الذي أسلم؛ لأن ملك الوارث خلف عن ملك المورث؛ لاستغنائه، فإذا جاء مسلماً تبين أنه محتاج إليه، فيعاد إليه ملكه، ولا وجه إلى بطلان الكتابة، لصدورها عن ولاية شرعية، فجعل الابن كالوكيل من جهته، وحقوق هذا العقد ترجع إلى الموكل فوقع العتق عن المورث الموكل، والولاء لمن أعتق أي لمن يقع عنه العتق ونظيره المكاتب إذا كاتب عبده ثم عجز وفسخت الكتابة الأولى، تبقى الكتابة الثانية على حالها، ويكون بدل الكتابة وولاؤه لمولاه، بخلاف ما إذا رجع بعد أداء الكتابة؛ لأن الملك الذي له غير قائم بعد الأداء، وكذا إذا باع الابن العبد فيكون الولاء وثمنه للابن. (مستخلص، عيني) لمورثه: أي لمورث الابن وهو المرتد الذي جاء مسلماً؛ بخلاف ما إذا رجع بعد ما عتق المكاتب فإن الولاء للابن.

The hanafi dispute is about the amount of compensation. The OCR in this window is garbled; the proper text appears on page 207 with the resolution: the cutter must pay half the diyah if the apostate dies on apostasy, and full diyah if he returns to Islam then dies. Children of Apostates in Dar al-Harb as Fay'
Ruling on status of children born to apostate spouses in enemy territory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the children of an apostate couple who flee to dar al-harb and explain why they are considered fay'.

Core Idea
Children of apostates born in enemy territory become booty (fay') for Muslims upon conquest.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in the law of jihad: when an apostate couple flees to enemy territory and has children there. The Hanafi school rules that these children are treated as booty (fay') upon Muslim conquest, following the status of their mother as a captive. Understanding this ruling clarifies the legal status of individuals born in dar al-harb under apostate parents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes a married couple who apostatize from Islam and join dar al-harb (enemy territory). While there, the wife gives birth to a child, and that child later has a child of his own. The Muslims then overcome (conquer) that territory.
2
Determine the ruling
The text states ' فالولدان فيء ' meaning 'the two children are fay' (booty).' This means upon conquest, the children are treated as spoils of war, becoming slaves of the Muslim state.
Fay' is booty taken without actual fighting, but here the conquest may involve fighting; the term fay' is used broadly.
3
Understand the basis
The mother (apostate wife) is considered a free person who becomes a captive upon conquest. Her child follows her status as a captive, and the grandchild follows the mother's line. Thus, both children are enslaved as booty.
Apostasy does not nullify the mother's capacity to be enslaved; rather, her joining dar al-harb makes her an enemy combatant.
4
Apply the ruling to similar cases
If the children were born before the apostasy, their status would differ—they would not automatically be booty because they were born while their parents were Muslims. The ruling here is specific to children born after apostasy and in dar al-harb.
The text does not address pre-apostasy children, but the general principle is that the mother's status at birth determines the child's status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ارتد الزوجان ولحقا فولدت ولداً، وولد له ولد، فظهر عليهم، فالولدان فيء، أي الزوجة في دار الحرب بدار الحرب أي غنيمة
And if the two spouses apostatize and join (dar al-harb), and (the wife) gives birth to a child, and that child has a child, and (the Muslims) overcome them, then the two children are fay', i.e., the wife is in dar al-harb, dar al-harb, i.e., spoils.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling: If a married couple apostatize and flee to dar al-harb, and there the wife gives birth to a child, and that child later has a child of his own, then upon the Muslims conquering that territory, both the child and the grandchild are considered fay' (booty). This is because the mother (apostate woman) is treated as a free person who becomes a captive, and her child follows her in being enslaved. The grandchild similarly follows the mother's line. The mention of the wife being in dar al-harb indicates that the apostate woman is considered an enemy combatant and is thus subject to being taken as booty.

Key Terms
فيء (fay'): Booty taken from non-Muslims without actual fighting, often includes property and captives.
دار الحرب (dār al-ḥarb): Territory not under Muslim rule, where the rulings of war apply.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The child is free because born outside Islamic territory.
B) The child is fay' (booty) and becomes a slave.
C) The child is returned to the parents if they repent.
D) The child is killed as an apostate.

Key Takeaway
Children of apostates born after their apostasy in dar al-harb are considered fay' (booty) for the Muslim army upon conquest.

6 min
Liability of the Cutter When the Victim Apostatizes
Intra-Hanafi dispute on diyah when victim apostatizes and returns.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on diyah liability when a limb is cut, the victim apostatizes, returns to Islam, and dies, and explain the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
ʿIṣmah at cause and effect determines diyah; intervening apostasy does not break the guarantee for the two shaykhs.

This passage addresses a nuanced question in diyah law: what happens if a Muslim's hand is cut, he then apostatizes, later returns to Islam, and dies from the injury? The Hanafi school has two views, and the text explains the reasoning behind each. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the concept of ʿiṣmah in time-sensitive legal scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The victim is a Muslim whose hand is cut. He then apostatizes but does not join dār al-ḥarb. Later he returns to Islam and dies from the injury.
2
State the two positions
The two shaykhs (Abū Ḥanīfa and Abū Yūsuf) hold that the cutter owes full diyah. Muḥammad and Zufar hold that he owes half diyah (the diyah of the hand alone).
3
Analyze the key reasoning
For the two shaykhs, ʿiṣmah is required at the time of the cause (cutting) and at the time of the effect (death); the intermediate apostasy does not break the guarantee. For Muḥammad and Zufar, the apostasy nullifies the sarāyah (spreading), so only the initial cutting is considered.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is the amount of diyah: full vs. half. According to the relied-upon view of the two shaykhs, the cutter pays full diyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ضمن القاطعُ نصف الدّية في ماله لورثته فإن لم يلحق وأسلم ومات ضمن الدية، على ردته أي القاطع ضمن القاطع: أي فيما إذا مات أو لحق. نصف الدية في ماله لأن في المسألة الأولى القطع حل محلاً معصوماً، والسراية حلت محلا غير معصوم، فاعتبر القطع لا السراية، فيجب نصف الدية، وهو دية اليد في ماله خاصة؛ لأن العاقلة تتحمل العمد، ولم يجب القصاص، بشبهة الارتداد وفي الصورة الثانية يعني إذا لحق بدار الحرب بعد الردة وقضى بلحاقه، فلأنه يصير ميتا تقديراً، والموت يقطع السراية، وإسلامه بعد ذلك حياة حادثة تقديراً، فلا يعود حكم الجناية الأولى، وقوله لورثته أي يكون ذلك المال لورثة المقطوع يده، ولا يجب على القاطع شيء غير ذلك. (عيني، فتح) فإن لم يلحق إلخ : [ أي المرتد بدار الحرب بعد القطع أو لحق ولم يقض بلحاقه. (ط، عيني)] أي إذا قطع رجل يد مسلم ثم ارتد المقطوع ولم يلحق بدار الحرب بل أسلم في دارنا ثم مات من سراية ذلك القطع، فعلى القاطع دية كاملة عند الشيخين، وقال محمد وزفر : يضمن نصف الدية في هذه الصورة أيضاً؛ لأن اعتراض الردة أهدر السراية، فلا ينقلب بالإسلام معتبراً، وللشيخين: أن الجناية وردت على محل معصوم وتمت على محل معصوم؛ لأنه كان وقت القطع والموت مسلماً، وفيما بينهما حال البقاء فلا يعتبر، فوجب كل الدية كما لو لم تتخلل الردة بينهما؛ رمز الحقائق: ٤٤٦/١٢] لأن الردة لم توضع لإبراء الضمان عن الجناية، إلا أنه إذا مات على ذلك لم يجب الضمان؛ لهدر دمه بالردة؛ ولأن العصمة لا يشترط قيامها في حال بقاء الجناية، بل يشترط قيامها حال انعقاد السبب وحال ثبوت الحكم. (عيني، فتح)
The cutter owes half the diyah from his wealth to the victim's heirs. If he did not join [dar al-harb] and became Muslim and died, he owes the full diyah. On his apostasy, i.e., the cutter. Cutter: i.e., in the case when he died or joined. Half the diyah from his wealth because in the first case, the cutting occurred on a protected limb, but the spreading injury occurred on an unprotected limb, so the cutting is considered, not the spreading, so half the diyah is obligatory, which is the diyah of the hand from his own wealth specifically because the 'aqilah bears [the diyah of] accidental killing, and qisas was not obligatory due to the doubt of apostasy. In the second scenario, i.e., if he joined dar al-harb after apostasy and it was decreed that he joined, then because he becomes as if dead constructively, and death cuts off the spreading, and his Islam after that is a new life constructively, so the ruling of the first injury does not return. His saying 'to his heirs' means that wealth belongs to the heirs of the one whose hand was cut, and nothing else is due from the cutter. ('Ayni, Fath) 'If he did not join, etc.': i.e., the apostate to dar al-harb after the cut, or joined but it was not decreed that he joined. (T, 'Ayni) i.e., if a man cut the hand of a Muslim, then the victim apostatized and did not join dar al-harb but rather became Muslim in our abode, then died from the spreading of that cut, then the cutter owes a full diyah according to the two shaykhs. Muhammad and Zufar said: he owes half the diyah in this scenario as well, because the intervening apostasy nullified the spreading, so it is not considered effective by Islam. The two shaykhs' [proof]: the injury occurred on a protected limb and ended on a protected limb, because at the time of cutting and death he was Muslim, and in between the state of remaining is not considered, so the full diyah is obligatory as if apostasy had not intervened. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 12/446) Because apostasy was not placed to discharge liability from the injury, except that if he died in that state, liability is not obligatory due to the spilling of his blood by apostasy, and because 'ismah is not required to exist during the period of the injury, rather it is required at the time of the cause and at the time of the establishment of the ruling. ('Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability of a person who cuts off the hand of a Muslim, after which the victim apostatizes and either dies as an apostate, joins dar al-harb, or returns to Islam and then dies from the injury. The text first states the ruling: if the victim dies as an apostate or joins dar al-harb, the cutter owes half the diyah (the diyah of a hand) from his own wealth to the victim's heirs, because the 'aqilah (tribal guarantors) do not bear the diyah for intentional injury, and qisas is not due due to the doubt of apostasy. If the victim returns to Islam and then dies, the cutter owes full diyah. However, there is a dispute regarding the scenario where the victim apostatizes but does not join dar al-harb, then returns to Islam and dies. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that full diyah is obligatory because both the cutting and the death occurred while the victim was Muslim; the intervening apostasy is disregarded since it does not remove the protected status retroactively. Muhammad and Zufar argue that the apostasy nullifies the spreading injury, so only half diyah is due. The commentary explains the reasoning: the two shaykhs emphasize that the protection ('ismah) is required at the time of the cause (cutting) and at the time of the effect (death), not during the intermediate state. Muhammad and Zufar consider the apostasy as a break that nullifies the connection. The text also distinguishes the case where the victim joins dar al-harb: that is treated as a constructive death, cutting off the spreading, and later Islam does not revive the earlier injury.

Key Terms
القطع (al-qat'): The act of cutting a limb, specifically the hand in this context
السراية (al-sarāyah): The spreading of the injury that leads to death
العصمة (al-'iṣmah): Legal protection of life and limb, which when violated requires compensation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), what does the cutter owe when a Muslim's hand is cut, then the victim apostatizes (without joining dar al-harb), returns to Islam, and dies from the injury?
A) The cutter owes half diyah
B) The cutter owes full diyah
C) The cutter owes nothing
D) The cutter owes the diyah of a hand only

Key Takeaway
The key principle is that ʿiṣmah at the time of cause and effect determines liability; intermediate states like apostasy do not break the guarantee according to the two shaykhs.

Ruling on the Apostate Mukatib's Kitabah Payment
Ruling on distribution of apostate mukatib's wealth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state how the kitabah payment and remaining wealth are distributed when an apostate mukatib is killed in dar al-harb, and explain the reasoning behind the ruling.

Core Idea
The kitabah debt of an apostate mukatib remains due to his master; apostasy does not invalidate the contract.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in the laws of jihad: a mukatib (a slave under a kitabah contract) who apostatizes and flees to dar al-harb, acquires wealth there, and is killed. The question arises: who gets his kitabah payment and his remaining wealth? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling, with a subtle difference in reasoning among the three imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties involved
Who are the mukatib, master, and heirs? The mukatib is the slave who had a kitabah contract; the master is the owner; the heirs are the Muslim relatives of the mukatib.
2
State the primary ruling
The kitabah payment is for the master, and whatever remains after that payment is for the mukatib's heirs.
3
Understand the reasoning of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that the mukatib owns his acquisitions like a free person, so his apostasy earnings are his; the kitabah debt remains a debt on his estate.
4
Understand Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa argues that the mukatib owns his acquisitions through the kitabah contract, and apostasy does not affect the contract; however, his blood becomes permissible, but the master's ownership of his person remains.
5
Apply the analogy to true death
The distribution is similar to when a mukatib dies a natural death: the kitabah payment is deducted first for the master, then the remainder is inheritance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ارتد مكاتب ولحق، فأخذ بماله وقتل، فمكاتبته لمولاه، وما بقي لورثته. ولو من بدل الكتابة كما في الموت الحقيقي. ولحق أي المكاتب المرتد بدار الحرب واكتسب مالاً. (ط، عيني) فمكاتبته لمولاه أي إذا ارتد المكاتب ولحق بدار الحرب واكتسب مالاً، وأخذ بماله، وأبي عن الإسلام، فقتل، فبدل كتابته لمولاه، وما بقي من بدل الكتابة لورثته. وهذا على أصلهما ظاهر؛ لأن كسب الردة ملكه إذا كان حراً، فكذا إذا كان مكاتباً، وأما عند أبي حنيفة؛ فلأن المكاتب إنما يملك أكسابه بالكتابة، والردة لا تؤثر في الكتابة، فكذا في أكسابه، غير أنه صار دمه مباحاً بالردة وبإباحة دم العبد لا يزول ملك سيده منه كما لو وجب عليه قود. (مستخلص عيني لمولاه : أي لمولى المكاتب؛ لأنه ملك المولى لم يزل عن رقبته بالردة. (عيني)
And if a mukatib apostatizes and joins [dar al-harb], and his wealth is taken and he is killed, then his kitabah is for his master, and what remains is for his heirs. And it is as if it were from the kitabah payment just as in true death. (T, 'Ayni) 'And joins' means the apostate mukatib joins dar al-harb and acquires wealth. 'His kitabah is for his master' means if the mukatib apostatizes and joins dar al-harb, acquires wealth, and his wealth is taken, and he refuses Islam and is killed, then the payment of his kitabah is for his master, and whatever remains of the kitabah payment is for his heirs. This is apparent according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] because the acquisition of apostasy is owned by him if he is free, so too if he is a mukatib. As for Abu Hanifa, because the mukatib owns his acquisitions through the kitabah, and apostasy does not affect the kitabah, so too his acquisitions, except that his blood becomes permissible by apostasy, and by the permissibility of the slave's blood, his master's ownership of him does not cease, just as if qisas were obligatory against him. (Mukhtasar 'Ayni) 'For his master' means for the master of the mukatib, because the master's ownership of his person has not ceased by apostasy. ('Ayni)
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for a mukatib (a slave who has contracted to earn his freedom) who apostatizes and flees to dar al-harb, where he acquires wealth and is killed. The payment he owed for his kitabah goes to his master, and the remainder of his acquired wealth goes to his heirs (presumably his Muslim heirs). The reasoning is that the kitabah debt is like any other debt; apostasy does not nullify it. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, since a free person's apostate earnings are his own, similarly for a mukatib. According to Abu Hanifa, the mukatib's acquisition is owned by him due to the kitabah contract, and apostasy does not invalidate that, but his blood becomes permissible; however, the master's ownership of his person remains, so he cannot be seized without compensation. The phrase 'as if it were from the kitabah payment just as in true death' means that the distribution of the mukatib's wealth is similar to when he dies a natural death: the kitabah payment is deducted first for the master, then the remainder is inheritance.

Key Terms
المكاتب (al-mukātab): A slave who has made a contract of kitabah to earn his freedom by paying a sum to his master
بدل الكتابة (badal al-kitābah): The payment owed by the mukatib to his master under the kitabah contract

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When an apostate mukatib is killed in dar al-harb, who receives the kitabah payment?
A) His Muslim heirs
B) The state treasury
C) His master
D) His fellow apostates

Key Takeaway
An apostate mukatib's kitabah debt is paid to his master first, and the remainder is inherited by his Muslim heirs.

Children of Apostate Spouses in Dar al-Harb
Ruling that children born to apostate spouses in dar al-harb are booty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling regarding children born to apostate spouses in dar al-harb and explain why they become fay'.

Core Idea
A child follows the mother's status: if she is enslaved, so too is her child.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a specific scenario in the law of jihad: the fate of children born to apostate parents who have joined enemy territory. It clarifies that these children are not free but become part of the booty (fay') because they follow their mother's legal status. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the principle that lineage and freedom status are determined by the mother, especially in dar al-harb.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The scenario involves apostate spouses who have joined dar al-harb and had children there. The key is that both parents are apostates and the children are born in enemy territory.
2
State the ruling
When Muslims overcome these individuals, the children (both immediate child and grandchild) become fay' (booty) and are enslaved.
3
Understand the reasoning
The child follows the mother's status. Since the mother is an apostate, she can be enslaved, so her child is enslaved as well. This is the Hanafi principle of tabaiyyah.
4
Apply to the grandchild
The grandchild's mother is a harbiyyah (enemy woman), and she too is enslaved. Therefore, the grandchild also becomes fay'.
This shows that the principle applies even when the direct mother is a harbiyyah rather than an apostate.
5
Recognize the scope
This ruling is specific to children born after apostasy and flight to dar al-harb. It does not apply to children of Muslim women or children born before apostasy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ارتد الزوجان ولحقا فولدت ولداً، وولد له ولد، فظهر عليهم، فالولدان فيء، أي الزوجة في دار الحرب بدار الحرب أي غنيمة. ولحقا أي الزوجان بدار الحرب. وولد له أي لولدها المولود في دار الحرب فظهر عليهم: أي غلب على الزوجين والولد وولد الولد جميعاً. (عيني) فالولدان فيء لأن الولد يتبع الأم في الحرية والرق، والمرتدة تسترق، فكذا ولدها، وهو ظاهر في الولد وأما ولد الولد، فأمه حربية وهي أيضاً تسترق. (مستخلص، فتح)
And if the two spouses apostatize and join [dar al-harb], and she gives birth to a child, and that child has a child, and they are overcome [by Muslims], then the two children are fay' (booty), i.e., the wife in dar al-harb, 'b' meaning booty. 'And they join' means the two spouses join dar al-harb. 'And he has a child' means her child born in dar al-harb. 'And they are overcome' means they prevailed over the spouses, the child, and the grandchild all together. ('Ayni) 'The two children are fay' because the child follows the mother in freedom and slavery, and an apostate woman is enslaved, so too her child. This is apparent for the child; as for the grandchild, his mother is a harbiyyah and she is also enslaved. (Mukhtasar, Fath)
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage addresses the status of children born to apostate spouses who have fled to dar al-harb. If the Muslim army overcomes them, the children (both the immediate child and the grandchild) become fay' (booty) and are enslaved. The reasoning is that the child follows the mother in status: since the mother is apostate and thus can be enslaved, her child born in dar al-harb shares that status. For the grandchild, his mother is a harbiyyah (enemy woman), and she too is enslaved, so he follows her. This is different from the child of a Muslim woman, who would be free.

Key Terms
الفيء (al-fay'): Booty taken from polytheists without battle, or property of apostates
تبعية الأم (tabaiyyat al-umm): The principle that a child's status (free/slave) follows the mother's status.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the status of a child born to apostate parents in dar al-harb when the Muslims overcome them?
A) The child is free
B) The child is enslaved as fay'
C) The child is given to the father's family
D) The child is put to death

Key Takeaway
The child's status in dar al-harb follows the mother: if she is apostate or harbiyyah, the child is enslaved as fay'.

Forcing the Apostate's Child to Islam
Ruling on which children of apostates are forced to Islam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on forcing the children of apostates to Islam and distinguish between the child and grandchild.

Core Idea
A child follows parents in religion, so he is forced to Islam; a grandchild does not follow the grandfather, so he is not forced.

This passage addresses a specific issue in the chapter of apostasy: when a couple apostatizes, what happens to their children? The Hanafi school rules that the immediate children are forced to embrace Islam because they follow their parents. However, grandchildren are not forced, because the chain of religious following does not extend beyond one generation. The text also mentions a minority view from Abu Hanifa that the grandchild is also forced.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage distinguishes between the child (walad) and the grandchild (walad al-walad) of apostate parents. Note which is forced and which is not.
The ruling hinges on the concept of taba'iyyah (followership).
2
Understand the legal principle
A minor child follows his parents in religion. This principle is applied to the child: since the parents apostatized, the child is forced to Islam.
The child is forced just as the parents would be forced to return to Islam.
3
Apply the principle to the grandchild
The grandchild is not forced because his father (the original child) was himself a follower of his parents. A follower cannot have a follower.
If the grandchild were forced, it would imply all humans follow Adam, which is false.
4
Note the exception
Al-Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa that the grandchild is also forced, following the grandfather. This is a minority view (nawadir).
The standard view (zahir al-riwayah) is that the grandchild is not forced.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If the grandchild is not forced, he is treated like a captive of war: enslaved, jizyah imposed, or killed.
This is the ruling for the grandchild when not forced to Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجبر الولد على الإسلام لا ولد الولد وارتداد الصبي العاقل صحيح كإسلامه ويجبر عليه ولا يقتل. ويجبر الولد على الإسلام: لأنه يتبع أبويه في الإسلام والردة، فيجبر كما يجبران. وقوله: "لا ولد الولد" أي لا يجبر ولد الولد على الإسلام؛ لأنه لو أجبر إما أن يجبر تبعاً لأبيه، ولا وجه له؛ لأن أباه كان تبعاً لأبويه، والتبع لا يكون له تبع، أو يجبر تبعاً لجده، ولا وجه له؛ لأن تبعية الآباء في الدين على خلاف القياس، فلا يلحق به الجد، ولو ألحق لكان الناس كلهم مسلمين تبعاً لآدم وحواء عليهما السلام، ولم يوجد في ذريتهما كافر غير المرتد، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه يجبر عليه أيضاً تبعاً للجد، فإذا لم يتبع الجد يسترق أو توضع عليه الجزية، أو يقتل؛ لأن حكمه حينئذ حكم سائر أهل الحرب إذا أسروا. (عيني وفتح)
And the child is forced to embrace Islam, not the child's child. And the apostasy of a discerning minor is valid like his Islam, and he is forced to [Islam] and not killed. The child is forced to Islam because he follows his parents in Islam and apostasy, so he is forced just as they are forced. His saying 'not the child's child' means the grandchild is not forced to Islam, because if he were forced, it would be either following his father, which has no basis because his father was a follower of his own parents, and a follower has no follower; or following his grandfather, which has no basis because the following of one's ancestors in religion is contrary to analogy, so the grandfather is not attached. If he were attached, all people would be Muslims following Adam and Eve, peace be upon them, and no disbeliever would exist among their descendants except apostates. Al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he is forced also, following the grandfather. Then if he does not follow the grandfather, he is enslaved, or jizyah is imposed on him, or he is killed, because his ruling then is the ruling of other people of war when captured. ('Ayni and Fath)
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage explains that when a couple apostatizes and have children, the immediate children are forced to embrace Islam because they follow their parents in religion. However, the grandchildren are not forced, because the chain of following does not extend beyond one generation. The reasoning is that if grandchildren were forced as followers of their grandfather, then logically all humans would be followers of Adam and Eve, which is not the case. There is a narration from Abu Hanifa (through al-Hasan ibn Ziyad) that the grandchild is also forced, but the majority opinion is that he is not forced; instead, he is treated like a captive of war: enslaved, jizyah imposed, or killed.

Key Terms
الولد (al-walad): Immediate child of apostate parents

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the standard Hanafi view, who is forced to Islam when a couple apostatizes?
A) Both the child and grandchild
B) Only the child, not the grandchild
C) Neither the child nor grandchild
D) Only the grandchild

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rule on apostasy limits forced Islam to the immediate child, not the grandchild, based on the principle that followership does not extend beyond one generation.

Apostasy of a Discerning Minor: Validity and Ruling
Inter-madhhab dispute on validity of apostasy of discerning minor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the apostasy of a discerning minor and explain the key proofs and the opposing view.

Core Idea
A discerning minor's apostasy is valid like his Islam, but he is not executed – only forced back to Islam.

In this passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, the author addresses a nuanced point of apostasy law: whether a child who has reached discernment (al-ṣabiyy al-'āqil) can be considered an apostate. This is a significant intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute, with implications for inheritance, marriage, and maintenance.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Begin by clearly stating the majority Hanafi view: the apostasy of a discerning minor is valid. Note the consequences: he is forced to return to Islam and is not killed.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Identify the scholars who disagree (Abu Yusuf, Zufar, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, some Malikis) and their core argument: apostasy would impose harmful rulings (inheritance loss, marital separation, loss of maintenance) on a minor, which is unjust.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the Hanafi dalil: the hadith of Jabir (every child is born on fitrah but can become ungrateful when able to speak) and the precedent of 'Ali embracing Islam as a minor. Understand how these establish that a discerning minor's religious choice is valid.
4
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider the practical consequences of the dispute: if valid, the minor is an apostate; if invalid, he remains Muslim. Trace the effects on marriage, inheritance, and maintenance.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify the relied-upon position for fatwa (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's view that apostasy is valid) and note the tarjih mechanism: the text presents it as correct, citing clear evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وارتداد الصبي العاقل صحيح كإسلامه ويجبر عليه ولا يقتل. وقال أبو يوسف وزفر والشافعي وأحمد وبعض المالكية إن ارتداد الصبي العاقل ليس بصحيح؛ لأنه لا يلزمه أحكام يشوبه بها ضرر محض كحرمان الإرث، ولزوم الفرقة بينه وبين امرأته المشركة أو المسلمة، وامتناع نفقته على أبويه أو غيرهما من أقاربه ولهما ما روي عن جابر الله أنه عليها قال: "كل مولود يولد على الفطرة حتى يعرب عنه لسانه، فإذا أعرب عنه لسانه، فإما شاكراً وإما كفوراً"، رواه أحمد، وقوله: كإسلامه أي كما يصح إسلام الصبي العاقل خلافا للشافعي وزفر، ولنا أنه عليه صح إسلام على اله وكان صغيراً وافتخاره بذلك معروف كما قال علي ه: وجوب سبقتكموا إلى الإسلام طرا غلاما ما بلغت أوان حلم وعن عروة أنه قال أسلم علي الله وعمره ثمان سنين أخرجه البخاري، فدل على أنه يصح إسلام الصبي العاقل. (عيني، فتح، مستخلص) ويجبر عليه ولا يقتل [ إن أبي لأن القتل عقوبة ولا عقوبة على الصبي في حقه]
And the apostasy of a discerning minor is valid like his Islam, and he is forced to [Islam] and not killed. Abu Yusuf, Zufar, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and some Malikiyyah said that the apostasy of a discerning minor is not valid, because it imposes rulings that involve pure harm, such as deprivation of inheritance, separation between him and his polytheist or Muslim wife, and prevention of his maintenance from his parents or other relatives. Their proof is what is narrated from Jabir ibn 'Abdillah: 'Every child is born upon the fitrah until his tongue expresses for him; when his tongue expresses, he is either grateful or ungrateful.' (Ahmad) And his saying 'like his Islam' means just as the Islam of a discerning minor is valid, contrary to al-Shafi'i and Zufar. Our proof is that 'Ali ibn Abi Talib embraced Islam while young and took pride in that, as he said: 'I preceded all of you to Islam as a boy who had not reached the age of puberty.' And from 'Urwah that he said 'Ali embraced Islam at the age of eight. (Bukhari) This indicates that the Islam of a discerning minor is valid. ('Ayni, Fath, Mukhtasar) 'And he is forced to [Islam] and not killed' because killing is a punishment, and there is no punishment upon a minor out of mercy.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage addresses whether the apostasy of a discerning minor (a minor who understands the meaning of Islam and disbelief) is legally valid. The Hanafi position (stated in the matn) is that it is valid, just as his Islam is valid. However, Abu Yusuf, Zufar, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and some Malikiyyah hold that it is not valid because it would impose harmful consequences (like denying inheritance, separation from his wife, or loss of maintenance) that a minor should not be subjected to. The Hanafi proof includes the hadith that every child is born on fitrah but can become ungrateful when he speaks, and the precedent of 'Ali ibn Abi Talib embracing Islam as a minor, which is accepted. The text also notes that even though his apostasy is valid, he is not killed (unlike an adult apostate) because capital punishment is not for minors; instead, he is forced to return to Islam.

Key Terms
الصبي العاقل (al-ṣabiyy al-'āqil): A minor who has reached the age of discernment (tamyiz), capable of understanding Islam and disbelief

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the apostasy of a discerning minor?
A) It is invalid and he remains Muslim
B) It is valid, and he is executed
C) It is valid, but he is forced to Islam and not killed
D) It is invalid, but he is still punished

Key Takeaway
The apostasy of a discerning minor is valid in the Hanafi school, but the minor is not executed; he is forced to return to Islam.
