Apostasy of the Intelligent Minor: Valid or Not?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of minor's apostasy and compulsion of children

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the apostasy of an intelligent minor, identify the key condition (intelligence), and explain the dispute with Abu Yusuf and Zufar.

Core Idea
An intelligent minor's apostasy is valid; he is forced back to Islam but never executed.

This passage from the chapter on apostates addresses a delicate question: can a child who has not reached puberty leave Islam? The Hanafi school, led by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, says yes—if the child is intelligent and discerning. But other Hanafi authorities like Abu Yusuf and Zufar disagree. Let's work through the proofs and consequences.

Guided Path
1
Define the intelligent minor
Identify what makes a minor 'intelligent' (al-sabi al-`aqil): one who knows truth from falsehood, and distinguishes good from bad. This is the key condition for valid apostasy.
The text says: 'the intelligent one is he who knows that Islam is true and disbelief is false, and it is said: he who understands that Islam is a cause of salvation and distinguishes the bad from the good and the sweet from the bitter.'
2
State the Hanafi position
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the apostasy of an intelligent minor is valid, just as his Islam is valid. Consequently, he is compelled to return to Islam but is not killed.
This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view from the zahir al-riwayah.
3
Examine the primary proof
The Hanafi proof is the example of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) who accepted Islam at the age of eight, as narrated in Bukhari. Because his Islam was valid, by parity of reasoning (qiyas), his apostasy would also be valid if it occurred.
The text quotes Ali: 'I preceded all of you to Islam as a boy not yet having reached the age of dreaming.'
4
Analyze the opposing arguments
Abu Yusuf, Zufar, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and some Malikis argue that the apostasy of an intelligent minor is not valid. Their evidence: the hadith 'Every child is born on the fitra until his tongue expresses for him' (narrated by Ahmad). They also argue that apostasy entails harmful consequences (loss of inheritance, separation from spouse, loss of maintenance) that should not be imposed on a minor.
The Hanafi response: the fitra hadith does not negate the possibility of valid apostasy once the child chooses disbelief. The harmful consequences are a result of the child's own choice, not an imposition against his capacity.
5
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the minor's apostasy is valid (Hanafi opinion), his marriage is dissolved, he is deprived of inheritance from Muslims, and if he dies no janazah is performed. If invalid (opposing view), these consequences do not apply and he remains Muslim.
This difference has significant real-world implications for family law and inheritance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المرتدين
ويجبر الولد على الإسلام لا ولد الولد وارتداد الصبي العاقل صحيح كإسلامه ويجبر عليه ولا يقتل.
ويجبر الولد على الإسلام: لأنه يتبع أبويه في الإسلام والردة، فيجبر كما يجبران. وقوله: "لا ولد الولد" أي لا يجبر ولد الولد على الإسلام؛ لأنه لو أجبر إما أن يجبر تبعاً لأبيه، ولا وجه له؛ لأن أباه كان تبعاً لأبويه، والتبع لا يكون له تبع، أو يجبر تبعاً لجده، ولا وجه له؛ لأن تبعية الآباء في الدين على خلاف القياس، فلا يلحق به الجد، ولو ألحق لكان الناس كلهم مسلمين تبعاً لآدم وحواء عليهما السلام، ولم يوجد في ذريتهما كافر غير المرتد، وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه يجبر عليه أيضاً تبعاً للجد، فإذا لم يتبع الجد يسترق أو توضع عليه الجزية، أو يقتل؛ لأن حكمه حينئذ حكم سائر أهل الحرب إذا أسروا. (عيني وفتح)
ولد الولد مطلقا سواء كانت الزوجة حبلت فيها أو في دارنا (مس) وارتداد الصبي العاقل إلخ: العاقل هو الذي يعلم أن الإسلام حق والكفر باطل، وقيل: هو الذي يعقل أن الإسلام سبب للنجاة، ويميز الخبيث من الطيب والحلو من المر، والمعنى أن ارتداد الصبي العاقل ارتداد عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد ويجبر على الإسلام، ولا يقتل، أقاربه الكفار ولا من أقاربه المسلمين، ولو كانت تحته مسلمة أو كتابية تبين منه، ولو مات لا يصلى عليه وإنما قيد بالعاقل؛ لأن غير العاقل لا يعتبر منها الردة ولا الإسلام. وقال أبو يوسف وزفر والشافعي وأحمد وبعض المالكية إن ارتداد الصبي العاقل ليس بصحيح؛ لأنه لا يلزمه أحكام يشوبه بها ضرر محض كحرمان الإرث، ولزوم الفرقة بينه وبين امرأته المشركة أو المسلمة، وامتناع نفقته على أبويه أو غيرهما من أقاربه ولهما ما روي عن جابر الله أنه عليها قال: "كل مولود يولد على الفطرة حتى يعرب عنه لسانه، فإذا أعرب عنه لسانه، فإما شاكراً وإما كفوراً"، رواه أحمد، وقوله: كإسلامه أي كما يصح إسلام الصبي العاقل خلافا للشافعي وزفر، ولنا أنه عليه صح إسلام على اله وكان صغيراً وافتخاره بذلك معروف كما قال علي ه: سبقتكموا إلى الإسلام طرا غلاما ما بلغت أوان حلم وعن عروة أنه قال أسلم علي الله وعمره ثمان سنين أخرجه البخاري، فدل على أنه يصح إسلام الصبي العاقل. (عيني، فتح، مستخلص)
ويجبر عليه ولا يقتل [فإن أبي] لأن القتل عقوبة ولا عقوبة على الصبي في حقه أي وإذا صحت ردة الصبي العاقل المرتد يجبر على الإسلام بالحبس والتهديد ولا يقتل؛ لأن القتل عقوبة، ولا عقوبة على الصبي رحمة في حقه، ويلحق الساحر بالمرتد وكذلك المرأة الساحرة أي تقتلان؛ لأن عمر كتب إلى نوابه أن اقتلوا الساحر والساحرة، رواه البخاري وأحمد وأبو داود، وفي المنتقى إنها لا تقتل ولكن تحبس وتضرب كالمرتدة والأول أصح، وكذلك الزنديق يقتل ولا تقبل له توبة، وفي "العيون": تقبل توبته بالإجماع إلا عند الشافعي ورواية عنا.
Chapter of Apostates
And the child is compelled to Islam, not the grandchild. And the apostasy of the intelligent minor is valid like his Islam, and he is compelled to it and is not killed.
And the child is compelled to Islam: because he follows his parents in Islam and apostasy, so he is compelled as they are compelled. And his statement: 'not the grandchild' means the grandchild is not compelled to Islam; because if he were compelled, either he would be compelled following his father, and there is no basis for that because his father was a follower of his own parents, and a follower does not have a follower; or he would be compelled following his grandfather, and there is no basis for that because the following of forefathers in religion is contrary to analogy, so the grandfather is not included. And if it were included, then all people would be Muslims following Adam and Eve, peace be upon them, and there would be no disbeliever among their descendants other than the apostate. And Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he is also compelled following the grandfather; then if he does not follow the grandfather, he is enslaved, or jizya is imposed upon him, or he is killed, because his ruling then is the ruling of other people of war when captured. (Ayni and Fath)
Grandchild absolutely, whether the wife conceived in it (i.e., dar al-harb) or in our land. (Mas) And apostasy of the intelligent minor etc.: the intelligent one is he who knows that Islam is true and disbelief is false, and it is said: he who understands that Islam is a cause of salvation and distinguishes the bad from the good and the sweet from the bitter. The meaning is that the apostasy of the intelligent minor is apostasy according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and he is compelled to Islam and not killed; his relatives [who are] disbelievers [do not inherit from him] nor from his Muslim relatives; and if he had a Muslim or kitabi wife, she is separated from him; and if he dies, no funeral prayer is performed over him. And he is restricted by 'intelligent' because from the unintelligent neither apostasy nor Islam are considered. And Abu Yusuf, Zufar, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and some Malikis said that the apostasy of the intelligent minor is not valid, because rulings that involve pure harm are not imposed on him, like deprivation of inheritance, the occurrence of separation between him and his polytheist or Muslim wife, and the prevention of his maintenance from his parents or other relatives. And they have what was narrated from Jabir that he [the Prophet] said: 'Every child is born upon the fitra until his tongue expresses for him; when his tongue expresses for him, then either grateful or ungrateful.' Narrated by Ahmad. And his statement: 'like his Islam' means just as the Islam of the intelligent minor is valid, contrary to al-Shafi'i and Zufar. And our proof is that Islam of Ali was valid when he was young, and his pride in that is well-known, as Ali said: 'I preceded all of you to Islam as a boy not yet having reached the age of dreaming.' And from Urwa that he said: 'Ali accepted Islam when he was eight years old,' narrated by Bukhari. So it indicates that the Islam of the intelligent minor is valid. (Ayni, Fath, Mustakhlas)
'And he is compelled to it and not killed' [if he refuses] because killing is a punishment, and there is no punishment for the minor in his right. Meaning: when the apostasy of the intelligent minor apostate is valid, he is compelled to Islam by imprisonment and threats and is not killed, because killing is a punishment and there is no punishment for the minor out of mercy for him. And the sorcerer is annexed to the apostate, likewise the female sorcerer: they are killed. Because Umar wrote to his deputies: 'Kill the sorcerer and the sorceress,' narrated by Bukhari, Ahmad, and Abu Dawud. And in al-Muntaqa: she is not killed but is imprisoned and beaten like the apostate woman, and the first is more correct. Likewise the zindiq is killed and his repentance is not accepted. And in al-Uyun: his repentance is accepted by consensus except according to al-Shafi'i and a narration from us.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on apostates (bab al-murtaddin) in Kitab al-Siyar wal-Jihad. It begins by stating the ruling: a child (son) is compelled to embrace Islam, but not a grandchild. The reason given is that a child follows his parents in religion, whereas the grandchild's connection to the grandfather is too remote. The text reports a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad that Abu Hanifa also compelled the grandchild following the grandfather, in which case the grandchild is treated as a war captive (enslaved, jizya, or killed). Then it turns to the intelligent minor (al-sabi al-aqil). The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that his apostasy is valid, just as his Islam is valid. Consequently, he is compelled to return to Islam but is not killed. The text defines 'intelligent' as one who knows truth from falsehood and understands the consequence of religion. If he apostatizes, his marriage is dissolved, and if he dies, no janazah is performed. The opposing view of Abu Yusuf, Zufar, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and some Malikis is that his apostasy is not valid because it entails harmful consequences (loss of inheritance, separation from spouse, loss of maintenance) which should not be imposed on a minor. They cite a hadith that every child is born on fitra until his tongue expresses. The Hanafi response is that the hadith does not negate the possibility of valid apostasy, and the example of Ali (who accepted Islam at a young age) proves that the Islam of an intelligent minor is valid, and by parity of reasoning, apostasy is also valid. Finally, the passage states that the minor apostate is compelled to Islam but not killed, as killing is not for minors. The sorcerer is treated like an apostate and killed, following the practice of Umar. For the zindiq (hypocrite/heretic), there is a difference: one view is that he is killed and his repentance not accepted; another view (from al-Uyun) that repentance is accepted by consensus except for al-Shafi'i and a Hanafi narration.

Key Terms
الردة (ar-riddah): Apostasy: the act of a Muslim leaving Islam and returning to disbelief.
الصبي العاقل (as-sabi al-`aqil): An intelligent minor who has not reached puberty but possesses reason and discernment: knows truth from falsehood, distinguishes good from bad.
الجبر (al-jabr): Compulsion: forcing someone to embrace Islam, typically by imprisonment or threats, but not killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, what is the ruling on the apostasy of an intelligent minor?
A) It is not valid because a minor cannot commit apostasy.
B) It is valid, and he is forced to return to Islam but not killed.
C) It is valid, and he is killed like an adult apostate.
D) It is valid only if his parents also apostatize.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that an intelligent minor's apostasy is valid, so he is compelled to return but not executed; this differs from Abu Yusuf and Zufar who deny its validity.

Jihad — Armed Conflict Rules
intermediate
10 min
Chapter on Rebels: Definition and Rulings
Definition of rebels (bughat) and how the imam should deal with them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of bughat, distinguish them from highway robbers, and explain the imam's required procedure before fighting them.

Core Idea
Rebels are Muslims with a corrupt interpretation; the imam must call them to obedience before fighting.

This passage from Kitab al-Siyar introduces the legal category of rebels (bughat). Understanding the precise definition—Muslims who rebel against the legitimate imam with a corrupt interpretation—is crucial because their treatment differs from both highway robbers and apostates. The passage also outlines the conditions for valid imamate and the imam's duty to call rebels to repentance before resorting to force.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Definition of Bughat
Locate the definition in the passage: bughat are Muslims who go out from obedience to the rightful imam thinking they are right, based on a corrupt interpretation (ta'wil fasad). Note the three categories: highway robbers, rebels, and Khawarij.
The Khawarij are treated as rebels by consensus, even though they declare Companions disbelievers.
2
Distinguish Conditions for Bughat
For a group to be considered bughat, they must have overpowered a land and have a ta'wil. Without ta'wil, they are highway robbers; if they declare the imam a disbeliever, they are Khawarij but still treated as rebels.
Overpowering (taghallub) means gaining strength and control of a territory.
3
Understand the Imam's Obligation
The imam must first call them to obedience, as Ali did with the Khawarij at Harura. This call is recommended but not obligatory because they already know they are fighting.
The call aims to remove doubts and hope for repentance.
4
Determine the Response Based on Rebel Claims
If rebels admit the imam's oppression, the imam refrains from oppression. If they claim the truth is with them and assert authority, the imam may fight them and the people must support him.
If they claim oppression, the imam should correct that; if not, they become like apostates after the call.
5
Note the Rules of Engagement
Rebels may be fought with all means used against people of war: arrows, catapults, water, fire. They are not apostates, so their property and blood are protected unless they initiate attack.
This is stricter than for highway robbers, who may be killed for murder and theft without prior call.

باب البغاة
أي في بيان أحكامهم
خرج قوم مسلمون عن طاعةِ الإمام وغلبوا على بلد، دعاهم إليه، أي الإمام
باب البغاة: [هو جمع باغ كالقضاة جمع قاض من بغى إذا تعدى وظلم، وهو الخارج عن طاعة الإمام الحق بغير حق. (عيني)] لما فرغ من بيان الجهاد مع الكفار شرع في بيان الجهاد مع المسلمين من البغاة. وهم قوم من المسلمين خرجوا عن طاعة الإمام الحق ظانين أنهم على الحق والإمام على الباطل، مستمسكين في ذلك بتأويل فاسد، فإن لم يكن لهم تأويل فحكمهم حكم اللصوص، فيؤخذون لقتل النفس وأخذ المال. ثم الخارجون عن طاعة الإمام ثلاثة قطاع طريق وعلم حكمهم، وبغاة سيجيء حكمهم، وخوارج، وهم قوم لهم منعة خرجوا عليه بتأويل يرون أنه على باطل كفر أو معصية يوجب قتاله بتأويلهم، يستحلون دماءنا وأموالنا، ويسبون نساءنا، ويكفرون أصحاب نبينا عليه، وحكمهم حكم البغاة بإجماع الفقهاء، وإنما لم نكفرهم لكونه عن تأويل وإن كان باطلاً. والإمام يصير إماماً بأمرين بالمبايعة من الأشراف والأعيان وبأن ينفذ حكمه في رعيته خوفاً من قهره وجبروته، وإذا صار إماماً فاجراً لا ينعزل إن كان له قهر وغلبة وإلا ينعزل بالجور؛ لأنه مفسد، ويكره تقليد الفاسق ويعزل به وشرط صحة إمامة الإسلام والحرية والعقل والبلوغ والعدالة. (فتح) خرج قوم مسلمون قيد بالمسلمين؛ لأن أهل الذمة إذا غلبوا على بلدة صاروا أهل حرب، ولو قاتلونا مع أهل البغي لم يكن ذلك نقضاً للعهد منهم؛ لأنهم أتباع للبغاة المسلمين. وقوله: "وغلبوا" قيد بغلبتهم؛ لأنه لا يثبت حكم البغي ما لم يتغلبوا ويجتمعوا ويصير لهم منعة، والمراد بالتغلب الاستيلاء. (فتح) دعاهم إليه : [ أي إلى نفسه يعني إلى طاعته ] لأن علياً له بعث عبد الله عباس هما إلى أهل حروراء، فدعاهم إلى التوبة، وناظرهم قبل قتالهم ولأنه ترجى توبتهم، ولعل الشر يندفع بالتذكرة، وهو أهون، فيبدأ به، وهذه الدعوة ليست بواجبة؛ لأنهم علموا لماذا يقاتلون. وحروراء قرية بالكوفة كان بها اجتماع الخوارج بسبب تحكيم علي الله الأشعري الله بينه وبين معاوية، قائلين: إن القتال واجب بقوله تعالى: فَقَاتِلُوا الَّتِي تَبْغِي (الحجرات: 9) وعليه ترك القتال بالتحكيم، وهو كفر لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ لَمْ يَحْكُمْ بِمَا أَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ فَأُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْكَافِرُونَ ﴾ (المائدة: ٤٤) فبعث علي الله ابن عباس هما ليكشف شبهتهم، ويدعوهم إلى العود إلى الجماعة.
أبا
موسى
فلما ذكروا شبهتهم قال ابن عباس ما هذه الحادثة ليست بأولى من بيض حمام، وفيه التحكيم كما قال تعالى: يحْكُمُ بِهِ ذَوَا عَدْلٍ مِنْكُمْ﴾ (المائدة: ٩٥) فكان تحكيم علي الله موافقاً للنص، فألزمهم الحجة، فتاب البعض وأصر آخرون. وقوله : وكشف شبهتهم" فإن أجابوا لذلك تم المرام وحصل الالتيام، وإن قالوا: فعلنا لظلمك، فالإمام يمتنع عن الظلم، ولو لم يمتنع ،وقاتلهم فالناس لا يعينون الإمام ولا البغاة، ولو قالوا فعلنا؛ لأن الحق معنا، وادعوا الولاية، فله أن يقاتلهم، وعلى الناس أن يعينوه؛ لأنهم صاروا كالمرتدين وأهل الحرب الذين بلغتهم الدعوة، ولهذا يجوز قتالهم بكل ما يقاتل به أهل الحرب كالرمي بالنبل والمنجنيق، وإرسال الماء والنار عليهم. (عيني، فتح)
Chapter of Rebels
That is, in explanation of their rulings.
A group of Muslims went out from the obedience of the imam and overpowered a land; he called them to him, i.e., the imam.
Chapter of Rebels: [It is the plural of baghi like al-qudat is plural of qadi, from bagha meaning to transgress and wrong, and it is the one who goes out from obedience to the rightful imam without right. (Ayni)] When he finished explaining jihad against the disbelievers, he began explaining jihad against the Muslims who are rebels. And they are a group of Muslims who went out from obedience to the rightful imam, thinking that they are upon the truth and the imam is upon falsehood, adhering in that to a corrupt interpretation. If they have no interpretation, their ruling is the ruling of highway robbers: they are taken for killing the soul and taking wealth. Then those who go out from obedience to the imam are three types: highway robbers—their ruling is known; rebels—their ruling will come; and the Khawarij—they are a group who have strength and go out against him with an interpretation, thinking he is upon falsehood, disbelief, or sin that obligates fighting him according to their interpretation; they consider our blood and wealth lawful, enslave our women, and declare the Companions of our Prophet disbelievers. Their ruling is the ruling of rebels by consensus of the jurists. We do not declare them disbelievers because it is due to an interpretation, even if corrupt. And the imam becomes imam by two things: by the pledge of allegiance from the nobles and prominent people, and by executing his rule over his subjects due to fear of his power and force. And if he becomes a corrupt imam, he is not removed if he has power and dominance; otherwise he is removed due to injustice because he is corrupt. And it is disliked to appoint a corrupt person, and he is removed for it. And the conditions for the validity of the imamate are: Islam, freedom, intellect, puberty, and uprightness. (Fath) 'A group of Muslims' is restricted to Muslims because if dhimmis overpower a town, they become people of war, and if they fight us alongside the rebels, that is not a breach of covenant from them because they are followers of the Muslim rebels. And his statement: 'and overpowered' is restricted to their overpowering because the ruling of baghy is not established unless they gain strength, gather, and have power. And the meaning of 'overpowering' is taking control. (Fath) 'He called them to him' [i.e., to himself, meaning to his obedience] because Ali sent Abd Allah ibn Abbas and Abu Musa to the people of Harura, calling them to repentance, and he debated them before fighting them, and because their repentance is hoped for, and perhaps evil is repelled by reminding, and it is easier, so one begins with it. And this call is not obligatory because they know why they fight. Harura is a village in Kufa where the Khawarij gathered due to the arbitration of Ali with Abu Musa al-Ash'ari between him and Muawiya, saying: Fighting is obligatory by His statement: 'So fight the one that transgresses' (49:9), and leaving fighting by arbitration is disbelief by His statement: 'And whoever does not judge by what Allah has revealed, then those are the disbelievers' (5:44). So Ali sent Ibn Abbas and Abu Musa to uncover their doubts and call them to return to the congregation. When they mentioned their doubt, Ibn Abbas said: This incident is not more worthy than the egg of a pigeon, and arbitration is in it as Allah says: 'Judge by it two just persons among you' (5:95). So the arbitration of Ali was in accordance with the text, so he established the argument against them. Some repented and others persisted. And his statement: 'and uncover their doubts'—if they respond to that, the goal is achieved and harmony is obtained. And if they say: 'We did it because of your oppression,' then the imam refrains from oppression. If he does not refrain and fights them, the people neither support the imam nor the rebels. And if they say: 'We did it because the truth is with us' and claim authority, then he may fight them, and the people must support him because they have become like apostates and people of war who have received the call. Therefore, it is permissible to fight them with all that people of war are fought with, like shooting arrows, using catapults, and releasing water and fire upon them. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on rebels (bughat) in Kitab al-Siyar wal-Jihad. It defines the legal category of al-bughat: Muslims who rebel against the legitimate imam based on a corrupt interpretation (ta'wil fasad). The passage distinguishes three types of those who go out from obedience: highway robbers (qutta' al-tariq), rebels (bughat), and the Khawarij (a specific group that deemed the Companions disbelievers). The ruling for the Khawarij is the same as for rebels by consensus. Then it discusses the conditions for the imamate: the imam gains authority through allegiance or power. If the imam becomes corrupt, he is not removed if he has power; otherwise he is removed. The conditions for valid imamate are Islam, freedom, intellect, puberty, and uprightness. Then the passage explains the requirement that the rebels must have strength and control of a land for the rules of rebellion to apply. The imam should first call them to obedience, as Ali did with the Khawarij at Harura. This call is recommended but not obligatory. The passage recounts the story of the Khawarij's doubts about arbitration, which Ibn Abbas refuted using Quranic verses (5:44, 5:95). Finally, it states how the imam should respond to different claims by the rebels. If they admit oppression, he stops oppressing. If they claim the truth is with them and assert their own authority, then he may fight them with all means of warfare, like against people of war, and the Muslims must support him.

Key Terms
البغاة (al-bughat): Rebels: Muslims who rise against the legitimate imam based on a corrupt interpretation, believing themselves to be right.
التأويل الفاسد (at-ta'wil al-fasid): A corrupt interpretation: a flawed reasoning that leads a group to believe they are justified in rebelling despite being wrong in Islamic law.
الإمام الحق (al-imam al-haqq): The legitimate imam: the ruler who meets conditions of Islam, freedom, intellect, puberty, and uprightness, and has authority through allegiance or dominance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the first step the imam should take when faced with a rebel group that has overpowered a land?
A) Immediately attack them with full force.
B) Send a delegation to call them to obedience and clarify their doubts.
C) Declare them apostates and confiscate their property.
D) Ignore them until they attack the capital.

Key Takeaway
Rebels are Muslims with a corrupt interpretation; the imam must call them to obedience before fighting, and they retain Muslim status.
